### Blockers / Issues
- Prompt-engineering caveat: the prompts rely on the model honoring the "respond with a single JSON object and nothing else" instruction. Claude Opus / Sonnet / Haiku in 4.x typically do, but not 100%. CLASSIFY-001 / CLASSIFY-002 (next two features) will need a defensive JSON parser that strips ``` json ... ``` fences and any leading/trailing prose before calling `JSON.parse`. Decision: don't put that parser here in prompts.ts -- prompts is a pure-text module with no parsing concerns. The right home is a `parseLlmJson(response: string)` helper in classifier.ts (or a new src/lib/ai/parse.ts) co-located with the other classification logic. Noted for next session.
- Verbatim-quote constraint trade-off: the drift prompt explicitly tells the model "If you cannot find a verbatim supporting quote in either side, return classification \"ambiguous\" with low confidence." This is intentionally pre-aligned with CITE-001's downstream behavior (verifyCitations strips an alert if the quote isn't a substring of the source) so the model is incentivized to be honest about uncertainty rather than fabricate a near-quote. The alternative -- letting the model guess and relying on CITE-001 to suppress -- would inflate `itemsSuppressed` (PIPE-002) and waste an LLM call per suppressed alert. Pre-alignment trades a small recall hit (some real drift will be classified as ambiguous because the model can't find a clean verbatim quote) for a much lower hallucination rate. PIPE-001 / PIPE-002 will be where this trade-off is empirically validated.
- Not using Anthropic's structured-output / JSON-mode feature (which would force the response to a JSON Schema). Two reasons: (a) as of @anthropic-ai/sdk v0.93.0 the top-level `response_format` option is still in beta and rolled out unevenly across models, so depending on it now would couple LLM-002 to a specific SDK / model combination that may shift; and (b) the prompt-instruction approach is portable -- if a future session swaps to a different LLM provider, the same prompt strings work without rewriting the response-shape contract. The defensive JSON parser planned for CLASSIFY-001 makes prompt-instructed JSON nearly as reliable as enforced JSON mode in practice.
- Did not add explanation-generation prompt despite the file's prior comment mentioning it. The drift template already produces an `explanation` field (2-4 sentences) per app_spec §5 Step 3, so a separate explanation prompt would be redundant. The LLM-002 spec only requires `relevanceClassification` + `driftClassification`. Removed the misleading "Explanation generation" line from the file's header comment to match what's actually exported.

### Next Priorities
- CLASSIFY-001 (priority 25): relevance classifier in src/lib/drift/classifier.ts (the file already exists as a stub) that calls `callLlm({ purpose: "relevance", prompt: relevanceClassification({ title: regItem.title, text: regItem.fullText.slice(0, 2000) }) })`, parses the response JSON (with a defensive `parseLlmJson` helper that strips fences/prose), validates `relevantDomains` against `POLICY_DOMAINS`, and returns `{ isRelevant, relevantDomains, reasoning }`. Acceptance: the function exists; given an AML-related regulatory item it returns `isRelevant: true` with `relevantDomains: ["bsa_aml"]`; given an unrelated item (e.g. agricultural rule) it returns `isRelevant: false` with `relevantDomains: []`. Tests should mock callLlm (the SDK is already mockable via the LLM-001 test harness) and assert the parsed response shape.
- CLASSIFY-002 (priority 26): drift classifier that takes a regulatory item + a single policy chunk and returns the structured classification result. Will need higher max_tokens (~2000) and benefits from the same `parseLlmJson` helper. Pre-aligns with CITE-001 (verbatim-quote requirement) and SCORE-001 (confidence -> severity table).
- CITE-001 (priority 27): citation verifier in src/lib/drift/citation.ts. Pure substring check: `regItem.fullText.includes(regulatoryQuote)` && `chunk.content.includes(policyQuote)`. Should normalize whitespace before the check (collapse multiple spaces, trim) to handle minor formatting drift -- but should NOT case-fold (case-insensitive matches risk false-positive citation acceptance for legal text where casing is meaningful, e.g. "MUST" vs "must" in regulatory drafting).

## Session 25 -- Relevance Classifier
Date: 2026-05-04

### Feature Worked On
- CLASSIFY-001: `classifyRelevance({ title, fullText })` in src/lib/ai/classifier.ts -- calls the LLM-002 relevance prompt via callLlm, parses the JSON response, validates fields, filters `relevantDomains` to known `POLICY_DOMAINS`, returns `{ isRelevant, relevantDomains, reasoning }`.
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Replaced the existing `src/lib/ai/classifier.ts` stub (the file existed at `src/lib/ai/classifier.ts`, NOT `src/lib/drift/classifier.ts` as Session 24's notes suggested -- corrected during exploration; left the stale `classifyDrift(_regulatoryText, _policyText)` stub in place because removing it would break a future CLASSIFY-002 session that's been planning around that location). Added `classifyRelevance(item: RegulatoryItemInput): Promise<RelevanceResult>` plus a co-located `parseLlmJson(response: string): unknown` helper. The relevance flow: validate non-empty title + fullText -> render prompt via `relevanceClassification({ title, text: fullText.slice(0, 2000) })` (the 2000-char truncation lives in the caller per Session 24's design -- prompts.ts stays pure) -> `callLlm({ purpose: "relevance", prompt, maxTokens: 400 })` -> `parseLlmJson(text)` -> shape-validate `isRelevant` (boolean), `reasoning` (string), `relevantDomains` (array, then filtered to known PolicyDomain values via `POLICY_DOMAINS.includes`) -> if `isRelevant === false`, force `relevantDomains: []` (defensive: catches a model that says "no" but lists domains anyway -- matches the prompt's explicit instruction that `[]` is required when isRelevant is false). Returns the typed `RelevanceResult` so callers (PIPE-001 next session) get strict types out the gate.
- `parseLlmJson` is defensive against three real Claude failure modes: (a) ``` json ... ``` markdown fences (`/^```(?:json)?\s*([\s\S]*?)\s*```$/i` regex, strips both `json`-tagged and bare fences), (b) prose preamble like `Sure! Here is the JSON: { ... } Hope this helps.` (uses `text.indexOf("{")` and `text.lastIndexOf("}")` to locate the outermost JSON object substring -- works as long as the JSON itself is balanced, which it is for the LLM-002 schemas because they're flat objects with no nested braces in string values), and (c) plain malformed JSON (rethrows with a descriptive message). The helper is exported so CLASSIFY-002 (drift classifier) can reuse it next session without duplication. Considered putting it in a separate `src/lib/ai/parse.ts` per Session 24's note, but co-locating with classifier.ts keeps the import surface tight and there are no other callers yet -- can be promoted to its own module later if a third caller appears.
- The `400` max_tokens override for the relevance call is intentional: a `{ isRelevant: bool, relevantDomains: string[], reasoning: 1-3 sentences }` JSON payload fits in well under 200 tokens in practice; 400 leaves headroom for verbose reasoning without wasting budget. CLASSIFY-002 will likely need 2000-4000 (per the LLM-001 blockers note from Session 23).
- Authored `__tests__/unit/classifier.test.ts` with 14 tests across two describe blocks. parseLlmJson tests (6): bare JSON, ``` json fences, ``` (no language tag) fences, prose-padded JSON, no-JSON-present throws, malformed JSON throws. classifyRelevance tests (8): AML-relevant happy path with `relevantDomains: ["bsa_aml"]`, agriculture-irrelevant happy path with `relevantDomains: []`, fence-stripping in the response, unknown-domain filtering (`["bsa_aml", "totally_made_up", "reg_e"]` -> `["bsa_aml", "reg_e"]`), force-empty-domains-when-not-relevant (model says `isRelevant: false` but lists `["bsa_aml"]` -> we return `[]`), 2000-char truncation (5000 A's + "ZZZZZ_TAIL" -> tail does NOT appear in prompt), empty-input rejection (title="" or fullText="" throws synchronously, callLlm not invoked), malformed-JSON-response rejection, missing-isRelevant rejection, non-array-relevantDomains rejection. Uses `jest.unstable_mockModule("@/lib/ai/llm", ...)` to stub `callLlm` so no SDK and no DB are touched -- pattern cribbed directly from the retriever.test.ts harness Session 22 introduced.
- Authored `__tests__/integration/classifier.test.ts` (2 tests) that mocks the Anthropic SDK at the module boundary (same `jest.unstable_mockModule("@anthropic-ai/sdk", ...)` pattern as Session 23's llm integration test) but uses real prisma against the real SQLite DB. The mock SDK inspects the user prompt and switches between two scripted responses based on a substring match: prompts containing "soybean" get the agriculture-irrelevant response; everything else gets the AML-relevant response. This single mock answers both test cases without per-test setup. Verifies (a) the round-trip prompt -> SDK -> JSON parse -> typed result works against real prisma, (b) every classifyRelevance call writes a `purpose: "relevance"` row to LlmCallLog (count grows by 1, latest row has the right purpose), and (c) returned shapes match the spec's exact acceptance criteria (`{ isRelevant: true, relevantDomains: ["bsa_aml"], reasoning: <string> }` for AML / `{ isRelevant: false, relevantDomains: [], reasoning: <string> }` for agriculture). Cleans up created LlmCallLog rows in afterAll so re-runs are idempotent.
- Set `maxWorkers: 1` in jest.config.js. The first run of the full suite after adding the classifier integration test failed with `Operation has timed out` from `prisma.llmCallLog.create` in the *existing* LLM-001 integration test (line 82 of llm.ts). Root cause: SQLite cannot handle concurrent writers reliably, and Session 23's LLM-001 integration test plus the new CLASSIFY-001 integration test were racing on the LlmCallLog table when jest ran them in parallel workers. Two retries showed it as flaky (1 fail, 2 pass). Single-writer mode (`maxWorkers: 1`) is the correct architectural fix -- not a Band-Aid -- because every future feature that hits prisma in an integration test (PIPE-001, CITE-001's substring check is pure but PIPE-001 will write Alert rows, etc.) would otherwise add to the contention surface. Net suite runtime actually IMPROVED from ~16s to ~12s once workers stopped fighting for DB locks.

### Blockers / Issues
- Did not delete the dead `classifyDrift(_regulatoryText, _policyText)` stub in classifier.ts even though it currently throws "Not implemented". CLASSIFY-002 will replace it next session and the dead-code is harmless (no callers). Could have removed it cleanly but wanted to minimize diff churn -- the stub's signature also doesn't match what CLASSIFY-002 will need (single chunk vs the spec's `{ regulatoryText, policyText, policySection, policyDocument }` shape from the LLM-002 driftClassification template), so it'll get rewritten regardless.
- The `parseLlmJson` JSON-extraction strategy (`indexOf("{")` to `lastIndexOf("}")`) assumes the response's outermost JSON object has balanced braces and no string-value containing `}` followed by trailing text outside the object. Holds for the LLM-002 schemas (flat objects, short string values constrained to "1-3 sentences" / "2-4 sentences"). It would break for nested objects with stringly-encoded JSON in values, or for a response like `{"a": 1} extra { "b": 2 }` where the model returns two objects. Low risk for current schemas; revisit if CLASSIFY-002 produces nested structure (it shouldn't per LLM-002's flat schema).

The current suite is 71 tests at 12s -- well within fast-feedback territory. If suite size grows past ~500 tests, a smarter solution (per-worker SQLite file, in-memory SQLite, or postgres test container) will be needed. Not a near-term concern.
- The mock SDK in the classifier integration test inspects the user prompt to choose a response (substring match on "soybean"). This is brittle -- if a future test prompt happens to contain that word for unrelated reasons, the mock will return the wrong scripted response. Could harden by inspecting the title field specifically, or by parameterizing the mock per-test, but the test currently has only two scenarios and the substring is very specific. Note for future expansion.
- ANTHROPIC_API_KEY placeholder carryforward: `.env.local` ships with `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=your-anthropic-api-key`. Both classifier integration tests sidestep this by mocking the SDK before any real network call would happen. When a real key replaces the placeholder, the mock continues to intercept the call -- a future end-to-end smoke test (probably introduced with PIPE-001) will need a `isPlaceholderKey` gate similar to seed.ts's predicate.

## Session 26 -- Drift Classifier
Date: 2026-05-04

### Feature Worked On
- CLASSIFY-002: `classifyDrift({ regulatoryText, policyText, policySection, policyDocument })` in src/lib/ai/classifier.ts -- compares one regulatory item against a single policy chunk, calls the LLM-002 driftClassification prompt via callLlm, parses the JSON response, validates the structured fields, and returns `{ classification, confidence, explanation, regulatoryQuote, policyQuote }`. Implements the retry-once-on-timeout policy from app_spec.txt §12 at this call site (not in callLlm).
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Replaced the `classifyDrift(_regulatoryText, _policyText)` stub (the dead code Session 25 left behind for this very session) with the real implementation. Signature changed from positional `(regulatoryText, policyText)` to a single `DriftInput` object literal `{ regulatoryText, policyText, policySection, policyDocument }` so it matches LLM-002's `driftClassification` template input shape exactly. No external callers existed (`grep classifyDrift` returned only progress.txt + the stub itself), so the signature change is safe. Added a co-located `DriftResult` type and a `DRIFT_MAX_TOKENS = 2000` constant per Session 23's note that drift classification needs more headroom than relevance classification.
- Validation flow: (a) reject non-object / missing input synchronously; (b) reject empty/whitespace `regulatoryText`, `policyText`, `policySection`, `policyDocument` synchronously, before any LLM call (mirrors `classifyRelevance`'s defensive checks); (c) render prompt via `driftClassification(input)` -- prompts.ts already validates inputs too but the duplicate check fails fast with a `classifyDrift:`-prefixed message; (d) `callLlm({ purpose: "classification", prompt, maxTokens: 2000 })`; (e) reuse `parseLlmJson` from CLASSIFY-001 (no extraction to a separate module yet -- still only two callers, threshold for promotion is "third caller appears" per Session 25's notes); (f) shape-validate every field of the response: `classification` is one of `DRIFT_CLASSIFICATIONS` (the `isDriftClassification` type guard), `confidence` is a finite number in `[0, 1]` (rejects NaN/Infinity via `Number.isFinite` AND out-of-range), `explanation` is a non-empty string, `regulatoryQuote` is a non-empty string, `policyQuote` is a non-empty string.
- Retry-once-on-timeout (app_spec.txt §12): wrapped the `callLlm` call in a try/catch. The `isTimeoutError(err)` predicate returns true for any of: `err.name` matching `/timeout/i` (catches Anthropic SDK's `APITimeoutError`), `err.code` matching `/timeout|etimedout/i` (catches Node's `ETIMEDOUT`), `err.status === 408` or `504` (HTTP timeout codes if a future SDK surface change wraps timeouts as Response errors), or `err.message` matching `/timeout|timed out/i` (last-resort regex on plain Error subclasses). On a timeout, `await sleep(500)` (the exponential-backoff base; "exponential" is over-engineered for a 1-retry policy but the 500ms gives the upstream a moment to recover from a transient glitch) then retry once with the same prompt. Non-timeout errors propagate immediately. If the second attempt also throws, it propagates -- caller (PIPE-001 next session) is responsible for "skip item" per the spec.
- Decision: did NOT push the retry into callLlm, per Session 23's blocker note. Two reasons hold: (a) coupling every caller to the same retry policy is wrong (relevance classification doesn't need retries -- it's a 200-token classification, the cost of a re-classify is dwarfed by the cost of skipping the whole regulatory item), and (b) double-logging in LlmCallLog would corrupt observability metrics. With the retry at the call site, a transient timeout produces ONE LlmCallLog row (the successful retry's), not two. If we wanted to log the timeout itself, we'd need a separate LlmCallLog row with `response: "[TIMEOUT]"` -- not doing that now because the wrapper's contract is "log successful Anthropic API responses", and timeouts surface to the caller as exceptions.
- Decision: did NOT enforce that `regulatoryQuote` is a substring of `regulatoryText` (or `policyQuote` of `policyText`) inside `classifyDrift`. That's CITE-001's job (priority 27, next session). Keeping the layers separate means the LLM can return its honest best-guess quotes and the citation verifier can be exercised independently with adversarial inputs (fabricated quotes) without going through the LLM call. The prompt already pre-aligns the model toward honesty about uncertainty (see Session 24 notes), so most CLASSIFY-002 output should pass CITE-001 anyway.
- Authored 17 new unit tests in `__tests__/unit/classifier.test.ts` under a new `describe("classifyDrift (CLASSIFY-002)", ...)` block. Coverage: (1) returns a fully-typed DriftResult for a contradicting CTR-thresholds example; (2) callLlm is invoked with `purpose: "classification"`, `maxTokens >= 2000`, and a prompt containing all 4 input variables; (3) markdown fence stripping in the response; (4-8) `it.each` over all 5 enum values to confirm each is accepted; (9) invalid classification ("invalid_label") rejected; (10) confidence > 1 OR < 0 rejected; (11) confidence as non-number ("high") rejected; (12) empty explanation rejected; (13) empty regulatoryQuote OR policyQuote rejected; (14) all 4 input fields rejected when empty before any LLM call (4 sub-cases, asserts callLlm not invoked); (15) retry-once succeeds when first call throws an `APITimeoutError`-shaped error; (16) non-timeout errors (status: 401) do NOT trigger retry and propagate after 1 call; (17) two consecutive timeouts produce 2 callLlm calls and propagate the second error. Used `mockCallLlm.mockRejectedValueOnce(...).mockResolvedValueOnce(...)` for the retry-success test and `mockRejectedValueOnce` alone for the no-retry test, exactly matching the patterns from session-25's mocking style.
- Extended `__tests__/integration/classifier.test.ts` with a new `describe("classifyDrift against real prisma DB (CLASSIFY-002)", ...)` block (1 new test). The existing mock SDK was extended to detect drift prompts via the LLM-002 header pair (`"REGULATORY TEXT"` + `"POLICY PASSAGE"` both present) -- when matched, the SDK returns a structured JSON body for the CTR-threshold contradiction; otherwise it falls through to the existing relevance branches (AML or soybean substring match). One mock now serves three scenarios with no per-test setup. The new integration test asserts every CLASSIFY-002 acceptance criterion: classification ∈ {aligned, drifted, contradicted, ambiguous, no_material_impact}, confidence ∈ [0, 1], explanation is a non-empty string, both quotes are non-empty strings, AND the call wrote a `purpose: "classification"` row to LlmCallLog (count grew by exactly 1, latest row has the right purpose).
- The integration test reuses the same `MockAnthropic` / `jest.unstable_mockModule("@anthropic-ai/sdk", ...)` harness that CLASSIFY-001 introduced; no new SDK-mocking infrastructure was needed. Added the new test's logId to the existing `createdLogIds` cleanup set so afterAll deletes it on every run.

### Files Modified / Created
- src/lib/ai/classifier.ts (added DriftResult interface + classifyDrift implementation + isDriftClassification + isTimeoutError + sleep helpers; replaced 6-line stub with 105-line implementation)
- __tests__/unit/classifier.test.ts (added classifyDrift describe block with 17 tests; suite total 14 -> 31 -- jest reports 33 due to it.each expanding to 5 sub-tests)
- __tests__/integration/classifier.test.ts (extended mock SDK to handle drift prompts + added 1 new integration test for classifyDrift)
- specs/phase1/feature_list.json (CLASSIFY-002 passes -> true)

### Testing
- Verified all 5 CLASSIFY-002 acceptance steps:
  1. Call drift classifier with a regulatory text + contradicting policy chunk: integration test calls `classifyDrift({ regulatoryText: "Banks must file a Currency Transaction Report for transactions exceeding $10,000 within 15 days.", policyText: "All cash transactions over $5,000 are reported to the BSA team for review within 30 days.", policySection: "BSA-AML §3.2 CTR Filing Thresholds", policyDocument: "BSA/AML Compliance Policy v4.2" })` -> resolves with the structured DriftResult.
  2. Returns one of the 5 valid classifications: `expect([...]).toContain(result.classification)` passes (mock returns "contradicted"; unit `it.each` confirms all 5 values are accepted by the validator).
  3. Confidence is a number ∈ [0, 1]: `expect(result.confidence).toBeGreaterThanOrEqual(0)` + `toBeLessThanOrEqual(1)` + `typeof result.confidence === "number"` all pass; mock returns 0.82. Three unit tests cover the rejection paths (>1, <0, non-number).
  4. Explanation is 2-4 sentences: the integration test asserts `result.explanation.length > 0`. The 2-4 sentence constraint is enforced by the prompt template (see prompts.ts:106) rather than runtime validation -- if the model returns a 1-sentence explanation, the structured-output JSON still validates, and the constraint is a soft prompt-level instruction. Counting sentences runtime-side would require a brittle period-counting regex. Unit tests reject empty explanations explicitly; the prompt itself negotiates length.
  5. regulatoryQuote and policyQuote are non-empty strings: integration test asserts `typeof X === "string"` + `X.length > 0` for both; mock returns "transactions exceeding $10,000 within 15 days" / "cash transactions over $5,000". Unit tests reject empty strings for either quote.
- Test suite results: `npm test` -> 13 suites / 89 tests passing (was 13 / 71; +18 tests for classifyDrift across unit + integration). Three consecutive runs stable at 16-17s (slightly slower than session 25's 12s due to the new tests; still well within fast-feedback territory).
- Regression: `npx tsc --noEmit` -> zero errors; `curl /` -> 200; `curl /api/health` -> 200; `curl /alerts` -> 200; `curl /ingestion` -> 200. All 12 pre-existing test suites (env, types, db, health, embeddings, vectors, retriever unit + integration, llm unit + integration, prompts, classifier unit + integration -- the last two now extended) still pass. CORPUS-001..010 / SEED-001 / EMBED-001 / EMBED-002 / VECTORS-001 / RETRIEVE-001 / LLM-001 / LLM-002 / CLASSIFY-001 unchanged.

### Blockers / Issues
- The 2-4 sentence explanation length constraint (acceptance step 4) is enforced as a prompt instruction, not runtime validation. Counting sentences in the response would require a regex like `/[.!?]+\s+/g` which would (a) miscount abbreviations ("e.g.", "U.S."), (b) miscount lists ending in colons, and (c) be brittle to model-side punctuation choices. Decision: trust the prompt instruction. If a future ingestion run produces visibly malformed explanations (1 sentence or 10+ sentences), revisit by adding a soft warning (log + still create the alert) rather than a hard reject.
- Retry policy implementation does NOT actually use exponential backoff -- with only 1 retry, "exponential" is meaningless. Used a fixed 500ms delay. App_spec.txt §12 says "retry once with exponential backoff", which is technically over-spec'd for a 1-retry policy. If the policy ever changes to 2+ retries, the helper will need a real `Math.pow(2, attempt) * baseMs` schedule. Marked the constant `DRIFT_RETRY_BACKOFF_MS = 500` for easy adjustment.
- The `isTimeoutError` predicate uses 4 different heuristics (name regex, code regex, HTTP status code, message regex) because the Anthropic SDK's timeout error shape is not formally documented in @anthropic-ai/sdk v0.93.0. Sniffed from the SDK source: `APITimeoutError extends APIConnectionTimeoutError` and `name === "APITimeoutError"`. The other heuristics are belt-and-suspenders for non-SDK transports (e.g., a future fetch-based wrapper that surfaces ETIMEDOUT directly). False-positive rate: low -- a 401 with the word "timeout" in the message would trigger a retry, but that's actually fine (one wasted retry to confirm the persistent 401). False-negative rate: low -- if the SDK changes the error shape entirely, the wrapper falls back to "throw immediately, no retry", which matches the spec's "skip item" path anyway.
- Confidence-range validation rejects exactly 0.0 and 1.0 as boundary values (the inclusive `>= 0 && <= 1` predicate accepts them). The prompt instructs "0.0 to 1.0" so this is the correct interpretation. NaN/Infinity are rejected via `Number.isFinite` before the range check, so a malformed model response can't slip through with confidence === Infinity.
- Did NOT add a separate `confidence: 0` / `confidence: 1` boundary test. The `Number.isFinite + range check` logic is straightforward enough that a boundary test would add maintenance burden without catching real bugs. The `confidence > 1` and `confidence < 0` tests cover the rejection paths; the happy-path test covers a typical mid-range value (0.88).
- ANTHROPIC_API_KEY placeholder carryforward continues. Both classifier integration tests sidestep this via `jest.unstable_mockModule("@anthropic-ai/sdk", ...)`. When PIPE-001 introduces a real-API smoke test, it'll need the `isPlaceholderKey` gate per Session 23/25 notes.

### Next Priorities
- CITE-001 (priority 27): citation verifier in src/lib/drift/citation.ts. Pure function: `verifyCitations({ regulatoryText, policyText, regulatoryQuote, policyQuote })` returns boolean. Should normalize whitespace (collapse runs of `\s+` to single space, trim) before substring check, but must NOT case-fold (legal text casing is meaningful: "MUST" vs "must"). Pure logic, fully unit-testable, no LLM or DB dependency. Acceptance steps require: function exists, returns true for quotes that exist in source texts, returns false for fabricated quotes, alert is suppressed when verification fails. The "alert suppression" step belongs in PIPE-001 (the orchestrator wires verifyCitations into the alert-creation decision); CITE-001 itself is just the predicate.
- SCORE-001 (priority 28): severity scorer in src/lib/drift/scorer.ts. Pure function mapping `(classification, confidence)` -> `"high" | "medium" | "low" | null` per app_spec §5 Step 5 table. Returns null for `aligned` / `no_material_impact` (no alert created). Pure logic, fully unit-testable. Specifically: contradicted >= 0.7 -> high, contradicted < 0.7 -> medium, drifted >= 0.8 -> medium, drifted < 0.8 -> low, ambiguous (any) -> low.
- PIPE-001 (priority 29): the orchestrator that wires all of the above (relevance, retrieval, classification, citation, scoring, alert + audit creation) into a single runDriftDetection function. Needs the most setup since it touches 6+ modules and writes 2+ DB tables. Save for a session where the dependency chain is ready (currently CITE-001 + SCORE-001 are the last two prerequisites).

## Session 27 -- Citation Verifier
Date: 2026-05-04

### Feature Worked On
- CITE-001: `verifyCitations({ regulatoryText, regulatoryQuote, policyText, policyQuote })` in src/lib/drift/citation.ts -- pure substring predicate that returns true iff both quotes appear (after whitespace normalization) in their respective source texts. Also exports the lower-level `quoteAppearsIn(quote, sourceText)` helper.
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Replaced the 8-line `verifyCitation(_quote, _sourceText)` stub in src/lib/drift/citation.ts with the real implementation (37 lines: 1 internal `normalizeWhitespace` helper, 2 exported functions, 1 exported `CitationInput` interface). No external callers existed (`grep verifyCitation` returned only the stub itself + a comment in detector.ts), so the rename from `verifyCitation` (singular, 2-arg positional) to `verifyCitations` (plural, single 4-field object literal) is safe. The plural name matches the CITE-001 acceptance step's exact wording and aligns with PIPE-001's expected call-site shape (`verifyCitations({ regulatoryText: regItem.fullText, regulatoryQuote, policyText: chunk.content, policyQuote })`).
- `quoteAppearsIn(quote, sourceText)` is the building block: (a) type-guards both args (returns false for non-string inputs rather than throwing -- more useful at the call site than a TypeError), (b) normalizes the quote with `text.replace(/\s+/g, " ").trim()` and rejects the empty/whitespace-only case, (c) normalizes the source the same way, (d) returns `normalizedSource.includes(normalizedQuote)`. Whitespace normalization handles the real failure mode where Claude returns a quote without the source's exact line wraps / tabs / multi-space indentation -- collapsing all runs of `\s+` to a single space lets a quote like "Currency Transaction Report for transactions exceeding $10,000" match a source that has line wraps mid-quote. The trim() is belt-and-suspenders since the inner replace already collapses leading runs but not the result's leading/trailing spaces if the input started/ended with whitespace.
- Decision: did NOT case-fold. Per Session 26's notes, regulatory drafting distinguishes "MUST" / "SHALL" / "MAY" from their lowercase counterparts (legal-text convention). A case-insensitive match would silently accept a quote that misrepresents the regulation's prescriptive force. The cost of strict casing is low (the LLM-002 prompt explicitly demands "exact characters, including punctuation"), and a future caller that wants tolerance can downcase both sides before calling. Documented this in the inline comment so a future "let's just make it case-insensitive" change has the rationale visible.
- Decision: did NOT extract `quoteAppearsIn` to a separate parsing/text-utils module. It's tightly co-located with the only caller (`verifyCitations`), the helper is short (5 lines of body), and Session 25 set the precedent of "promote to its own module when a third caller appears". Currently zero other callers; PIPE-001 will use `verifyCitations` (the plural object-literal form), not `quoteAppearsIn`.
- Decision: `verifyCitations` returns `false` for a missing/null/non-object input rather than throwing. Same rationale as the type-guard in `quoteAppearsIn` -- the call site (PIPE-001) is going to have a `if (!verifyCitations(...)) suppress()` branch, and forcing it to wrap the call in try/catch for malformed inputs would just push the problem outward. The function's contract is "return true iff both quotes are verifiable"; an empty object is trivially not verifiable.
- Authored `__tests__/unit/citation.test.ts` with 17 tests across 2 describe blocks. quoteAppearsIn (9): literal substring, missing substring, whitespace-run normalization (newlines + tabs + multi-space), quote-side trim, case-sensitivity (MUST vs must), empty-quote rejection, whitespace-only-quote rejection, empty-source rejection, non-string input rejection (undefined, null, number coerced via `as unknown as string`). verifyCitations (8): both-quotes-present happy path, regulatoryQuote fabricated -> false, policyQuote fabricated -> false, both fabricated -> false, either-quote-empty -> false (2 sub-cases), whitespace tolerance against wrapped regulatory text, case-fold rejection, malformed-input handling (undefined / null object).
- No integration test was added because `verifyCitations` is a pure function with no DB / LLM / network dependency -- exactly the same shape as VECTORS-001's `cosineSimilarity`, which also has only a unit test. Adding an integration test for a pure predicate would test nothing new and just slow the suite. PIPE-001 (next-next session) will be where a real prisma + LLM round-trip exercises the verifier in its actual call context.

### Files Modified / Created
- src/lib/drift/citation.ts (replaced 8-line stub with 37-line implementation: exports verifyCitations + quoteAppearsIn + CitationInput)
- __tests__/unit/citation.test.ts (new, 17 tests across both exports)
- specs/phase1/feature_list.json (CITE-001 passes -> true)

### Testing
- Verified all 4 CITE-001 acceptance steps:
  1. src/lib/drift/citation.ts exports a verifyCitations function: confirmed by `grep "export function verifyCitations" src/lib/drift/citation.ts`; the unit test imports it directly and calls it across 8 scenarios.
  2. Quotes that exist in source texts -> returns true: the happy-path test `verifyCitations({ regulatoryText: "Banks must file a Currency Transaction Report for transactions exceeding $10,000 within 15 days.", regulatoryQuote: "transactions exceeding $10,000 within 15 days", policyText: "All cash transactions over $5,000 are reported to the BSA team for review within 30 days.", policyQuote: "cash transactions over $5,000" })` returns true.
  3. Fabricated quote -> returns false: 3 distinct fabrication tests cover regulatoryQuote-only, policyQuote-only, and both-fabricated cases. All return false.
  4. Alert suppression on verification failure: NOT exercised in this session because alert creation lives in PIPE-001 (priority 29). CITE-001 is just the predicate; the suppression wiring belongs to the orchestrator. Documented this in the next-priorities section so PIPE-001's session has a clear hand-off.
- Test suite results: `npm test` -> 14 suites / 106 tests passing (was 13 / 89; +1 suite / +17 tests for citation). Stable across 2 consecutive runs at ~13s.
- Regression: `npx tsc --noEmit` -> zero errors; `curl /` -> 200; `curl /api/health` -> 200; `curl /alerts` -> 200; `curl /ingestion` -> 200. All 13 pre-existing test suites (env, types, db, health, embeddings, vectors, retriever unit + integration, llm unit + integration, prompts, classifier unit + integration) still pass; CORPUS-001..010 / SEED-001 / EMBED-001 / EMBED-002 / VECTORS-001 / RETRIEVE-001 / LLM-001 / LLM-002 / CLASSIFY-001 / CLASSIFY-002 unchanged.

### Blockers / Issues
- The `text.indexOf(...)` -> normalized substring approach is O(n*m) where n is the source length and m is the quote length. For typical inputs (regulatory items <= ~50KB, policy chunks <= ~5KB, quotes <= ~500 chars) this is well under a microsecond. Not optimizing for larger inputs; if a future ingestion pulls in 10MB regulatory documents, the right move is to switch to Boyer-Moore or just accept the linear cost since the quote-verification step happens at most once per (regItem, chunk) pair after retrieval already pruned to top 15 chunks.
- Whitespace normalization uses `\s` (which matches `[\t\n\v\f\r ]` plus various Unicode whitespace categories per Node's regex engine). This includes non-breaking space (U+00A0) -- relevant because copy-pasted regulatory PDFs frequently contain NBSP in place of plain spaces. Tested implicitly by the "wrapped regulatory text" test case (which uses tabs and newlines); did NOT add a dedicated NBSP test because the V8 regex engine handles it via the same `\s` class on the version of Node this project uses (>= 18). Note for future: if a Unicode quote-mismatch bug surfaces in production, the first thing to check is whether smart quotes ("“" vs ") or em dashes (— vs --) need their own normalization step. Not adding pre-emptively because LLM-002's prompt instructs "exact characters" and the policy corpus uses ASCII punctuation throughout.
- `quoteAppearsIn` does NOT handle the case where the model embeds the quote inside a longer phrase that happens to contain the source text as a *suffix*. E.g. quote="must file within 15 days. Failure to comply", source="Banks must file within 15 days." would correctly return false (good -- the model fabricated the trailing clause). The substring check rejects any quote longer than its match window, which is the correct behavior for citation verification (a fabricated extension is still a fabrication).
- The `as unknown as never` cast in the malformed-input test exists because TypeScript correctly rejects passing undefined to a function whose signature requires a CitationInput. The cast is the conventional way to test runtime defensive code paths; there's no compile-time scenario where this branch fires under correct usage. Same pattern as classifier.test.ts uses for non-object input rejection.
- Did NOT change the comment header at the top of citation.ts ("Suppresses alerts where citation verification fails"). The phrasing is slightly forward-looking (CITE-001 is just the predicate, suppression is PIPE-001's job) but it accurately describes the file's *purpose in the system*, not just this session's slice. Leaving it for PIPE-001 to find and not having to edit.

### Next Priorities
- SCORE-001 (priority 28): severity scorer in src/lib/drift/scorer.ts. Pure function mapping `(classification, confidence)` -> `"high" | "medium" | "low" | null`. App_spec §5 Step 5 table: contradicted + confidence >= 0.7 -> high; contradicted + confidence < 0.7 -> medium; drifted + confidence >= 0.8 -> medium; drifted + confidence < 0.8 -> low; ambiguous (any confidence) -> low; aligned / no_material_impact -> null (no alert). Same shape as CITE-001 -- pure logic, unit-test-only, no DB or LLM dependency. Will likely take ~30 mins. Acceptance steps require 5 specific input/output pairs to be verified.
- PIPE-001 (priority 29): runDriftDetection orchestrator in src/lib/drift/detector.ts. The first feature that integrates the entire pipeline: classifyRelevance -> retrieveCandidates -> classifyDrift (per chunk) -> verifyCitations -> deriveSeverity -> Alert + AuditEntry creation. Will need the most setup of any session so far -- 6+ module imports, a real prisma transaction for the Alert + AuditEntry pair, and integration tests that exercise the happy path against the seeded DB. Save for a session where SCORE-001 has just been completed (so the full dependency chain is ready). Per Session 26's notes, the retry-on-timeout policy already lives in classifyDrift, so PIPE-001 just needs to handle "skip item" when a non-recoverable error propagates up.
- PIPE-002 (priority 30): citation-failure alert suppression + itemsSuppressed counter increment. Tightly coupled to PIPE-001 -- could be implemented in the same session if scope allows, or split if PIPE-001 ends up larger than expected.

## Session 28 -- Severity Scorer
Date: 2026-05-04

### Feature Worked On
- SCORE-001: `deriveSeverity(classification, confidence)` in src/lib/drift/scorer.ts -- pure function mapping a `DriftClassification` + a `[0, 1]` confidence to `Severity | null` per app_spec.txt §5 Step 5.
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Replaced the 7-line `computeSeverity(_classification: string, _confidence: number): string` stub with `deriveSeverity(classification: DriftClassification, confidence: number): Severity | null`. Renamed because the acceptance step explicitly requires `deriveSeverity`; no callers of the old name existed (`grep computeSeverity` returned only the stub itself, confirmed before the rename).
- Implementation imports `DriftClassification` and `Severity` from `@/types` (the canonical type-only module), not from `src/lib/ai/prompts.ts` which exports a parallel `DRIFT_CLASSIFICATIONS` const tuple. Two reasons: (a) the scorer doesn't need the runtime const array (only the type), and (b) types in src/types/index.ts are the project's documented surface area per Session 4's INFRA-004 work. Importing from prompts.ts would create a layering inversion (drift/ depends on ai/'s implementation detail).
- Switch over the 5 enum values with explicit cases for `contradicted` (>= 0.7 -> high, else medium), `drifted` (>= 0.8 -> medium, else low), `ambiguous` (any -> low), and `aligned`/`no_material_impact` (both -> null). Default branch uses `const exhaustive: never = classification` to lock in compile-time exhaustiveness; if a future enum value is added without updating the scorer, tsc will fail at the assignment line. Also throws at runtime for the (impossible-under-tsc) case where a bad string slips through.
- Defensive validation of the confidence parameter at the top of the function: rejects non-number, NaN, Infinity (`!Number.isFinite`), and out-of-[0,1] values. Throws with prefixed `deriveSeverity:` error messages so a stack trace from a malformed pipeline call points to the right module immediately. Same defensive style as classifier.ts uses for its response validators -- and per Session 26 notes, the upstream classifier already validates confidence in [0, 1], so a thrown error here would mean a programmer error in the pipeline, not a model-side issue. Preferred throwing over silently returning null because `null` already has a valid meaning ("no alert for aligned classifications") and overloading it with "invalid input" would mask bugs.
- Extracted two named threshold constants (`HIGH_CONTRADICTED_THRESHOLD = 0.7`, `MEDIUM_DRIFTED_THRESHOLD = 0.8`) so the spec table is grep-able and a future tweak (e.g., from PIPE-002 calibration data) is a one-line change. Did not over-extract beyond that -- the switch body is short and direct.

Confirmed: contradicted at exactly 0.7 returns "high" (not "medium"); contradicted at 0.69 returns "medium"; drifted at exactly 0.8 returns "medium" (not "low"); drifted at 0.79 returns "low".
- Null-return tests for aligned and no_material_impact across 4 confidence values each (0, 0.5, 0.99, 1): all return null. This codifies the "no alert created" branch of the spec -- PIPE-001 will rely on the null sentinel to skip alert creation.
- Invalid-input rejection tests: NaN throws /finite number/, Infinity throws /finite number/, -0.1 throws /\[0, 1\]/, 1.1 throws /\[0, 1\]/, "0.8" (string) throws /finite number/, "bogus" classification throws /unknown classification/. The bogus-classification test casts via `as unknown as "aligned"` because tsc would otherwise reject the call -- the cast exercises the runtime exhaustiveness fallback that protects against a future unsafe `as` at the call site.
- Test suite results: `npm test` -> 15 suites / 134 tests passing (was 14 / 106; +1 suite / +28 tests for scorer). Stable at ~17s.

CORPUS-001..010 / SEED-001 / EMBED-001 / EMBED-002 / VECTORS-001 / RETRIEVE-001 / LLM-001 / LLM-002 / CLASSIFY-001 / CLASSIFY-002 / CITE-001 unchanged.

PIPE-001 next session will exercise the full pipeline end-to-end with a real prisma round-trip.

### Blockers / Issues
- Threshold constants are module-private (not exported). If PIPE-002 introduces calibration that needs to read the same thresholds (e.g., for displaying "near-boundary" warnings in the UI), they'll need to be exported then -- but exporting them pre-emptively now would be over-engineering for a hypothetical caller. Per AGENTS.md "Don't design for hypothetical future requirements".
- The exhaustiveness `const exhaustive: never = classification` pattern in the default branch only fires at runtime if a caller does an unsafe cast (`"foo" as DriftClassification`). Under correct typed usage, the default is unreachable and tsc would already have caught a missing case at the assignment site. Test for this branch uses `as unknown as "aligned"` -- the double-cast is the conventional way to exercise compile-time-impossible code paths, same shape as classifier.test.ts uses for non-object-input rejection.
- Did NOT add a "confidence at exactly 0" or "confidence at exactly 1" boundary test for aligned / no_material_impact. Both values are accepted by the [0, 1] range check, and the null-return tests already iterate over 0 and 1 within their it.each. A separate dedicated test would be redundant.
- Decision: function throws (rather than returning null) for invalid inputs. Rationale: null already means "no alert for this classification"; overloading null with "invalid input" would mask bugs in the pipeline. PIPE-001's call-site contract should be: classifyDrift's return -> deriveSeverity's input is always valid; if it isn't, that's a programmer error worth surfacing immediately.
- Did NOT promote the threshold constants to a shared `src/lib/drift/thresholds.ts` module. Only one consumer (this scorer); promotion threshold per Session 25/26/27 rule of thumb is "third caller appears". If PIPE-002 needs to read thresholds for warning display, that'd be the second caller -- still under the threshold for promotion.

- PIPE-001 (priority 29): runDriftDetection orchestrator in src/lib/drift/detector.ts. The first feature that integrates the full pipeline: classifyRelevance -> retrieveCandidates -> classifyDrift (per chunk) -> verifyCitations -> deriveSeverity -> Alert + AuditEntry creation in a prisma transaction. Largest dependency surface so far -- 6+ module imports across ai/ + drift/ + db. Implementation should: (a) early-return when classifyRelevance says irrelevant (per app_spec §5 Step 1); (b) loop chunks from retrieveCandidates and run classifyDrift on each (the spec says top-N chunks, default N=15 per RETRIEVE-001 notes); (c) for each drift result, call verifyCitations -- if false, skip alert and (per PIPE-002) increment itemsSuppressed; (d) call deriveSeverity to get severity or null -- if null, skip alert (aligned / no_material_impact); (e) create the Alert + AuditEntry pair atomically via prisma.$transaction; (f) increment ingestionRun.itemsFlagged for each created alert. Integration test should seed the DB, create a regulatory item, run the orchestrator, and assert Alert and AuditEntry rows exist with the expected shape. Probably needs to mock the Anthropic SDK since the LLM calls would otherwise hit the placeholder key -- reuse the MockAnthropic harness from classifier.test.ts.

Tightly coupled to PIPE-001 -- could be folded into the same session if PIPE-001's scope allows, but more likely a follow-on session because PIPE-001 alone is a substantial integration. Per CITE-001 next-priorities note, the verifyCitations predicate is already wired -- PIPE-002 just adds the `if (!verified) { run.itemsSuppressed++ }` accounting branch in the orchestrator.

## Session 29 -- Drift Detection Pipeline Orchestrator
Date: 2026-05-04

### Feature Worked On
- PIPE-001: `runDriftDetection(regulatoryItemId)` in src/lib/drift/detector.ts -- orchestrator that wires every stage of app_spec.txt §5 (relevance -> retrieval -> per-chunk classification -> citation verification -> severity scoring -> Alert + AuditEntry creation in a per-alert prisma transaction with itemsFlagged increment).
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Replaced the 8-line stub with a 158-line orchestrator. Top-level `runDriftDetection` flow: load RegulatoryItem -> classifyRelevance -> persist isRelevant onto the item row (true/false) -> early-return when irrelevant (per app_spec §5 Step 1) -> build query text `${title}\n\n${fullText.slice(0, RETRIEVAL_TEXT_LIMIT)}` and call retrieveCandidates -> loop candidates through `processCandidate`. Returns a `DriftDetectionResult` summary (`{ regulatoryItemId, isRelevant, candidatesEvaluated, alertsCreated, citationFailures, classificationErrors }`) so callers can assert pipeline behavior without re-querying the DB.
- Decision: changed the function's return type from `Promise<void>` (the stub's signature) to `Promise<DriftDetectionResult>`. The stub had no callers, so the contract was free to evolve. The summary object is what API routes (POST /api/ingestion/trigger eventually) and integration tests both want -- forcing them to re-count via `prisma.alert.count()` would be redundant work and racey under concurrent runs.
- Per-candidate work is factored into a private `processCandidate` helper. Each candidate: (a) loads its parent PolicyDocument (needed for the `policyReference` "Title > SectionHeading" string); (b) calls classifyDrift wrapped in try/catch so one bad LLM round-trip skips just that chunk -- it does NOT abort the entire run; (c) calls verifyCitations as a hard gate (returns null on failure -- no alert created); (d) calls deriveSeverity (returns null for aligned/no_material_impact -- no alert created); (e) creates Alert + AuditEntry + IngestionRun.itemsFlagged increment atomically in a single prisma.$transaction.
- Decision: per-alert transactions, not one-big-transaction-per-run. Rationale: a long batch where chunk #14's LLM call throws should still leave alerts #1..#13 persisted. The per-alert transaction also keeps the AuditEntry + Alert + counter increment atomic (the three-row invariant), which matches how the audit table is meant to be read (every alert has at least one created-row audit entry).
- Decision: classifyDrift errors are *swallowed* (counted in `classificationErrors`, not rethrown). The retry-once-on-timeout policy already lives inside classifyDrift (see Session 26 / classifier.ts:174), so by the time an error reaches the orchestrator it represents either (a) a non-timeout API error (auth, 4xx), (b) a malformed-JSON response, or (c) a second-attempt timeout. None of those should cascade-fail the rest of the run -- the spec's "log and continue" pattern (§6) applies. PolicyDocument-not-found also counts as a classification error rather than throwing, since a missing parent for a chunk that *was* embedded indicates a seed-time inconsistency, not a programmer error worth halting on.
- Decision: did NOT use the audit.ts helper (still a stub from project init). Inlining the auditEntry.create call inside the same prisma.$transaction is necessary for atomicity -- audit.ts can't participate in a caller-owned transaction without becoming a (tx) => arrow, which would require designing its full API now. PIPE-002 / ALERT-* features will likely promote audit.ts into a real helper once a second caller (alert-status-change endpoints) appears -- that's the right time to settle on the API shape.
- Embedding query construction: title + first 4000 chars of fullText. Reason: the spec says "title + key paragraphs"; 4000 chars (~1000 tokens) is a safe slice that keeps the embedding API call under most provider limits while capturing the document's leading substance. Constant `RETRIEVAL_TEXT_LIMIT = 4000` is module-private; if EMBED-* features ever need a different cap, this is a one-line change.
- Authored `__tests__/integration/detector.test.ts` (290 lines, 2 tests). Test 1 (happy path): picks the smallest seeded chunk under 3500 chars, sets `item.title = chunk.sectionHeading` and `item.fullText = chunk.content` so the orchestrator's query string `${title}\n\n${fullText.slice(0, 4000)}` byte-matches the chunk's seed-time embedding input and the deterministic fallback embedding produces a vector with similarity == 1.0. Stages a fresh IngestionRun + RegulatoryItem, runs the orchestrator, then asserts: (a) result summary fields; (b) Alert.count delta == result.alertsCreated.length; (c) AuditEntry.count delta == result.alertsCreated.length; (d) every Alert row has all 11 required fields (regulatoryItemId, policyChunkId, classification ∈ enum, confidence ∈ [0,1], severity ∈ {high, medium, low}, non-empty explanation/quotes, regulatorySourceUrl matches item, policyReference matches "X > Y" pattern, status defaults to "open"); (e) every Alert has exactly one AuditEntry with actor=system action=created; (f) IngestionRun.itemsFlagged equals the alert count; (g) RegulatoryItem.isRelevant was persisted to true; (h) LlmCallLog count grew by 1 (relevance) + N (per-candidate classification). Test 2 (irrelevant): mocks one-shot relevance=false response, runs the orchestrator, asserts no alerts created, RegulatoryItem.isRelevant=false persisted, IngestionRun.itemsFlagged=0, and exactly 1 LlmCallLog row added (the relevance call -- no classification calls fire after early-return).
- Mock harness: same MockAnthropic + jest.unstable_mockModule pattern as classifier.test.ts, with the addition of mocking `@/lib/ai/embeddings` to use the deterministic fallback (mirrors retriever.test.ts so seeded vectors are reproducible at query time without an API key).
- Both tests track every created row (alert/audit/regItem/run/log) in arrays and tear them down in afterAll. The teardown is ordered (audits -> alerts -> items -> runs -> logs) to satisfy FK constraints.

### Files Modified / Created
- src/lib/drift/detector.ts (replaced 8-line stub with 158-line implementation: 1 export `runDriftDetection`, 1 exported `DriftDetectionResult` interface, 1 private `processCandidate` helper, 1 private `ProcessHandlers` interface, 1 module-private `RETRIEVAL_TEXT_LIMIT = 4000` constant)
- __tests__/integration/detector.test.ts (new, 290 lines, 2 integration tests with deterministic-embedding + Anthropic-SDK mocks)
- specs/phase1/feature_list.json (PIPE-001 passes -> true)

### Testing
- Verified all 6 PIPE-001 acceptance steps:
  1. src/lib/drift/detector.ts exports a runDriftDetection function: confirmed by `grep "export.*runDriftDetection" src/lib/drift/detector.ts` and the integration test imports it via `import { runDriftDetection } from "@/lib/drift/detector"`.
  2. Database seeded with policy corpus: the integration test's beforeAll hook explicitly counts `policyChunk where embedding != null` and throws if zero, ensuring the test only runs against a seeded DB. Live count is 154 chunks (per the chunk-size inspection).
