- Test suite results: `npm test` -> 16 suites / 136 tests passing (was 15 / 134; +1 suite / +2 tests for detector). Stable at ~15s.
- Regression: `npx tsc --noEmit` -> zero errors; `curl /` -> 200; `curl /api/health` -> 200; `curl /alerts` -> 200; `curl /ingestion` -> 200. All 15 pre-existing test suites unchanged. CORPUS-001..010 / SEED-001 / EMBED-001 / EMBED-002 / VECTORS-001 / RETRIEVE-001 / LLM-001 / LLM-002 / CLASSIFY-001 / CLASSIFY-002 / CITE-001 / SCORE-001 unchanged.
- No Playwright verification: PIPE-001 has no UI surface (it's invoked by API routes that have not yet been implemented). PIPE-002 follows the same pattern. The first feature that needs Playwright will be the dashboard-trigger button (`POST /api/ingestion/trigger`) where the orchestrator runs in response to a UI action.

### Blockers / Issues
- The integration test required deterministic-embedding alignment between the orchestrator's query construction and the seed's chunk-content hashing. The first attempt set `item.fullText` to `${chunk.sectionHeading}\n\n${chunk.content}\n\nFinal rule: ${quote}...` -- which, sliced to 4000 chars and prefixed with the title, did NOT byte-match the seed's `${chunk.sectionHeading}\n\n${chunk.content}` input. Result: similarity ≈ 0, no candidates returned, alert count 0. Fix: set `item.title = chunk.sectionHeading` and `item.fullText = chunk.content` directly (and pick a chunk whose content is < 3500 chars so the slice(0, 4000) is a no-op). This is a TEST-ONLY constraint -- in production, the embedding API produces semantically-similar vectors for related-but-not-identical text, so the orchestrator's title+slice query is correct. The deterministic fallback's byte-sensitivity is a seed-time convenience for keyless dev environments, NOT a real similarity surface.
- The classifier.ts `classifyDrift` already retries once on timeout (Session 26). The orchestrator does NOT add a second retry layer -- a swallowed-then-counted classification error after the inner retry is the spec's "skip item" path. Adding orchestrator-level retry would double the latency cost on persistent failures without improving the recovery rate.
- itemsSuppressed counter is NOT incremented by PIPE-001 even though the orchestrator already detects citation failures and skips the alert. Reason: PIPE-002 explicitly owns "increments the itemsSuppressed counter on the ingestion run" -- splitting that one-line accounting from the suppression decision keeps PIPE-001's diff focused. The orchestrator already returns `citationFailures` in its summary, so PIPE-002 only needs to add a single `await tx.ingestionRun.update({ ..., data: { itemsSuppressed: { increment: 1 } } })` in the suppression branch.
- The `processCandidate` helper takes a structurally-typed regItem `{ id, fullText, sourceUrl, ingestionRunId }` rather than a Prisma `RegulatoryItem`. Reason: the helper only needs 4 fields; importing the Prisma model type would couple the helper to a generated module path that ts-jest sometimes resolves differently than `tsc --noEmit`. The structural type is precise enough that tsc rejects passing a `{ id }`-only object.
- audit.ts is still a stub (`throw new Error("Not implemented")`). Not a regression -- nothing calls it. PIPE-001 inlines the AuditEntry creation inside its own transaction. Future audit-related features (alert status changes, dismissal, escalation) will need to settle on whether audit.ts becomes a transaction-aware helper (`createAuditEntry(tx, ...)`) or stays caller-owned. Defer until the second caller appears (per the Session 25/26/27/28 promotion-threshold rule).
- Did NOT add a separate test for the "drift result whose verifyCitations returns false" suppression branch. Reason: that's PIPE-002's acceptance step. PIPE-001's coverage is "alerts ARE created in the happy path" + "no alerts when not relevant". The PIPE-002 session will add a third test where the mock returns a fabricated quote and assert `result.alertsCreated.length === 0` + `result.citationFailures > 0` + `run.itemsSuppressed > 0`.
- The integration test's deterministic-embedding setup relies on the seed having been run with the placeholder OPENAI_API_KEY (so the fallback path was used). If a real OpenAI key is later configured and the seed is re-run, the chunk vectors will be real OpenAI embeddings, and the test's deterministic-embedding mock will produce uncorrelated query vectors -> similarity == 0 -> no candidates -> test fails. Workaround for that future case: the test would need to re-seed in beforeAll with a forced-fallback EMBEDDING_PROVIDER (or mock retrieveCandidates entirely to return a fixed chunk). Documenting here so the failure mode is recognizable.

### Next Priorities
- PIPE-002 (priority 30): citation-failure alert suppression + itemsSuppressed counter. The orchestrator already detects citation failures and skips alert creation -- PIPE-002 just needs to add `await tx.ingestionRun.update({ where: { id: regItem.ingestionRunId }, data: { itemsSuppressed: { increment: 1 } } })` in the citation-failure branch (currently only `handlers.onCitationFailure()` runs the in-memory counter). The increment must be in its own transaction (the Alert.create transaction never runs in this branch). Integration test should mock the LLM to return a fabricated quote, run the orchestrator, assert `result.alertsCreated.length === 0`, `result.citationFailures > 0`, and `run.itemsSuppressed === result.citationFailures`. Tightly scoped, ~30 min including the test.
- INGEST-001 (priority 31): the actual ingestion entry point (`POST /api/ingestion/trigger`). This is where runDriftDetection finally gets called from a real HTTP path. Will need: (a) IngestionRun creation; (b) parser dispatch (SEC/FINRA/CFPB/OCC fetchLatest stubs are already in place); (c) per-item runDriftDetection calls in a sequential or bounded-parallel loop; (d) IngestionRun.completedAt + status="completed" finalization. Larger scope than PIPE-001 -- save for a session after PIPE-002. Per app_spec.txt §6, the parsers may return a small number of real or cached items; the trigger endpoint just needs to wire them into the orchestrator.
- DASH-001 / API-002 / API-003: dashboard endpoints + API contract. Lower urgency than completing the pipeline plumbing -- the data flow needs to work end-to-end before the UI can display it.

## Session 30 -- Citation-Failure Alert Suppression Counter
Date: 2026-05-05

### Feature Worked On
- PIPE-002: orchestrator suppresses alerts when verifyCitations returns false AND increments `IngestionRun.itemsSuppressed` for each suppressed candidate. Per Session 29 hand-off, the suppression DECISION already existed in PIPE-001 (the `if (!verified) return null` branch) -- this session adds the persistent counter accounting alongside it.
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Added a single `await prisma.ingestionRun.update({ where: { id: regItem.ingestionRunId }, data: { itemsSuppressed: { increment: 1 } } })` immediately after the existing `handlers.onCitationFailure()` call in `processCandidate` (src/lib/drift/detector.ts:145-152). The in-memory counter (returned in the result summary) and the persistent counter (visible to dashboard queries / IngestionRun reads) are now both updated in the same suppression branch.
- Decision: kept the increment OUTSIDE a transaction. The Alert.create transaction never runs in this branch (the function returns null before reaching it), so there's no atomicity boundary to share -- a one-row counter increment is naturally atomic in SQLite/Prisma. Adding a transactional wrapper would be ceremony for a single statement.
- Decision: did NOT batch suppressed counts across the run (e.g., counting all failures in memory and writing a single `update({ data: { itemsSuppressed: { increment: N } } })` after the loop). Per-suppression increments cost one extra UPDATE per failed candidate, but mean partial-run visibility (a query against IngestionRun while the orchestrator is still iterating sees an accurate-so-far count). Matches the existing per-alert `itemsFlagged: { increment: 1 }` pattern from PIPE-001 -- consistency over micro-optimization.
- Decision: the integration test reuses the existing detector.test.ts harness (MockAnthropic + deterministic embedding mock) rather than creating a parallel test file. The mutation pattern -- module-scoped `driftRegulatoryQuote` / `driftPolicyQuote` that the mock reads on each call -- already supports per-test customization, so the new test just sets fabricated values and re-runs the orchestrator. Avoids duplicating ~90 lines of mock harness setup.
- Updated the file-level comment block in detector.ts (lines 12-14) to drop the "PIPE-002 will add..." forward-reference and replace it with the present-tense statement of the feature now that PIPE-002 is implemented.

### Files Modified / Created
- src/lib/drift/detector.ts (+5 lines: 4 for the increment block, 1 net for the comment update)
- __tests__/integration/detector.test.ts (+78 lines: new third `it()` block exercising the fabricated-quote path)
- specs/phase1/feature_list.json (PIPE-002 passes -> true)

### Testing
- Verified all 4 PIPE-002 acceptance steps:
  1. "Create a test scenario where the LLM returns a fabricated quote": the new test sets `driftRegulatoryQuote = "this exact phrase never appears in any seeded chunk xyzzy 4242"` and `driftPolicyQuote = "another fabricated phrase plugh 9999 not in corpus"`. The mock then returns these strings as the quotes for every drift call, guaranteeing verifyCitations rejection (neither string is a substring of any seeded chunk content).
  2. "Run the pipeline": `await runDriftDetection(item.id)` -- same call shape as the happy-path test.
  3. "Verify no alert is created for the fabricated citation": `expect(result.alertsCreated).toEqual([])`; also `expect(alertCountAfter).toBe(alertCountBefore)` to confirm no rows were persisted to the Alert table.
  4. "Verify the ingestion run's itemsSuppressed count was incremented": `expect(updatedRun.itemsSuppressed).toBe(result.citationFailures)` -- and `expect(result.citationFailures).toBe(result.candidatesEvaluated)` codifies the "ALL candidates suppressed" branch (because the deterministic embedding only retrieves the matching chunk and the mock fabricates BOTH quotes, all retrievals hit the suppression branch).
- Test suite results: `npm test` -> 16 suites / 137 tests passing (was 16 / 136; +1 test for PIPE-002 suppression). Stable at ~18s.
- Regression: `npx tsc --noEmit` -> zero errors; `curl /` -> 200; `curl /api/health` -> 200; `curl /alerts` -> 200; `curl /ingestion` -> 200. All previously-passing tests still pass; PIPE-001's happy-path test (which asserts `citationFailures === 0` and `itemsSuppressed` is unchanged) still passes -- my new branch only fires when verifyCitations returns false, and in the happy path it does not.
- No Playwright verification: PIPE-002 has no UI surface (it's a backend counter accessed via the orchestrator). The first PIPE-* feature to need browser verification will be the dashboard's "items suppressed" metric tile (DASH-* range), which reads IngestionRun.itemsSuppressed.

### Blockers / Issues
- The PIPE-002 test relies on the deterministic embedding only returning ONE candidate (the sample chunk itself), because the SHA-256-based fallback produces near-zero cosine similarity for unrelated chunks and only the byte-identical query crosses SIMILARITY_THRESHOLD=0.3. If the seed is ever re-run with a real OpenAI key, the fallback path won't fire and multiple chunks may get retrieved -- the assertion `expect(result.citationFailures).toBe(result.candidatesEvaluated)` would still pass (the mock returns fabricated quotes for ALL drift calls), but `expect(updatedRun.itemsSuppressed).toBe(result.citationFailures)` would scale with N>1. Both assertions remain correct; the test is robust to the candidate count.
- Decision: the in-memory `result.citationFailures` counter and the persistent `IngestionRun.itemsSuppressed` field are intentionally separate. The in-memory one is the orchestrator's "what happened in THIS invocation" counter and is what the test asserts equality against. The persistent one is the cross-invocation total across the run (an IngestionRun may aggregate calls from multiple regulatory items in the future via INGEST-001). For a single-item invocation they happen to be equal; for a multi-item run the persistent counter accumulates while in-memory resets per call.
- Did NOT promote `prisma.ingestionRun.update({...itemsSuppressed: { increment: 1 } })` and the matching `itemsFlagged: { increment: 1 }` (PIPE-001's per-alert path) into a shared `incrementRunCounter(runId, field)` helper. Two callers, one each per field, no third caller in sight. Per the Session 25/26/27/28 promotion-threshold rule, wait for the third call site -- likely INGEST-001's per-run setup/teardown counters.
- The orchestrator does NOT decrement itemsSuppressed if a later stage somehow fails after a successful citation pass. There's no such stage -- the only thing after the citation gate is `deriveSeverity` (which can return null but means "aligned/no_material_impact", a different, non-suppressed branch) and the Alert.create transaction (which throws on failure, propagating up out of processCandidate). Defensive bookkeeping for compensation isn't needed here.
- The MockAnthropic harness in detector.test.ts uses module-scoped mutable state (`driftRegulatoryQuote` / `driftPolicyQuote`) that the three tests now read in different ways. Tests run in file declaration order in jest, so test 1 sets the substring quotes, test 2 doesn't touch them (uses a one-shot relevance=false override), test 3 sets fabricated quotes. If a future test added a fourth `it()` between test 1 and test 3, it would inherit test 1's substring quotes -- a setup/cleanup pattern (e.g., `beforeEach` resetting to a sentinel) might be cleaner. Deferred because it's a 78-line file-level concern that doesn't affect this session's correctness.

### Next Priorities
- INGEST-001 (priority 31): the actual ingestion entry point -- `POST /api/ingestion/trigger`. This is where runDriftDetection finally gets called from a real HTTP path. Will need: (a) IngestionRun creation; (b) parser dispatch (SEC/FINRA/CFPB/OCC fetchLatest stubs are already in place); (c) per-item runDriftDetection calls in a sequential or bounded-parallel loop; (d) IngestionRun.completedAt + status="completed" finalization. Larger scope than PIPE-001/002 -- likely 1-2 sessions. Per app_spec.txt §6, the parsers may return a small number of real or cached items; the trigger endpoint just needs to wire them into the orchestrator.
- INGEST-005 (priority 35): HTTP fetcher utility. Cross-cutting dependency for INGEST-001..004; could be implemented first if the parsers are about to be touched. Pure utility (URL -> result | error), small surface, integration test against a known-bad URL.
- INGEST-001..004: the four regulator-specific parsers (SEC, FINRA, CFPB, OCC). Each is a separate feature but shares the same shape -- a single session might cover one parser end-to-end with real network calls (or fall back to cached fixtures if the upstream is unreachable). Order doesn't matter much; SEC has the most public-facing material to scrape so it's the natural first.
- DASH-001 / API-002 / API-003: dashboard endpoints + API contract. Lower urgency than the ingestion-trigger plumbing -- the data flow needs to work end-to-end before the UI can display it.

## Session 31 -- SEC Parser
Date: 2026-05-05

### Feature Worked On
- INGEST-001: `fetchLatest()` in `src/lib/ingestion/parsers/sec.ts` -- fetches the SEC's public press-releases RSS feed, parses each `<item>` into a `RawRegulatoryItem`, and falls back to a pre-downloaded `data/regulatory/sec/cache.json` fixture when the live request fails (network, non-2xx, timeout, or zero parseable items).
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Added a new `RawRegulatoryItem` interface to `src/types/index.ts` (sourceUrl, regulator: Regulator, publicationDate: Date, documentType: string, title: string, fullText: string -- matches app_spec.txt §6 exactly). The Regulator union and DocumentType union were already exported; reusing them keeps the parser/pipeline contract type-safe end to end. `documentType` stays a `string` (per the spec) because raw parser output may not yet match the canonical `DocumentType` union -- normalization happens during persistence (INGEST-006 territory).
- Replaced the 7-line `sec.ts` stub with a 132-line implementation:
  - `parseSecRss(xml)` -- regex-based RSS 2.0 `<item>` block extractor (case-insensitive `<item>`/`<ITEM>` matching, CDATA-aware tag content extractor, XML entity decoder, HTML stripper). No external dep -- the project has no XML library in package.json, and a regex extractor handles SEC's stable RSS shape without pulling in jsdom/cheerio for one feed.
  - `rssItemToRaw(item)` -- maps an `SecRssItem` to a `RawRegulatoryItem`; returns null when title/link/pubDate are missing or when `new Date(pubDate)` produces NaN. Documents documentType as `"press_release"` (raw, pre-normalization).
  - `fetchRss(url, timeoutMs)` -- private; uses a per-call `AbortController` with a 10s default to bound the network call; sets `User-Agent: "Tether Compliance Demo dev@tether.local"` per SEC's developer-guidelines requirement that automated callers identify themselves with a contact-bearing UA (https://www.sec.gov/os/accessing-edgar-data); throws on non-2xx HTTP.
  - `loadCache()` -- private; reads `data/regulatory/sec/cache.json` and revives `publicationDate` strings into `Date` instances.
  - `fetchLatest()` -- exported; tries live fetch -> fall back to cache on any failure (caught in a single try/catch covering network errors, abort/timeout, HTTP errors, RSS-with-zero-parseable-items) -> fall back to `[]` if the cache load also fails. Logs every fall-back transition via `console.warn` with the failing URL/path and error message in the log line so an operator can trace which leg of the pipeline degraded.
- Created `data/regulatory/sec/cache.json` with two fixture press-release items (publicationDate, sourceUrl, regulator: "SEC", documentType, title, fullText). Realistic-looking SEC press release content covering AI disclosure controls and FY2024 enforcement results -- chosen so the integration tests can exercise the fall-back path with semantically sensible content (the cached items eventually get drift-detected against the synthetic policy corpus once INGEST-006 wires the parsers into the pipeline).
- Authored `__tests__/unit/sec.test.ts` (147 lines, 11 tests) covering `parseSecRss` (CDATA, entity decoding, no-items, case-insensitive matching) and `rssItemToRaw` (well-formed mapping, null returns for missing/invalid fields, fullText fallback to title, HTML stripping in titles).
- Authored `__tests__/integration/sec.test.ts` (138 lines, 5 tests) covering `fetchLatest` end-to-end: (a) live fetch success path -- verifies SEC_RSS_URL is hit with the contact-bearing User-Agent, parsed items match expected fields; (b) network error path -- mocks `global.fetch` to throw, verifies cache fall-back, asserts the warning log carries the failing URL + error message; (c) HTTP 503 path -- verifies cache fall-back; (d) empty-feed path (`<rss><channel></channel></rss>`) -- verifies cache fall-back; (e) timeout path -- mock fetch returns a Promise that respects the abort signal and rejects with AbortError when fired.
- Mocking pattern: each test reassigns `global.fetch` and resets it in `afterEach` (the previous LLM test pattern uses `jest.unstable_mockModule` to mock the Anthropic SDK; for `fetch` -- a global, not a module -- direct reassignment is the natural shape). `console.warn` is silenced via a top-level spy and asserted on a per-test basis through `mock.calls`.

### Files Modified / Created
- src/types/index.ts (+9 lines: new `RawRegulatoryItem` interface; existing types untouched)
- src/lib/ingestion/parsers/sec.ts (replaced 7-line stub with 132-line implementation: 4 exports `fetchLatest`/`parseSecRss`/`rssItemToRaw`/`SEC_RSS_URL`/`SEC_FETCH_TIMEOUT_MS`; 1 exported `SecRssItem` interface; private helpers `fetchRss`/`loadCache`/`extractTag`/`decodeEntities`/`stripHtml`)
- data/regulatory/sec/cache.json (new, 2 fixture items)
- __tests__/unit/sec.test.ts (new, 11 tests across parseSecRss + rssItemToRaw)
- __tests__/integration/sec.test.ts (new, 5 tests across the four fall-back paths + the live-success path)
- specs/phase1/feature_list.json (INGEST-001 passes -> true)

### Testing
- Verified all 4 INGEST-001 acceptance steps:
  1. `src/lib/ingestion/parsers/sec.ts` exists and exports `fetchLatest`: confirmed by `import { fetchLatest, SEC_RSS_URL } from "@/lib/ingestion/parsers/sec"` in the integration test (which compiles + executes successfully).
  2. Calling `fetchLatest` returns an array of items: integration test asserts `items.length > 0` (live success) or `items.length > 0` (cache fall-back) across all 5 test scenarios; type-system also enforces `Promise<RawRegulatoryItem[]>` return type.
  3. Each item has sourceUrl, regulator='SEC', publicationDate, documentType, title, fullText: integration test loops and asserts `item.regulator === "SEC"`, `item.sourceUrl` matches /^https?:\/\//, `item.publicationDate` is a Date with `Number.isFinite(getTime())`, `item.documentType.length > 0`, `item.title.length > 0`, `item.fullText.length > 0`.
  4. Parser handles network errors gracefully without crashing: 4 separate test scenarios exercise the fall-back paths -- thrown error (ECONNREFUSED), HTTP 503 non-OK, empty feed, abort/timeout. None of them throw out of `fetchLatest`; all return the cached fixture array.
- Test suite results: `npm test` -> 18 suites / 153 tests passing (was 16 / 137; +2 suites / +16 tests for INGEST-001 -- 11 unit + 5 integration). Stable at ~19s.
- Regression: `npx tsc --noEmit` -> zero errors; `curl /` -> 200; `curl /api/health` -> 200; `curl /alerts` -> 200; `curl /ingestion` -> 200. All 16 pre-existing test suites unchanged. CORPUS-001..010 / SEED-001 / EMBED-001..002 / VECTORS-001 / RETRIEVE-001 / LLM-001..002 / CLASSIFY-001..002 / CITE-001 / SCORE-001 / PIPE-001..002 unchanged.
- No Playwright verification: INGEST-001 has no UI surface (it's a backend module called from the ingestion pipeline). The first INGEST-* feature to need browser verification will be the dashboard's "Trigger Ingestion" button (INGEST-006 / API-001-trigger -- whichever wires the orchestrator to a UI POST).

### Blockers / Issues
- Decision: regex-based RSS parsing instead of pulling in fast-xml-parser, xml2js, jsdom, or cheerio. Rationale: the project has no XML library in package.json today, the SEC RSS shape is RFC-stable, and adding a dep just for one parser would balloon the install footprint. If FINRA/CFPB/OCC turn out to need richer XML/HTML handling (e.g., XPath, namespace-aware queries, or HTML scraping) we should revisit -- the natural promotion threshold per the Session 25..28 rule of thumb is "third caller appears". For now, two callers (parseSecRss + future regex shape for the remaining three regulators) is below the threshold.
- Decision: documentType = "press_release" as a raw string, not coerced into the `DocumentType` union (`final_rule | proposed_rule | enforcement | bulletin | notice | guidance | letter`). The spec at line 385 declares `RawRegulatoryItem.documentType: string` (lowercase string) while the persisted `RegulatoryItem.documentType` uses the enum union. Normalization is the pipeline's job (INGEST-006 territory) -- forcing the parser to guess a target union value from the press-release feed would either map everything to "notice"/"guidance" (lossy) or require a brittle keyword classifier inside the parser. Cleaner to surface the raw vendor-side type and let the persistence layer normalize.
- Decision: the cache fixture has only 2 items. Sufficient to verify the fall-back path returns a non-empty array with all six required fields. Adding more would inflate the diff without exercising new code paths -- the `parseSecRss` regex is exercised in unit tests with multi-item XML, so the multi-item handling is already covered.
- The integration test's timeout-path assertion uses `jest.useFakeTimers({ doNotFake: ["nextTick"] })` to force the AbortController's `setTimeout` to fire instantly without making the test wait the full 10s. The `doNotFake: ["nextTick"]` is needed because the AbortError rejection path resolves through process.nextTick microtasks and faking them would deadlock the await. This is a Jest 30 idiom -- if Jest is upgraded, re-verify.
- Decision: the `fetchLatest` warning logs use `console.warn`, not the structured-logger pattern that LLM-001 uses for `LlmCallLog`. Reason: there's no equivalent `IngestionRunLog` model in prisma/schema.prisma, and inventing one for a parser fall-back would be ahead of what the spec asks for. INGEST-006 (the pipeline orchestrator) will surface ingestion errors via `IngestionRun.errors` (text column) -- the parser's job is just to log + return; the orchestrator wraps the log in a run-level error trail.
- Decision: relied on Node 20+ global `fetch` rather than adding `node-fetch`. Next.js 16 / React 19.2 require Node 20+, so global fetch is guaranteed in every supported runtime. No polyfill needed.
- The User-Agent string `"Tether Compliance Demo dev@tether.local"` uses a placeholder contact email. SEC's access guidelines technically require a real, monitored contact. For the demo this is fine; for production deployment the User-Agent should be updated to a real contact at the deploying organization (this is a one-line edit in sec.ts:21 if needed).
- Did NOT promote the fetch-with-timeout helper to a shared `src/lib/ingestion/fetcher.ts` module (which is still a stub). INGEST-005 explicitly owns the shared fetcher utility. When INGEST-005 is implemented, the SEC parser's `fetchRss` should be refactored to call into it -- but doing the promotion now (with no second caller in sight) would be over-engineering for the same reason audit.ts and the threshold constants stayed module-private in earlier sessions.

### Next Priorities
- INGEST-005 (priority 35): HTTP fetcher utility (`src/lib/ingestion/fetcher.ts`). The SEC parser's `fetchRss` helper already does timeout + UA + non-2xx-throws -- promoting it to `fetcher.ts` and having the parser call into it is a natural refactor once a second caller exists. INGEST-002 (FINRA) is the natural second caller. Implementation order options: (a) implement INGEST-005 first as a clean utility, then INGEST-002..004 each call into it; (b) implement INGEST-002 with copy-paste of fetchRss, then INGEST-005 promotes the third copy. Option (a) is cleaner; option (b) follows the "third caller" rule strictly. Recommend (a) because `fetchRss` is already factored well enough to extract one-shot.
- INGEST-002 (priority 32): FINRA parser. Same shape as SEC -- the FINRA notices RSS feed at https://www.finra.org/rules-guidance/notices/rss is structurally identical RSS 2.0. Should be a near-copy of sec.ts with URL + regulator field swapped + a finra cache fixture. Probably 30 minutes including tests.
- INGEST-003 (priority 33): CFPB parser. CFPB exposes an RSS feed at https://files.consumerfinance.gov/f/feeds/cfpb_publications.xml (or similar) -- needs verification at implementation time. Same shape as SEC.
- INGEST-004 (priority 34): OCC parser. OCC bulletins/news live at https://www.occ.gov/news-issuances/ -- they have an RSS feed at https://www.occ.gov/rss/occ_alert.xml. Same shape.
- INGEST-006 (priority 36): pipeline orchestrator (`src/lib/ingestion/pipeline.ts:runIngestion`) -- the entry point that calls all four parsers, deduplicates by sourceUrl, persists new items, and runs `runDriftDetection` on each new item. Larger session -- save until 2..4 of the parsers are landed.

## Session 32 -- FINRA Parser
Date: 2026-05-05

### Feature Worked On
- INGEST-002: `fetchLatest()` in `src/lib/ingestion/parsers/finra.ts` -- fetches FINRA's regulatory-notices RSS feed, parses each `<item>` into a `RawRegulatoryItem`, and falls back to a pre-downloaded `data/regulatory/finra/cache.json` fixture when the live request fails (network, non-2xx, timeout, or zero parseable items). Structurally identical to INGEST-001's SEC parser.
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Replaced the 7-line `finra.ts` stub with a 132-line implementation mirroring `sec.ts`. Same export surface (`fetchLatest`, `parseFinraRss`, `rssItemToRaw`, `FINRA_RSS_URL`, `FINRA_FETCH_TIMEOUT_MS`, `FinraRssItem`); same private helpers (`fetchRss`, `loadCache`, `extractTag`, `decodeEntities`, `stripHtml`); same 3-tier fall-back (live -> cache -> []); same `console.warn` log format with the failing URL/path embedded.
- Differences vs SEC: `FINRA_RSS_URL = "https://www.finra.org/rules-guidance/notices/rss"`; `regulator: "FINRA"`; `documentType: "regulatory_notice"` (raw vendor-side type, not yet normalized to the `DocumentType` union -- normalization is INGEST-006's job per the same rationale as Session 31).
- Created `data/regulatory/finra/cache.json` with two fixture items: 25-01 (customer complaint reporting under Rule 4530, complaint-handling domain) and 25-04 (generative AI guidance, info-security/vendor-management domains). Chosen so the cached items eventually exercise drift-detection paths against the synthetic policy corpus when the orchestrator is wired up.
- Authored `__tests__/unit/finra.test.ts` (147 lines, 11 tests) covering `parseFinraRss` (CDATA, entity decoding, no-items, case-insensitive matching) and `rssItemToRaw` (well-formed mapping, null returns for missing/invalid fields, fullText fallback to title, HTML stripping in titles).
- Authored `__tests__/integration/finra.test.ts` (138 lines, 5 tests) covering `fetchLatest` end-to-end: (a) live fetch success path -- verifies FINRA_RSS_URL is hit with the contact-bearing User-Agent, parsed items match expected fields; (b) network error path -- mocks `global.fetch` to throw, verifies cache fall-back, asserts the warning log carries the failing URL + error message; (c) HTTP 503 path; (d) empty-feed path; (e) timeout/abort path.
- Decision: did NOT promote any of the duplicated helpers (`extractTag`, `decodeEntities`, `stripHtml`, `fetchRss`, `loadCache`, `ITEM_BLOCK_RE`) into a shared module. INGEST-005 owns the shared HTTP fetcher utility, and per the Session 25..31 promotion-threshold rule of thumb the right time to extract is when the third caller appears. Two callers (SEC + FINRA) are below the threshold; CFPB will be the third and is a natural promotion trigger. The duplication is mechanical and visible in adjacent files; refactoring now would couple INGEST-002's diff to INGEST-005's surface area.
- Decision: kept the User-Agent string identical to SEC's (`"Tether Compliance Demo dev@tether.local"`). FINRA does not have SEC's hard contact-UA requirement, but a consistent UA across regulators makes `fetcher.ts` a one-line drop-in when INGEST-005 lands. The placeholder email is still a placeholder; production would update to a real contact.

### Files Modified / Created
- src/lib/ingestion/parsers/finra.ts (replaced 7-line stub with 132-line implementation)
- data/regulatory/finra/cache.json (new, 2 fixture items)
- __tests__/unit/finra.test.ts (new, 11 tests)
- __tests__/integration/finra.test.ts (new, 5 tests)
- specs/phase1/feature_list.json (INGEST-002 passes -> true)

### Testing
- Verified all 4 INGEST-002 acceptance steps:
  1. `src/lib/ingestion/parsers/finra.ts` exists and exports `fetchLatest`: confirmed by `import { fetchLatest, FINRA_RSS_URL } from "@/lib/ingestion/parsers/finra"` in the integration test (compiles + runs).
  2. Calling `fetchLatest` returns an array of items: integration test asserts `items.length > 0` (live success) or `items.length > 0` (cache fall-back) across all 5 scenarios; type system enforces `Promise<RawRegulatoryItem[]>`.
  3. Each item has `regulator='FINRA'` and required fields: integration test loops items asserting `item.regulator === "FINRA"`, `item.sourceUrl` matches /^https?:\/\//, `item.publicationDate` is a valid Date, `item.documentType.length > 0`, `item.title.length > 0`, `item.fullText.length > 0`.
  4. Parser handles network errors gracefully: 4 fall-back paths exercised -- thrown error (ECONNREFUSED), HTTP 503, empty feed, abort/timeout. None throw out of `fetchLatest`; all return the cached fixture.
- Test suite results: `npm test` -> 20 suites / 169 tests passing (was 18 / 153; +2 suites / +16 tests for INGEST-002 -- 11 unit + 5 integration). Stable at ~20s.
- Regression: `npx tsc --noEmit` -> zero errors; `curl /` -> 200; `curl /api/health` -> 200; `curl /alerts` -> 200; `curl /ingestion` -> 200. All 18 pre-existing test suites unchanged. CORPUS-001..010 / SEED-001 / EMBED-001..002 / VECTORS-001 / RETRIEVE-001 / LLM-001..002 / CLASSIFY-001..002 / CITE-001 / SCORE-001 / PIPE-001..002 / INGEST-001 unchanged.
- No Playwright verification: INGEST-002 has no UI surface (backend module called from the future ingestion pipeline). Browser verification will land with the dashboard's "Trigger Ingestion" button (DASH-002) or the trigger endpoint (API-011), whichever lands first.

### Blockers / Issues
- The FINRA RSS URL `https://www.finra.org/rules-guidance/notices/rss` is the documented endpoint per FINRA's public site, but at implementation time was not network-verified -- the integration test mocks `global.fetch` and the cache fall-back covers offline / wrong-URL cases. If the live URL has changed (e.g., FINRA migrated the feed), `fetchLatest` will degrade to cache and emit a warning -- production deployment should re-verify and update `FINRA_RSS_URL` if needed. The single-line constant edit makes this trivial.
- Decision: documentType = "regulatory_notice" as a raw string. The normalized `DocumentType` union includes "notice" -- normalization at the persistence layer (INGEST-006 territory) will collapse "regulatory_notice" / "press_release" / "bulletin" / etc. into the canonical union. Surfacing the raw vendor-side label preserves the discriminator for normalization logic.
- Decision: all six helpers (`extractTag`, `decodeEntities`, `stripHtml`, `fetchRss`, `loadCache`, `ITEM_BLOCK_RE`) are duplicated byte-for-byte from `sec.ts`. This is intentional code duplication, not an oversight -- per the Session 25..31 rule of thumb, extraction happens at the third caller. Leaving the duplication visible and obvious lets the future extractor see the full pattern in two places.
- Decision: the two cache fixtures cover complementary domains (complaint handling under Rule 4530; generative AI guidance touching info-security and vendor-management). Intentional spread so the eventual end-to-end pipeline test (INGEST-006 + drift detection) has a non-trivial set of policy domains to retrieve against -- a single-domain fixture would only exercise one chunk's similarity path.
- Did NOT add `.gitkeep` files in the FINRA cache directory. The directory is created by `mkdir -p` when the cache is written; with the JSON file present, git tracks the directory naturally.
- Did NOT alter `src/types/index.ts`. The `RawRegulatoryItem` interface added in Session 31 is reused as-is; no FINRA-specific type was needed.

### Next Priorities
- INGEST-005 (priority 35): HTTP fetcher utility (`src/lib/ingestion/fetcher.ts`). Now that two parsers (SEC + FINRA) duplicate the same `fetchRss` shape with timeout + UA + non-2xx-throws, INGEST-005 is overdue for promotion. CFPB (INGEST-003) and OCC (INGEST-004) would be the third and fourth callers -- promoting before them would be cleanest. Target API: `fetchUrl(url, opts) -> Promise<{ ok: true, body: string } | { ok: false, error: string }>` per the spec's "returns a failure result instead of throwing" requirement.
- INGEST-003 (priority 33): CFPB parser. Same RSS shape; the candidate URL `https://files.consumerfinance.gov/f/feeds/cfpb_publications.xml` needs verification at implementation time. If implemented after INGEST-005, this parser would be the first user of the shared fetcher.
- INGEST-004 (priority 34): OCC parser. RSS feed candidate: `https://www.occ.gov/rss/occ_alert.xml`. Same shape.
- INGEST-006 (priority 36): pipeline orchestrator -- entry point that calls all four parsers, deduplicates by sourceUrl, persists new items, runs `runDriftDetection` on each. Save until at least three of INGEST-001..005 land.

### Blockers / Issues
- The CFPB RSS URL `https://www.consumerfinance.gov/about-us/newsroom/feed/` is the standard WordPress-style newsroom RSS endpoint per CFPB's public site, but at implementation time was not network-verified -- the integration test mocks `global.fetch` and the cache fall-back covers offline / wrong-URL cases. If the live URL has changed (e.g., CFPB migrated the feed location), `fetchLatest` will degrade to cache and emit a warning -- production deployment should re-verify and update `CFPB_RSS_URL` if needed. The single-line constant edit makes this trivial.
- Decision: documentType = "publication" as a raw string (not "press_release", which the SEC parser uses, nor "regulatory_notice", which FINRA uses). The CFPB newsroom feed mixes circulars, final rules, enforcement announcements, blog posts, and press releases -- "publication" is the broadest accurate label for the vendor-side type. The normalized `DocumentType` union (final_rule | proposed_rule | enforcement | bulletin | notice | guidance | letter) will need the persistence layer (INGEST-006 territory) to do title/description-based classification, since the feed itself doesn't carry the type discriminator. Surfacing "publication" preserves the "needs normalization" signal without forcing the parser to guess.
- Decision: all six helpers (`extractTag`, `decodeEntities`, `stripHtml`, `fetchRss`, `loadCache`, `ITEM_BLOCK_RE`) are duplicated byte-for-byte from `sec.ts` / `finra.ts`. This is now THREE byte-identical copies. Per the Session 25..32 promotion-threshold rule, the third caller is the trigger -- INGEST-005 is the next session and will extract the duplication. Leaving this session's diff focused on CFPB rather than bundling the extraction keeps the commit boundary clean.
- Decision: the two cache fixtures cover complementary domains (fair lending under ECOA/Reg B; consumer protection / disclosures under TILA/Reg Z) -- intentional domain spread so the eventual end-to-end drift-detection pipeline test has more than one policy domain to exercise. Single-domain fixtures would only test one chunk's similarity path.

- Did NOT alter `src/types/index.ts`. The `RawRegulatoryItem` interface added in Session 31 is reused as-is; no CFPB-specific type was needed. (If at some point we discover that CFPB items carry a discriminating field that the other regulators don't -- e.g., a category enum from a JSON-API endpoint -- a CFPB-specific raw type might be warranted, but the RSS-based fetcher matches the shared shape.)

With THREE byte-identical `fetchRss` helpers in sec.ts / finra.ts / cfpb.ts, INGEST-005 is now overdue per the established threshold rule. Target API per app_spec §6: `fetchUrl(url, opts) -> Promise<{ ok: true, body: string } | { ok: false, error: string }>` (returns a failure result instead of throwing). ## Session 35 -- HTTP Fetcher Utility
Date: 2026-05-05

### Feature Worked On
- INGEST-005: shared HTTP fetcher utility at `src/lib/ingestion/fetcher.ts`. Exposes `fetchUrl(url, opts)` returning a discriminated `{ ok: true, body, status } | { ok: false, error }` result -- never throws. Centralizes the timeout / User-Agent / Accept / abort-handling that previously lived as four byte-identical `fetchRss` helpers across the SEC / FINRA / CFPB / OCC parsers (the duplication trigger flagged in Sessions 32, 33, and 34). All four parsers were refactored to consume the shared fetcher.
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Wrote `src/lib/ingestion/fetcher.ts` (84 lines): exports `fetchUrl`, the `FetchResult` / `FetchSuccess` / `FetchFailure` types, the `FetchUrlOptions` interface, and the `DEFAULT_FETCH_TIMEOUT_MS` (10s) / `DEFAULT_USER_AGENT` ("Tether Compliance Demo dev@tether.local") / `DEFAULT_ACCEPT` ("application/rss+xml, application/xml;q=0.9, */*;q=0.5") constants. The function uses an internal `AbortController` for the timeout and additionally honors a caller-supplied `signal` (forwards external cancellation to the internal controller). Non-2xx responses produce `{ ok: false, error: "HTTP <status> <statusText> for <url>" }`; thrown fetch errors produce `{ ok: false, error: "fetch failed for <url>: <message>" }`; abort/timeout produces `{ ok: false, error: "request timed out after <Nms> for <url>" }`. Every failure path also `console.warn`s with the same string under a `[fetcher.fetchUrl]` prefix so the URL appears in the logs without the caller having to re-emit it.
- Refactored all four parsers (`sec.ts`, `finra.ts`, `cfpb.ts`, `occ.ts`) to import `fetchUrl` from the shared module and drop their per-file `fetchRss`, `<REGULATOR>_USER_AGENT`, and inline `AbortController` plumbing. Each parser shrank by ~22 lines net (~30 lines removed for the deleted helper, ~8 lines added for the new `if (result.ok) ... else ...` branch shape). The branch became: `const result = await fetchUrl(URL, { timeoutMs }); if (result.ok) { parse + early return on success; warn on zero items } else { warn that live failed }; try cache fall-back`. The `decodeEntities` / `stripHtml` / `extractTag` / `parseXxxRss` / `rssItemToRaw` / `loadCache` helpers were left in place per-parser -- INGEST-005's scope is the HTTP transport only, not the RSS-shape extractor (the per-regulator `documentType` constant + the `<Regulator>RssItem` typed interface still legitimately differ per parser). A dedicated RSS-extractor extraction is a future option but not in this feature's spec.
- Authored `__tests__/unit/fetcher.test.ts` (1 test, 22 lines) verifying the constants ship with sane defaults that callers can rely on (10s timeout, contact-bearing User-Agent, RSS-preferred Accept that doesn't 406 against type-stripping CDNs).
- Authored `__tests__/integration/fetcher.test.ts` (9 tests, 219 lines) covering: (a) successful 200 returns body+status; (b) default UA + Accept headers are sent; (c) caller can override `userAgent` and merge extra `headers` (e.g., `X-Trace-Id`); (d) thrown `fetch` (ECONNREFUSED) -> `{ ok: false }` with URL+message in error; (e) HTTP 503 -> `{ ok: false }` with status+statusText+URL in error; (f) HTTP 404 -> `{ ok: false }` with the URL embedded; (g) explicit `timeoutMs: 50` -> abort fires at 50ms with "timed out after 50ms" error; (h) default `timeoutMs` -> aborts at 10000ms; (i) externally supplied `AbortSignal` aborts the in-flight fetch. The 9 cases collectively exercise INGEST-005 acceptance steps 2 (bad-URL returns error not throw), 3 (valid URL returns content), and 4 (URL-embedded error logging).
- Behavioural decision: kept TWO log lines on the failure path (one from the fetcher with the "[fetcher.fetchUrl]" prefix, one from the parser with the "[regulator.fetchLatest]" prefix announcing the cache fall-back). Justification: they serve distinct observability purposes -- the fetcher log is per-request-attempt context (HTTP-level), the parser log is per-source-failure context (cache-fall-back signal). Collapsing to one would lose either the URL+http-error in the fetcher logs or the "falling back to cache" event in the parser logs. The pre-existing per-parser integration tests assert `warnings.some((w) => w.includes(URL))` and `warnings.some((w) => w.includes("ECONNREFUSED"))` -- both remain satisfied (the fetcher warning carries both pieces of context).
- Behavioural decision: detect AbortError via `err.name === "AbortError" || /aborted/i.test(message)` rather than `instanceof Error`. The Node 22+ runtime in this WSL environment surfaces aborts as `DOMException("aborted", "AbortError")`, which doesn't pass `instanceof Error`. The first iteration of the test suite caught this with two failures ("AbortError: aborted" leaking as the literal error message); the name+message check fixed both without regressing the other paths.
- Behavioural decision: kept the per-parser `XXX_FETCH_TIMEOUT_MS` / `XXX_RSS_URL` constants exported. They're still the right knob for per-regulator tuning (e.g., the OCC's news-release feed could later get a longer timeout if it proves slower than the others) and the existing integration tests import `XXX_RSS_URL` to assert against. Not a regression to keep them; they're now the single thing each parser passes into the shared fetcher.
- Did NOT extract the RSS-extractor helpers (`decodeEntities` / `stripHtml` / `extractTag` / `ITEM_BLOCK_RE`). They are a separate axis of duplication from the HTTP transport (parsing logic, not network logic). INGEST-005's spec text and verification steps speak only to the HTTP transport. A follow-up extraction could land if a fifth regulator with the same RSS shape arrives, or if INGEST-006 wants a single `parseGenericRss` -- not in scope here.
- Did NOT alter `src/types/index.ts` -- the new `FetchResult` / `FetchSuccess` / `FetchFailure` types live in the fetcher module itself (only its callers need them; not part of the broader app type surface).

- Verified all 4 INGEST-005 acceptance steps:
  1. `src/lib/ingestion/fetcher.ts` exists: confirmed by `import { fetchUrl, ... } from "@/lib/ingestion/fetcher"` in the test files (compiles + runs).
  2. Calling the fetcher with a known-bad URL returns an error result, not throws: integration tests "returns ok=false (does not throw) when the underlying fetch throws" (ECONNREFUSED), "returns ok=false on non-2xx HTTP responses" (503), "returns ok=false on 404" (404), and "aborts a hung request and returns a timeout error" all assert `result.ok === false` without an `expect(...).rejects` -- a thrown error from `fetchUrl` would surface as an unhandled rejection in jest and fail the test suite, so the absence of throws is part of the green-bar contract.
  3. Calling the fetcher with a valid URL returns the content: integration test "returns ok=true with the body when the underlying fetch succeeds" asserts `result.body === "hello world"` and `result.status === 200`.
  4. Errors are logged with context about which URL failed: integration test "returns ok=false (does not throw) when the underlying fetch throws" asserts `warnings.some((w) => w.includes("bad.example.test"))`. The other failure-path tests also embed the URL in the asserted error message (`error: "...for https://example.test/missing.xml"`), which exercises the URL-in-error contract by inspection.

Pre-flight regression check on `(sec|finra|cfpb|occ)` patterns -> 8 suites / 64 tests all passing before any new code was written; same 8 suites / 64 tests still passing after the refactor.

### Blockers / Issues
- The Node-runtime AbortError-detection issue (DOMException not passing `instanceof Error`) is a real footgun if any future caller writes their own catch-and-classify logic on `fetchUrl`'s callers. The fetcher hides it from them by translating to a stable `FetchResult.error` string, but anyone bypassing the fetcher to call `fetch()` directly will have to handle the same case. Documented in fetcher.ts source (the catch-block comment).
- The user-agent string still embeds a placeholder email (`dev@tether.local`). Production deployment should swap to a real contact mailbox; the constant is exported (`DEFAULT_USER_AGENT`) so an env-var override would be a one-line change. Out of scope for INGEST-005 (which speaks to the transport contract, not deployment-specific values).
- The fetcher logs every failure as a warning with the full URL in the string. If a malicious upstream URL could ever appear in the demo (e.g., from user-supplied input flowing into the ingestion layer), the URL string would land in warning logs verbatim. For phase 1 the URLs are constants in the parser modules, so this isn't a current concern -- but if INGEST-006 ever ingests user-supplied feed URLs, the fetcher's logging would need URL sanitization.
- Did NOT add a retry mechanism. `app_spec §12` mentions "API timeout -> retry once with exponential backoff" but that's specifically for the LLM error path, not the regulator-fetch path. The regulator path's spec is explicit: "404 / timeout from regulator site -> log error, continue with other sources". So fetchUrl returns a single failure result; the orchestrator (INGEST-006) can decide whether to retry, and the cache fall-back inside each parser already covers the most common failure modes for the demo.

### Next Priorities
- INGEST-006 (priority 36): pipeline orchestrator (`src/lib/ingestion/pipeline.ts:runIngestion`). All four parsers and the shared fetcher are now in place; the orchestrator is the natural next session. Entry point that calls all four parsers in parallel (with `Promise.allSettled` so a single parser failure doesn't bring down the run -- this is the failed-isolation contract that INGEST-007 separately verifies), deduplicates by `sourceUrl`, persists new items into `RegulatoryItem`, runs `runDriftDetection` on each, and finalizes the `IngestionRun` record (status transitions: `running` -> `completed` / `failed`; updates `itemsProcessed`, `itemsCreated`, `itemsSuppressed`, `errors`). The persistence step also needs to normalize the raw `documentType` strings ("press_release" / "regulatory_notice" / "publication" / "bulletin") into the canonical `DocumentType` union ("final_rule" | "proposed_rule" | "enforcement" | "bulletin" | "notice" | "guidance" | "letter") -- title/keyword classification is the natural mechanism. Larger session (multi-step orchestration + persistence + status state-machine).
- INGEST-007 (priority 37): failed-run isolation. The acceptance criteria assume INGEST-006 has landed (you trigger an ingestion run that fails, then a second run that should still execute). Likely a small session if INGEST-006 is implemented with status-machine cleanup that doesn't leave stale "running" rows behind on parser failures.
- API-011 (priority 47): `POST /api/ingestion/trigger` endpoint. The HTTP entry point that invokes the orchestrator. Naturally pairs with INGEST-006 -- one provides the function, the other the route. Could be a single session if both stay tightly scoped.
- Optional follow-up extraction: the `decodeEntities` / `stripHtml` / `extractTag` / `parseXxxRss` / `loadCache` helpers are still byte-identical across the four parsers (only the typed `XxxRssItem` interface, the regulator string, and the documentType constant differ). If INGEST-006 needs a `parseGenericRss(xml, regulator, documentType)` factory, this would be the trigger to extract them into `src/lib/ingestion/parsers/rss.ts` -- but it isn't blocking INGEST-006 itself.


## Session 36 -- Ingestion Pipeline Orchestrator
Date: 2026-05-05

### Feature Worked On
- INGEST-006: `runIngestion()` in `src/lib/ingestion/pipeline.ts` -- single entry point that drives a full ingestion run end to end. Creates an IngestionRun row with status='running', calls all four parsers in parallel via `Promise.allSettled` (so one parser failure doesn't bring down the run -- the failed-isolation contract that INGEST-007 separately verifies), deduplicates by sourceUrl (in-batch + cross-run), persists new RegulatoryItems with their raw vendor-side documentType normalized into the canonical DocumentType union, runs `runDriftDetection` per new item (each call wrapped in try/catch so a single drift-detection blow-up doesn't stop the run), and finalizes the run row (`status='completed'`, `completedAt=now`, `itemsProcessed=count`, `errors=JSON{parserErrors,driftErrors}` or null). Returns an `IngestionRunResult` summary so callers (API routes, tests) can assert what happened without re-querying.
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Replaced the 7-line `pipeline.ts` stub (`runIngestionPipeline` -- never imported anywhere; verified by grep before deleting) with a 211-line implementation. Public surface: `runIngestion(options?: RunIngestionOptions): Promise<IngestionRunResult>`, `normalizeDocumentType(raw): DocumentType`, plus the `ParserError` / `DriftError` / `IngestionRunResult` / `RunIngestionOptions` types. The `RunIngestionOptions.parsers` field is an explicit test seam -- lets integration tests inject mock parsers without having to `jest.unstable_mockModule` four separate parser modules.
- Implemented `normalizeDocumentType(raw)` -- title/keyword classifier that maps the four raw vendor-side labels ("press_release" / "regulatory_notice" / "publication" / "bulletin") into the canonical `DocumentType` union ("final_rule" | "proposed_rule" | "enforcement" | "bulletin" | "notice" | "guidance" | "letter"). Patterns are ordered most-specific to least-specific so "Final Rule on X" wins over a stray "rule" mention later in the body. Falls back to a per-regulator default when no signal is present (SEC -> enforcement, FINRA -> notice, CFPB -> guidance, OCC -> bulletin). Verified against all 8 cache fixture titles (SEC enforcement results -> enforcement; SEC charges adviser -> enforcement; FINRA reminds member firms -> notice via fallback; FINRA provides guidance -> guidance; CFPB issues circular -> guidance; CFPB finalizes rule -> final_rule via the `\bfinal(?:iz(?:e|es|ed|ing))?\s+rule\b` pattern; OCC bulletin 2025-3 -> bulletin; OCC bulletin 2025-7 -> bulletin).
- Dedupe is two-pass: an in-batch pass with a `Set<sourceUrl>` walks the collected items, then a single `prisma.regulatoryItem.findMany({ where: { sourceUrl: { in: [...] } } })` checks the persisted set. Items already in the DB are skipped, items duplicated within the batch are skipped, and the count of each is rolled into `result.duplicatesSkipped` (sum of in-batch + cross-run).
- Per-item drift detection is awaited sequentially (not `Promise.all`) so the per-alert `prisma.$transaction` calls in detector.ts don't race on SQLite. The orchestrator does NOT increment `itemsFlagged` / `itemsSuppressed` itself -- the detector already increments those counters on the run referenced by `regItem.ingestionRunId`. The orchestrator just reads them back via the final `prisma.ingestionRun.update` and surfaces them in the result.
- Top-level error path: if any unexpected throw escapes the parser/persist/drift loops (e.g., DB connectivity failure during the initial `create`), the run row gets updated to `status='failed'` with the error captured in the `errors` blob and the function returns an `IngestionRunResult` with `status: "failed"` (rather than re-throwing). This keeps the API route's contract simple -- a 200 with status='failed' instead of a 500.
- Authored `__tests__/unit/pipeline.test.ts` (12 tests) covering `normalizeDocumentType`: each canonical mapping (final_rule / proposed_rule / enforcement / guidance / bulletin), each per-regulator fallback (SEC->enforcement / FINRA->notice / CFPB->guidance / OCC->bulletin), and the "Finalizes Rule" edge case (CFPB cache fixture title that nearly fails the naive `\bfinal rule\b` regex; the broader `\bfinal(?:iz...)?\s+rule\b` catches it).
- Authored `__tests__/integration/pipeline.test.ts` (4 tests) covering `runIngestion` end to end against the seeded SQLite database, with `runDriftDetection` mocked via `jest.unstable_mockModule` so the suite doesn't need OPENAI/ANTHROPIC keys. Cases: (a) happy path -- 4 mock parsers return 5 items, all persist, IngestionRun status transitions running -> completed (verified by querying the DB inside the SEC parser's fetch callback before any item is persisted; that mid-flight read sees status='running'), drift detection driven exactly once per persisted item, documentType normalization reflected in the persisted rows; (b) deduplication -- a pre-existing item with sourceUrl X plus an in-batch duplicate (FINRA + CFPB return the same URL) yields itemsProcessed=2 and duplicatesSkipped=2; (c) failed-isolation -- SEC parser rejects, FINRA/CFPB/OCC succeed, run completes with itemsProcessed=3 and the SEC error embedded in `errors` JSON; (d) drift-isolation -- first drift call throws, second succeeds; both items are still persisted; result.driftErrors carries the one failure.
- Decision: did NOT pre-throw a fresh prisma RegulatoryItem dedupe constraint at the schema level. The dedupe is enforced in application code at the moment because (a) the schema doesn't have a unique index on sourceUrl, and adding one is a separate session-worthy schema migration (the seed data may already have duplicates per regulator across runs depending on test ordering), (b) per app_spec §6 dedupe is explicitly a parser/orchestrator concern. If a future session wants to harden this against race conditions between concurrent ingestion runs, the right move is to add `@unique` on `RegulatoryItem.sourceUrl` and let `findMany` -> `create` race become `create` -> `catch P2002`. Out of scope for INGEST-006.
- Decision: did NOT promote the four `fetchLatest` imports into a registry table. The current four-element array is the simplest possible structure and tests can swap the entire array via `RunIngestionOptions.parsers`. A registry table would make sense if the parser count were dynamic or driven by config, but it isn't.
- Decision: did NOT add a setInterval or cron loop. Per app_spec §6 the MVP scheduler is explicitly a stub; production scheduling is an external concern. The orchestrator is invoked exclusively via `POST /api/ingestion/trigger` (next session: API-011) or directly from tests.

### Files Modified / Created
- src/lib/ingestion/pipeline.ts (replaced 7-line stub with 211-line implementation)
- __tests__/unit/pipeline.test.ts (new, 12 tests)
- __tests__/integration/pipeline.test.ts (new, 4 tests)
- specs/phase1/feature_list.json (INGEST-006 passes -> true)

### Testing
- Verified all 6 INGEST-006 acceptance steps:
  1. `src/lib/ingestion/pipeline.ts` exports `runIngestion`: confirmed by `import { runIngestion } from "@/lib/ingestion/pipeline"` in the integration test (compiles + runs).
  2. Calling `runIngestion({ trigger: "manual" })` resolves: integration test "creates an IngestionRun, persists new items, and finalizes status='completed'" calls it with `trigger: "manual"` and asserts on the result.
  3. IngestionRun is created with status='running' then updated to 'completed': verified by the SEC parser fetch callback querying `prisma.ingestionRun.findMany({ orderBy: { startedAt: 'desc' }, take: 1 })` mid-fetch and asserting `status === "running"`; the post-run query asserts `finalRun.status === "completed"` and `completedAt !== null`.
  4. `itemsProcessed` matches new-item count: integration tests assert `result.itemsProcessed === 5` (happy path), `=== 2` (dedupe path), `=== 3` (failed-isolation path), and the post-run DB query `finalRun.itemsProcessed` matches.
  5. Duplicate sourceUrls are skipped: dedupe-path test pre-seeds an item with sourceUrl X, parsers return that same URL plus an in-batch duplicate across FINRA/CFPB; result.itemsProcessed=2 (the brand-new SEC item + one shared item), result.duplicatesSkipped=2 (one cross-run + one in-batch), and the persisted rows include only the two new sourceUrls (the old item still belongs to the prior run, not the new one).
  6. Run completes even if one parser fails: failed-isolation test has the SEC parser throw `new Error("simulated SEC parser network failure")`; result.status='completed', itemsProcessed=3 (FINRA/CFPB/OCC items), parserErrors carries `{ regulator: "SEC", error: "simulated SEC parser network failure" }`, and `JSON.parse(finalRun.errors).parserErrors` matches.

All 26 pre-existing test suites unchanged. CORPUS-001..010 / SEED-001 / EMBED-001..002 / VECTORS-001 / RETRIEVE-001 / LLM-001..002 / CLASSIFY-001..002 / CITE-001 / SCORE-001 / PIPE-001..002 / INGEST-001..005 unchanged.
- No Playwright verification: INGEST-006 has no UI surface (backend orchestrator). Browser verification will land with the dashboard's "Trigger Ingestion" button (DASH-002) or the trigger endpoint (API-011), whichever lands first.

### Blockers / Issues
- The dedupe is application-side, not schema-side. Two concurrent calls to `runIngestion` could race -- both see no existing row for sourceUrl X, both insert. For the MVP demo (single-button-press triggers, single-tenant SQLite) this is fine; production hardening would add `@unique` on `RegulatoryItem.sourceUrl` and convert the dedupe to a `create` -> `catch P2002` pattern. Documented in the source comment.
- The orchestrator returns `{ status: "failed", ... }` rather than throwing on a top-level catch. This was a deliberate API-stability choice (the API-011 route can render a 200 with the failure body instead of a 500 plus partial state) but it diverges slightly from the literal app_spec §12 rule "log error, continue". If a future caller wants throw-on-failure semantics, they can wrap and re-throw based on `result.status`. The IngestionRun row is still persisted with `status='failed'`, so the failure is observable in the DB regardless.
- The `documentType` normalization is keyword-based, not LLM-classified. App_spec §3 lists the canonical types but doesn't specify how to derive them from the raw vendor labels. The current regex map covers the 8 cache fixture titles correctly, but real production traffic could surface titles that fall through to the per-regulator default and end up mis-typed (e.g., an SEC press release announcing a final rule could end up tagged "enforcement" if the title doesn't say "rule"). A future hardening session could add an LLM-backed fallback in the normalize step, OR move the classification to the relevance/drift LLM call (which already sees the full title + body) and have the orchestrator just persist the LLM's verdict. Not blocking INGEST-006 acceptance.
- Did NOT extract the per-parser RSS-shape helpers (`decodeEntities` / `stripHtml` / `extractTag` / `parseXxxRss` / `loadCache` -- the byte-identical-across-four-parsers code flagged in Sessions 32..35). The orchestrator composes against `fetchLatest()` only; the RSS-extraction layer is internal to each parser. Bundling the extraction into this session would dilute the per-feature commit boundary again. The trigger remains a fifth regulator with the same RSS shape, OR a session that explicitly targets the RSS-extractor extraction.
