- INGEST-007 (priority 37): failed-run isolation. The orchestrator already implements this contract (one parser failing doesn't stop the others; a top-level throw produces a `status='failed'` row rather than poisoning the next run). The dedicated INGEST-007 test should verify "trigger run A which fails, then trigger run B; run B executes and is independent of A." Likely a small session -- mostly an integration test that pre-creates a run with status='failed', then calls runIngestion again and asserts the new run is independent. May not need any new code in pipeline.ts at all.
- API-011 (priority 47): `POST /api/ingestion/trigger` endpoint. The HTTP entry point that invokes `runIngestion`. Body: `{ url?: string }` (optional URL hook isn't implemented yet -- can be deferred or wired in this session). Response: `{ runId: string, status: "started" }`. Side effect: starts ingestion asynchronously (per app_spec §4). Pairs naturally with INGEST-006 -- one provides the function, the other the route.
- API-002 (priority 38): dashboard stats endpoint -- alert counts by severity / regulator / domain / status, plus recent IngestionRun list. Independent of INGEST-007 / API-011; could be done in parallel.
- Optional schema hardening: add `@unique` on `RegulatoryItem.sourceUrl` so the dedupe race is handled at the DB layer. Single-line schema change + migration; would let the orchestrator drop the explicit `findMany` lookup and use `create` -> `catch P2002` instead. Defer until a concrete need (concurrent ingestion runs) materializes.

## Session 37 -- Failed-Run Isolation
Date: 2026-05-05

### Feature Worked On
- INGEST-007: a failed ingestion run does not block subsequent runs from executing. Verifies the run-state machine is per-call, with no shared mutable state between invocations of `runIngestion()`. After a run that fails (every parser-fetch errors out, run row finalized with `status='failed'`), the next call to `runIngestion()` creates a fresh IngestionRun row, executes its parsers/persist/drift loops independently, and finalizes with `status='completed'`. The two runs share no items, no errors, and no counter state -- the failed run remains failed after the second run finishes.
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Refined `src/lib/ingestion/pipeline.ts`: introduced a `parserFetchFailures` counter and a final-status decision (`finalStatus = parserFetchFailures === parsers.length ? "failed" : "completed"`). A run where 100% of parsers' fetches reject is now persisted as `status='failed'` with the per-regulator errors captured in the `errors` JSON blob; partial failures (1..n-1 of n parsers fail) keep `status='completed'` per the existing failed-isolation contract. The `IngestionRunResult.status` returned to the caller mirrors the persisted state so API/test callers don't need to re-query the DB. Single targeted modification (~12 lines added including comment); no other behavior changed.
- Authored `__tests__/integration/pipeline-isolation.test.ts` (200 lines, 2 tests):
  1. "a run with all parsers failing is marked 'failed' with error details, and a subsequent run still executes independently": injects four `failingFetch(regulator)` parsers (each throws `simulated <REGULATOR> failure for run A`) and asserts result.status='failed', result.itemsProcessed=0, all four parserErrors recorded. Reads the persisted IngestionRun row and confirms status='failed', errors blob is non-null, and `JSON.parse(errors).parserErrors` lists all four regulators. Verifies `mockRunDriftDetection` was not called (nothing to detect drift on). Then drives a second `runIngestion()` with one SEC item and three empty parsers -- asserts result.runId !== runA.runId, status='completed', itemsProcessed=1, no parserErrors, no driftErrors. Reads persisted state for both runs and confirms run B's lone item belongs to run B's ingestionRunId (not run A's), drift detection ran exactly once (with run B's item id), and run A's status is still 'failed' (untouched by run B's success).
  2. "partial-failure runs (some parsers fail) remain status='completed' -- only ALL-failed flips to 'failed'": regression guard ensuring the new status refinement does not collapse the existing partial-failure-is-completed contract from INGEST-006. SEC/CFPB/OCC fail; FINRA succeeds with one item. Result: status='completed', itemsProcessed=1, parserErrors.length=3. Persisted run has status='completed' with errors blob populated.
- Decision: housed the new test in a dedicated file (`pipeline-isolation.test.ts`) rather than appending to `pipeline.test.ts`. The existing `pipeline.test.ts` file is the INGEST-006 contract test and is already 305 lines; INGEST-007 is its own feature with its own commit boundary, so a separate file keeps the per-feature scope crisp and makes the git log readable. The shared boilerplate (mockRunDriftDetection seam, TEST_TAG cleanup, makeRaw factory) is duplicated rather than extracted -- two integration test files is below the threshold where a shared `__tests__/integration/_helpers.ts` extraction would be worth the cross-file change. If a third integration test file with the same pattern lands, that's the natural extraction trigger.
- Decision: kept `parserFetchFailures` as a separate counter from `parserErrors.length` because `parserErrors` also accumulates persistence failures (the `try { prisma.regulatoryItem.create } catch` block at pipeline.ts:141-150). Conflating them would cause edge cases where (a) all parsers succeed but every persist call fails, or (b) some parsers fail and others succeed-but-fail-to-persist, to incorrectly flip status to 'failed'. The literal contract is "every fetch failed", which is exactly what `parserFetchFailures === parsers.length` measures.
- Decision: did NOT modify the top-level catch path. A genuine top-level throw (e.g., DB connectivity failure during the initial `prisma.ingestionRun.create`) still produces `status='failed'` via the existing top-level handler at pipeline.ts:190-214. The new all-parsers-failed branch is additive: it covers the case where the orchestrator runs to completion but every source was unreachable. Both paths produce the same status='failed' shape; callers can't tell which branch fired without inspecting the errors blob (top-level errors carry a `topLevel` field; per-parser errors don't).
- Decision: did NOT add a regression test that drives a top-level orchestrator throw (e.g., mocking `prisma.ingestionRun.create` to throw on the first call). The path is already covered by code inspection -- the catch block on line 190-214 is unchanged from Session 36, which had its own coverage notes -- and adding a prisma-internals mock would be brittle and high-maintenance. The all-parsers-failed test exercises the more realistic failure mode (network outage of every regulator) and a top-level throw is the same status='failed' state machine outcome by inspection.
- Did NOT add an isolation cleanup step (e.g., a defensive query that resets stale `status='running'` rows on startup). The current per-call state machine never leaves a row in 'running' once `runIngestion` returns -- both the success branch and the catch branch transition to a terminal state ('completed' or 'failed'). A stale 'running' row would only appear if the Node process crashed mid-run, which is out of scope for INGEST-007.

### Files Modified / Created
- src/lib/ingestion/pipeline.ts (+12 lines: parserFetchFailures counter, finalStatus decision, comment)
- __tests__/integration/pipeline-isolation.test.ts (new, 200 lines, 2 tests)
- specs/phase1/feature_list.json (INGEST-007 passes -> true)

### Testing
- Verified all 4 INGEST-007 acceptance steps:
  1. Trigger an ingestion run that fails: case (1) injects four failing parsers; result.status='failed' (asserted on the returned object).
  2. Verify the run is marked as 'failed' with error details: case (1) reads the persisted IngestionRun row, asserts `status === 'failed'`, `completedAt !== null`, and `JSON.parse(errors).parserErrors` lists all four regulator names with their error messages. Error details are visibly captured.
  3. Trigger another ingestion run immediately after: case (1) calls `runIngestion()` a second time without any teardown between calls (no `afterEach` runs between the two calls within a single `it` block).
  4. Verify the second run starts and completes independently: case (1) asserts runB.runId !== runA.runId, runB.status='completed', runB.itemsProcessed=1, runB.parserErrors=[], persistence rows of run B carry runB.runId only, drift detection was driven exactly once (for run B's item, not for any phantom run A items), and reading run A's row again shows it is still status='failed' (the second run did not roll back or modify the first run's state).
- Test suite results: `npm test` -> 29 suites / 229 tests passing (was 28 / 227; +1 suite / +2 tests for INGEST-007). Stable at ~26s.
- Pipeline-only run: `npm test -- --testPathPatterns=pipeline` -> 3 suites / 18 tests passing (was 2 / 16). The new isolation suite runs alongside the existing INGEST-006 pipeline tests.
- Regression: `npx tsc --noEmit` -> zero errors. `curl /` -> 200; `curl /api/health` -> 200. CORPUS-001..010 / SEED-001 / EMBED-001..002 / VECTORS-001 / RETRIEVE-001 / LLM-001..002 / CLASSIFY-001..002 / CITE-001 / SCORE-001 / PIPE-001..002 / INGEST-001..006 unchanged. The pre-existing INGEST-006 partial-failure test ("completes the run even when one parser throws") still passes because partial failures still produce status='completed' (the new `parserFetchFailures === parsers.length` branch only fires for total failure).
- No Playwright verification: INGEST-007 has no UI surface (backend orchestrator state-machine contract). Browser verification will land with the dashboard's "Trigger Ingestion" button (DASH-002) or the trigger endpoint (API-011), whichever lands first.

### Blockers / Issues
- The literal app_spec rule "(e.g., all parsers return errors) -> mark as 'failed'" wasn't satisfied by the orchestrator from Session 36 -- INGEST-006 marked all-parsers-failed runs as `status='completed'` with errors logged, on the rationale that parser-level errors are isolated and don't bubble to run-level failure. INGEST-007's verification step explicitly required `status='failed'`, which surfaced the inconsistency. Resolution: refined the orchestrator (the small `parserFetchFailures` branch) so total failure flips status to 'failed' while preserving the partial-failure-is-completed contract for the 1..n-1 of n case. This is a semantic refinement, not a regression -- the new branch is strictly additive.
- The two integration test files (`pipeline.test.ts` and `pipeline-isolation.test.ts`) duplicate the mockRunDriftDetection/jest.unstable_mockModule/TEST_TAG/makeRaw boilerplate. Per the established threshold rule, two callers is below the duplication-extraction threshold (the rule has been "third caller is the trigger" throughout this codebase: SEC/FINRA/CFPB/OCC parsers triggered fetcher.ts at four callers; INGEST-005 documented the wait). A future third pipeline integration test file (or a third integration test file in general) would be the natural trigger to extract the shared seam into `__tests__/integration/_helpers.ts`.
- Did NOT add a unit test for the new `parserFetchFailures === parsers.length` branch. The integration test exercises the full state machine end-to-end (parsers throw -> orchestrator persists status='failed' -> caller sees result.status='failed'), which is more representative than a unit test that would have to mock prisma + the parsers separately. If pipeline.ts grew a public helper around the failure-counting logic, that would be the unit-test trigger; right now the logic is a single branch in the orchestrator and is well-covered by integration.
- The orchestrator still has no schema-side dedupe constraint (carry-over from Session 36). Two concurrent calls to `runIngestion` could still race on dedupe -- INGEST-007 doesn't address this because the spec is about temporal isolation (run A then run B), not concurrency (run A and run B simultaneously). The single-tenant SQLite demo doesn't surface this; production hardening would still want `@unique` on `RegulatoryItem.sourceUrl`.

### Next Priorities
- API-011 (priority 47): `POST /api/ingestion/trigger` endpoint. The HTTP entry point that invokes `runIngestion`. With INGEST-006 (orchestrator) and INGEST-007 (failure isolation contract) both green, this is the natural follow-up -- it gives the dashboard's "Trigger Ingestion" button a backend to call and lets the orchestrator be exercised from the UI / curl. Body: `{ url?: string }` (optional URL hook isn't implemented yet -- can be deferred or wired in this session). Response: `{ runId: string, status: "started" }`. Side effect: starts ingestion asynchronously (per app_spec §4 -- the orchestrator returns a Promise so the route can either await it inline for synchronous semantics, or fire-and-forget for async semantics; app_spec leans async). Likely a small session.
- API-002 (priority 38): dashboard stats endpoint -- alert counts by severity / regulator / domain / status, plus recent IngestionRun list. Independent of API-011; could be done in parallel. The recent-runs portion would naturally read the new IngestionRun rows that the orchestrator produces.
- API-003 (priority 39): alerts list endpoint with pagination and nested regulatory item / policy chunk summaries. Pairs naturally with the future alerts UI.
- DASH-002: "Trigger Ingestion" dashboard button. Needs API-011 first. Once both land, the full ingestion path becomes browser-testable end-to-end via Playwright (button click -> API call -> orchestrator -> persistence -> dashboard update).
- Optional schema hardening: add `@unique` on `RegulatoryItem.sourceUrl` so the dedupe race is handled at the DB layer. Single-line schema change + migration; would let the orchestrator drop the explicit `findMany` lookup and use `create` -> `catch P2002` instead. Defer until a concrete need (concurrent ingestion runs) materializes.

## Session 38 -- Dashboard Stats Endpoint
Date: 2026-05-05

### Feature Worked On
- API-002 (priority 38): GET /api/dashboard/stats -- aggregates Alert rows across severity/regulator/domain/status, plus totalOpen and recentIngestion (up to 5 most recent IngestionRun rows). Replaces the 7-line stub in src/app/api/dashboard/stats/route.ts with a live Prisma-backed implementation that returns the canonical response shape from app_spec §11.
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Replaced the stub at src/app/api/dashboard/stats/route.ts with a 95-line implementation. Single GET handler that fans out six concurrent Prisma queries via Promise.all: (1) `alert.groupBy({ by: ['severity'] })` for the severity bucket, (2) `alert.findMany({ select: { regulatoryItem: { regulator } } })` for regulator counts (groupBy doesn't traverse relations in Prisma, so we hydrate the regulator from the related RegulatoryItem and tally in JS), (3) `alert.findMany({ select: { policyChunk: { policyDocument: { domain } } } })` for domain counts (same constraint -- two relations deep), (4) `alert.groupBy({ by: ['status'] })` for status counts, (5) `alert.count({ where: { status: 'open' } })` for the dedicated totalOpen counter, (6) `ingestionRun.findMany({ orderBy: { startedAt: 'desc' }, take: 5 })` for recentIngestion.
- The response always emits the canonical severity keys (high/medium/low) and the canonical regulator keys (SEC/FINRA/CFPB/OCC) -- even when the DB has zero alerts of that bucket. Dashboard cards (DASH-001) need stable keys to render counts including zeros, so the route initializes both objects with `{ high: 0, medium: 0, low: 0 }` / `{ SEC: 0, FINRA: 0, CFPB: 0, OCC: 0 }` and overlays observed counts on top. `alertsByDomain` and `alertsByStatus` are returned as bare records (no canonicalization) since the spec uses `Record<string, number>` for those; UI consumers iterate the keys.
- A try/catch wraps the whole handler so any DB failure surfaces as `{ error, details }` with HTTP 500 (per app_spec §11 error envelope).
- Authored __tests__/integration/dashboard-stats.test.ts (2 tests, ~290 lines including a `seedAlert(spec)` helper that wires up the four required parent rows: IngestionRun -> RegulatoryItem -> PolicyDocument -> PolicyChunk -> Alert). The helper takes a flat `{ regulator, severity, domain, status }` shape and returns the created alert IDs so the afterAll cleanup can scope deletes by id (no cross-test pollution). Strategy: seed 6 alerts spanning each axis, snapshot a baseline GET response *before* seeding, then assert the post-seed response equals baseline + the seeded deltas. This makes the test robust to whatever the dev SQLite already contains (real seed data, leftover items from manual exploration) without having to nuke the DB first.
- Test 1 ("aggregates seeded alerts across severity, regulator, domain, and status") seeds 2 high/2 medium/2 low alerts split across SEC(2)/FINRA(2)/CFPB(1)/OCC(1) and 6 distinct domains (bsa_aml/complaint_handling/fair_lending/reg_e/reg_z/vendor_management) with 3 open / 1 accepted / 1 dismissed / 1 escalated. Asserts the deltas vs. the pre-seed baseline match exactly. Also asserts recentIngestion is sorted desc by startedAt, capped at 5, and each entry has the expected IngestionRun shape (id/status/trigger/itemsProcessed all present and correctly typed).
- Test 2 ("returns the canonical severity and regulator keys even when the DB is empty for those buckets") asserts the canonical-keys contract on the live response: high/medium/low and SEC/FINRA/CFPB/OCC are all present as numbers regardless of whether the DB has any rows for them. Guards the dashboard-cards-render-zeros invariant.
- Decision: did NOT use raw SQL or `prisma.$queryRaw` for the regulator and domain aggregations even though a single SQL GROUP BY would be more efficient than findMany + JS tally. The current Prisma-only path keeps the code one-tier (no SQL injection risk, no schema-name drift between TS and SQL) and the demo's alert volume is far below the threshold where the round-trip cost matters. If a future optimization session ever needs sub-100ms p99 at scale, the natural move is to convert (2) and (3) into `prisma.$queryRaw<{regulator: string; count: bigint}[]>\`SELECT regulator, COUNT(*) ... \`` -- but defer until measurement justifies it.
- Decision: did NOT add a public types module for the response shape. The route's response type is consumed by the dashboard page (DASH-001 etc.) which lives in the same Next.js app, so a shared types file would create a fan-in dependency for one consumer. When DASH-001 lands, the natural pattern is `import type { DashboardStats } from "@/app/api/dashboard/stats/route"` -- I'll export the `Stats` type at that point. For now the response shape is implicit and asserted against in the test.
- Decision: did NOT pre-compute totalOpen from the alertsByStatus count (where status='open'). Spec lists totalOpen as a discrete top-level field, and a dedicated `prisma.alert.count({ where: { status: 'open' } })` is more efficient than a JS reduction over the groupBy result (single COUNT scan vs. all-status walk). Both give the same number; the dedicated path matches the spec verbatim.

CORPUS-001..010 / SEED-001 / EMBED-001..002 / VECTORS-001 / RETRIEVE-001 / LLM-001..002 / CLASSIFY-001..002 / CITE-001 / SCORE-001 / PIPE-001..002 / INGEST-001..007 / API-001 / NAV-001..002 unchanged. ### Blockers / Issues
- The regulator and domain aggregations use `findMany` + JS tally instead of `groupBy`, because Prisma's `groupBy` doesn't traverse relations -- you can only group by columns on the model itself, and the regulator/domain fields live on related models (RegulatoryItem.regulator, PolicyDocument.domain via PolicyChunk). For the demo's alert volume this is fine; the Promise.all parallelism keeps total latency at the slowest single query. If alert counts ever reach 10k+ per page-load this becomes the bottleneck and the right fix is `prisma.$queryRaw` with a JOIN+GROUP BY.
- The test snapshots a pre-seed baseline rather than nuking the DB. This is robust to any data the dev DB already contains (real seeds, manual experiments) but it does mean a parallel-running test that creates alerts mid-way would corrupt the baseline. Jest runs test files in parallel by default; each describe block within a file is sequential, and the dashboard-stats suite is a single describe block, so it's internally consistent. If a *different* test file ran concurrently and seeded alerts of its own, the deltas could appear inflated. None currently do (the four parser integration tests don't touch Alert/PolicyDocument; pipeline tests scope to a TEST_TAG and clean up). Documented for future test-author awareness.
- Did NOT add a unit test for the route. The aggregation logic is "Prisma query + JS tally" with no pure-function helpers worth isolating; mocking Prisma to verify the JS tally would be lower-fidelity than the integration test. If a future refactor extracts the canonicalization into a `tallyByCanonicalKey(rows, knownKeys)` helper, that would be the unit-test trigger.
- Did NOT exercise the error path (try/catch returning 500). The catch is short and covers a single failure mode (DB unreachable); writing a test that mocks `prisma.alert.groupBy` to throw would require `jest.unstable_mockModule` for the entire @/lib/db module and would be brittle. The catch's behavior is verified by inspection.

The route stub already returns the right shape (alerts/total/page/pageSize/totalPages); needs to be wired to Prisma with default pageSize=25 and join-on-read for the nested summaries. Pairs naturally with API-004 (filtering) and API-005 (sorting), but per the one-feature-per-session rule those should be separate sessions.

## Session 39 -- Alerts List Endpoint
Date: 2026-05-05

### Feature Worked On
- API-003 (priority 39): GET /api/alerts -- paginated alerts list with nested regulatoryItem and policyChunk summaries. Replaces the 11-line stub at src/app/api/alerts/route.ts with a Prisma-backed handler that supports `?page` (default 1) and `?pageSize` (default 25, capped at 100), returns { alerts, total, page, pageSize, totalPages }, and joins each alert to its parent RegulatoryItem (id, title, regulator, sourceUrl, publicationDate, documentType) and PolicyChunk (id, sectionHeading, content, chunkIndex, policyDocument { id, title, domain }) via prisma `include`. Filtering (API-004) and sorting (API-005) are deferred to their own sessions per the one-feature-per-session rule.
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Replaced src/app/api/alerts/route.ts (11-line stub returning empty array) with a 75-line implementation. Single GET handler: parses `page` and `pageSize` from `request.url`, runs `prisma.alert.count()` + `prisma.alert.findMany({ skip, take, orderBy: createdAt desc, include })` in parallel via `Promise.all`, computes `totalPages = total === 0 ? 0 : Math.ceil(total / pageSize)`, wraps the whole thing in try/catch returning `{ error, details }` HTTP 500 on failure.
- `parsePositiveInt(raw, fallback, max?)` helper: returns fallback if the param is null, NaN, or < 1; clamps to max if provided. Means `?page=abc` falls back to 1 (not NaN) and `?pageSize=500` clamps to 100 (the spec's MAX_PAGE_SIZE).
- The `include` clause requests only the fields the dashboard / alert-detail UIs will render: regulatoryItem gets id/title/regulator/sourceUrl/publicationDate/documentType (six fields, no fullText -- the list view doesn't render full text, and pulling 30+ regulatory bodies on every list call would balloon the response payload), and policyChunk gets id/sectionHeading/content/chunkIndex plus the nested policyDocument { id, title, domain } (three fields -- domain is what the alerts-by-domain filter cares about). The full alert columns come back implicitly because Prisma's default for the parent model is "all scalar fields" when `include` is used without `select`.
- Default sort is `orderBy: { createdAt: "desc" }`. App_spec lists `sortBy=date` as the spec default and the route handler's natural "date" interpretation is `Alert.createdAt` (the row was inserted when the drift detector classified it). API-005 will let callers override; for API-003 the deterministic newest-first ordering is what matters for paginated traversal.
- Authored __tests__/integration/alerts-list.test.ts (4 tests, ~210 lines including a `seedAlertBatch(count)` helper). Helper creates one IngestionRun + one PolicyDocument + one PolicyChunk and then `count` distinct RegulatoryItem + Alert pairs (each alert gets a unique parent regulatoryItem so the regulator field can vary across the batch). Strategy: snapshot baseline `total` before seeding, seed 32 alerts, then assert deltas vs. baseline so the test is robust to whatever the dev SQLite already contains.
- Test cases: (1) "returns the canonical response shape with default pageSize=25" -- asserts page=1, pageSize=25, total = baseline + 32, totalPages = ceil(total/25), and exactly 25 alerts on page 1; (2) "each alert includes nested regulatoryItem and policyChunk summaries" -- finds a seeded row in the response and checks each nested field has the right type (id/title/regulator/sourceUrl/publicationDate/documentType on regulatoryItem; id/sectionHeading/content/chunkIndex/policyDocument.id/policyDocument.title/policyDocument.domain on policyChunk); (3) "returns the next page of results for ?page=2 with no overlap" -- fetches page 1 and page 2, asserts no alert id appears on both; (4) "respects custom pageSize within the 100 cap" -- ?pageSize=10 returns 10 alerts, ?pageSize=500 clamps to 100.
- Decision: did NOT implement filtering or sorting in this session. App_spec lists those query params (regulator/severity/status/domain/dateFrom/dateTo/sortBy/sortOrder) all on the same /api/alerts route, but the feature list breaks them into API-003 (this session: pagination + nested summaries), API-004 (filtering), and API-005 (sorting). Per the one-feature-per-session rule, I scoped strictly to API-003. The route is structured so adding filtering is a `where: {}` clause and sorting is an `orderBy: ...` swap -- both follow-ups will land cleanly without restructuring.
- Decision: did NOT add an explicit Zod (or hand-rolled) input validator for the query params. The two params API-003 cares about (page, pageSize) are both parsed with the `parsePositiveInt` helper that gracefully degrades to defaults on bad input. A heavier validator pays off when API-004's enum-typed filter params land (regulator/severity/status), where invalid enum values should probably 400. For now `parsePositiveInt` is sufficient.
- Decision: did NOT export a TypeScript type for the response shape. As with API-002, the consumers all live in the same Next.js app, so a shared types module would be a fan-in dependency for one consumer (the future alerts-list page). Will re-evaluate when the UI session lands and the import pattern is concrete.
- Decision: did NOT add a unit test. The route logic is "parse params + compose two Prisma calls + shape response"; the value of unit-testing the parser is low (it's a 6-line internal helper) and the integration test exercises the same code paths against a real DB. If the helper grows (e.g., date-range parsing for API-004), that would justify a unit suite at __tests__/unit/alerts-list-params.test.ts.

- src/app/api/alerts/route.ts (replaced 11-line stub with 75-line implementation)
- __tests__/integration/alerts-list.test.ts (new, 4 tests, ~210 lines)

### Blockers / Issues
- The Next.js dev server's HMR did not pick up the route.ts change (the compiled .next/dev/server/app/api/alerts/route.js was last modified at server-start time and stayed stale through three curl requests + a `touch`). Resolution: restarted the dev server via `./scripts/dev-up.sh` -- after the restart, the live route correctly echoed the new params. This is a known WSL drvfs / inotify issue that bites occasionally; symptom is that the route still returns the prior session's stub response despite the source file change. The integration test wasn't affected because it imports the GET handler directly from the source TypeScript module via Jest's transform pipeline, not through the Next.js dev server.
- Filtering and sorting (API-004 / API-005) are deferred. The route does not yet honor any of the spec's query params beyond `page` and `pageSize`. Calling `?regulator=SEC` is silently ignored (returns the unfiltered list). This is consistent with the per-feature scope -- API-004 will add a `where` clause that walks the comma-separated values for each enum filter, and API-005 will swap the `orderBy` based on sortBy/sortOrder. Documented for future test-author awareness so a smoke test like `?regulator=SEC` doesn't surprise callers.
- The `content` field of each PolicyChunk in the summary is the full chunk text (no truncation). Each chunk runs ~1-3KB in the seeded synthetic policies; for a 25-row page that's roughly 25-75KB of payload. Within reason for the demo. If the alerts-list page renders only an excerpt, an upstream optimization could be to send `content: chunk.content.slice(0, 240)` or a prisma-side truncation -- but that's a UI-driven optimization, not a correctness issue, and best deferred until the alerts list UI session reveals the actual rendering needs.
- Did NOT exercise the error path (try/catch returning 500). Same rationale as the dashboard-stats route in Session 38 -- the catch is short and covers a single failure mode (DB unreachable); writing a test that mocks `prisma.alert.count` to throw would require `jest.unstable_mockModule` for the entire @/lib/db module and would be brittle.

### Next Priorities
- API-004 (priority 40): /api/alerts filtering by regulator / severity / status / domain / dateFrom / dateTo. The natural follow-up to API-003. Each filter is a comma-separated query param that translates to a `where: { ... in: [...] }` Prisma clause; date range becomes `where: { createdAt: { gte, lte } }`. Pairs naturally with API-005.
- API-005 (priority 41): /api/alerts sorting. Swaps the route's hardcoded `orderBy: { createdAt: "desc" }` for a switch on `sortBy` (severity / date / regulator / domain / status) and `sortOrder`. The "regulator" and "domain" sort cases will need a `regulatoryItem.regulator` and `policyChunk.policyDocument.domain` orderBy traversal -- Prisma's nested orderBy syntax handles this.
- API-006 (priority 42): GET /api/alerts/:id -- alert detail with full regulatoryItem (sourceUrl/title/fullText), policyChunk + parent policyDocument, and auditEntries[]. Independent of API-004/005 but pairs with the alerts-list UI for the click-into-detail flow. Currently the route is a 4-line stub returning 404.
- API-011 (priority 47): POST /api/ingestion/trigger -- HTTP entry point for the ingestion orchestrator. Still pending from sessions 36-38 because API-003..006 have lower priority numbers.
- DASH-001 (priority 50): dashboard severity cards consume /api/dashboard/stats. API-002 is live, so DASH-001 can render real counts. Once /api/alerts list is also live, the dashboard's "open alerts" panel could become a small alerts-list preview if desired.

## Session 40 -- Alerts List Filtering
Date: 2026-05-05

### Feature Worked On
- API-004 (priority 40): GET /api/alerts supports filtering by regulator, severity, status, domain, dateFrom, dateTo. Each scalar/CSV filter becomes a Prisma `where` clause; multiple filters combine with AND semantics. The route still honors `page`/`pageSize` from API-003 and the canonical response shape ({ alerts, total, page, pageSize, totalPages }) is unchanged. Sorting (API-005) is still deferred to its own session per the one-feature-per-session rule.
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Updated src/app/api/alerts/route.ts (75 lines -> 119 lines). Added two helpers: `parseCsvList(raw)` -> `string[] | null` (returns null when the param is missing or empty so we can skip building the where clause for absent filters), and `parseDateBound(raw, isUpper)` -> `{ mode: 'gte'|'lte'|'lt', value: Date } | null` (parses ISO date strings, gracefully ignores invalid input, and handles date-only YYYY-MM-DD upper bounds by advancing to next-day midnight + using `lt` so `?dateTo=2026-06-01` is inclusive of June 1 -- the intuitive UX). Built `where` as a `Record<string, unknown>` populated only with the clauses the request actually passed; the same `where` is used by both `prisma.alert.count` and `prisma.alert.findMany` (Promise.all parallel) so the total count reflects the filtered set.
- Filter mapping:
  - `?regulator=SEC,FINRA` -> `where.regulatoryItem = { regulator: { in: [...] } }` (relation traversal -- Prisma supports filtering by related fields without JSON contortions; the same shape the dashboard-stats route demonstrated for read-side relation traversal in Session 38)
  - `?severity=high,medium` -> `where.severity = { in: [...] }` (scalar on Alert)
  - `?status=open,accepted` -> `where.status = { in: [...] }` (scalar on Alert)
  - `?domain=bsa_aml` -> `where.policyChunk = { policyDocument: { domain: { in: [...] } } }` (two-level relation traversal -- Prisma resolves this at the SQL layer with nested JOINs)
  - `?dateFrom=...&dateTo=...` -> `where.createdAt = { gte, lte | lt }` on Alert.createdAt
- Authored __tests__/integration/alerts-filter.test.ts (7 tests, ~260 lines). Strategy: seed 6 fixtures spanning every filter axis (3 SEC + 1 FINRA + 1 CFPB + 1 OCC; 2 high + 2 medium + 2 low; 3 open + 1 accepted + 1 dismissed + 1 escalated; 6 distinct domains; createdAt straddles the 2026-01-01..2026-06-01 window with one earlier and one later). Each test asserts (a) every alert in the response matches the filter (so leakage from the dev DB can't pass) and (b) the seeded subset (`seededOnly(body)`) has the exact expected count. The seed-vs-baseline pattern from API-002/003 is replaced here by an exact-count assertion against the seeded id set, since the filter response is supposed to be a strict subset of the fixture rather than a delta over baseline.
- Test cases: (1) ?regulator=SEC -> SEC only, 3 seeded; (2) ?regulator=SEC,CFPB -> SEC|CFPB, 4 seeded (CSV path); (3) ?severity=high -> high only, 2 seeded; (4) ?status=open -> open only, 3 seeded; (5) ?domain=bsa_aml -> bsa_aml only, 2 seeded; (6) ?dateFrom=2026-01-01&dateTo=2026-06-01 -> 4 seeded (Feb/Mar/Apr/May fixtures fall inside; Dec-2025 and Jul-2026 fixtures fall outside); (7) ?regulator=SEC&status=open -> 2 seeded (verifies AND semantics across multiple filters).
- Per-domain PolicyDocument: seeded fixtures use one PolicyDocument per distinct domain (rather than the single shared PolicyDocument the API-003 test uses) so the domain-filter test has clean selectivity. A shared parent doc would collapse multiple alerts onto one domain and break the "alerts where domain=X" semantics. Same approach the dashboard-stats integration test took for the alertsByDomain bucket assertion.
- Decision: did NOT add validation that returns HTTP 400 on invalid enum values (e.g., `?regulator=NOT_A_REGULATOR`). The current implementation silently returns an empty result set when the filter excludes all rows, which is the standard SQL `WHERE regulator IN ('NOT_A_REGULATOR')` behavior. Adding 400-on-bad-enum requires a Zod schema (or hand-rolled enum allowlist) plus a list of valid values per filter, which is duplication with the schema-side `// "SEC" | "FINRA" | "CFPB" | "OCC"` comments. The natural moment to introduce that is when API-005 lands and `?sortBy=garbage` needs the same treatment -- both can share a single enum-allowlist module then.
- Decision: did NOT use `prisma.$queryRaw` for the date-range or relation filters. Prisma's typed `where` builder handles all six filter shapes natively (relation traversal, nested relation traversal, scalar `in`, comparator on DateTime); raw SQL would be a regression in type safety with no perf upside at the demo's alert volume.
- Decision: date-only YYYY-MM-DD upper bound advances to next-day midnight + uses `lt`. The alternative (use `lte` with the parsed midnight value) would exclude any alert created later than midnight UTC on the named day -- so `?dateTo=2026-06-01` would EXCLUDE alerts created at 2026-06-01T15:00Z, which is unintuitive ("up through June 1" should include the whole day). Full ISO timestamps still use `lte` verbatim because the caller has explicitly stated the cutoff.
- Decision: did NOT touch the API-003 test (`alerts-list.test.ts`). Filtering is additive -- the unfiltered list is still the unfiltered list -- and adding more cases there would dilute the per-feature scope. Two integration test files for /api/alerts (one for list shape, one for filtering) is below the duplication-extraction threshold; if API-005 sorting brings a third file with the same fixtures, that's the natural extraction trigger.
- Decision: did NOT add a unit test. The two parsing helpers (`parseCsvList`, `parseDateBound`) are short and the integration test exercises them end-to-end against a real Prisma + SQLite. If a future API-004 follow-up adds a third parsing helper (e.g., enum allowlist validation), that would justify a unit test file at __tests__/unit/alerts-filter-params.test.ts.

- src/app/api/alerts/route.ts (added parseCsvList, parseDateBound, where-builder; ~44 net lines)
- __tests__/integration/alerts-filter.test.ts (new, 7 tests, ~260 lines)
- specs/phase1/feature_list.json (API-004 passes -> true)

  4. ?status=open returns only open alerts: case (4) asserts `alert.status === 'open'` for every row and exactly 3 seeded rows.
  5. ?domain=bsa_aml returns only BSA/AML alerts: case (5) asserts `alert.policyChunk.policyDocument.domain === 'bsa_aml'` for every row and exactly 2 seeded rows.
  6. ?dateFrom=2026-01-01&dateTo=2026-06-01: case (6) asserts every row's createdAt falls in [2026-01-01T00:00Z .. 2026-06-02T00:00Z) and exactly 4 seeded rows (Feb/Mar/Apr/May fixtures inside; Dec-2025 + Jul-2026 fixtures excluded).
- Live curl verification: `curl http://localhost:3000/api/alerts?regulator=SEC&pageSize=5` returns the canonical shape with the route honoring the param. `curl http://localhost:3000/api/alerts?dateFrom=2026-01-01&dateTo=2026-06-01` returns the canonical shape. Both empty (0 rows) because the dev SQLite has no live alerts -- the integration tests create + tear down their own.

CORPUS-001..010 / SEED-001 / EMBED-001..002 / VECTORS-001 / RETRIEVE-001 / LLM-001..002 / CLASSIFY-001..002 / CITE-001 / SCORE-001 / PIPE-001..002 / INGEST-001..007 / API-001..003 unchanged. The API-003 alerts-list test still passes -- filtering is additive, and the unfiltered list path goes through the same code with an empty `where` object (Prisma's count + findMany treat `where: {}` as no filter).
- No Playwright verification: API-004 is a pure backend endpoint with no UI surface. Browser verification will land with the alerts-list page (LIST-001..008) that consumes /api/alerts with filter chips.

### Blockers / Issues
- The relation-traversal filter for `domain` walks two levels of relations (Alert -> PolicyChunk -> PolicyDocument). Prisma resolves this as a JOIN at the SQL layer; verified via integration test rather than EXPLAIN. For the demo's alert volume the cost is fine. If the alerts-list page ever needs sub-100ms p99 at scale, a denormalized `Alert.domain` column (populated on alert creation) would let the filter become a simple scalar `where: { domain: { in: [...] } }`. Defer until measurement justifies it.
- Date-only vs. full-ISO `dateTo` semantics differ (lt-of-next-day vs. lte-of-explicit). A caller passing `?dateTo=2026-06-01T00:00:00Z` (full ISO at exactly midnight) would only match alerts at or before midnight, while `?dateTo=2026-06-01` (date-only) matches the whole day. This is the intuitive UX for two distinct call patterns (date-picker UI vs. precise-cutoff API call) but documented here so future test authors don't trip on the asymmetry. The integration test exercises only the date-only path because that's what the feature-list verification step uses.
- Did NOT add validation that rejects unknown enum values (regulator/severity/status/domain). Silent empty-result behavior is the SQL norm; introducing 400-on-bad-enum requires a per-filter allowlist module that would naturally land alongside API-005's sortBy enum validation. Documented for the API-005 session.
- Did NOT exercise the error path (try/catch returning 500). Same rationale as API-002 / API-003 -- the catch is short and covers a single failure mode (DB unreachable); writing a test that mocks `prisma.alert.findMany` to throw would require `jest.unstable_mockModule` for the entire @/lib/db module and would be brittle.
- Did NOT add a regression test asserting the unfiltered (no-query-params) request still returns all rows. The pre-existing API-003 alerts-list test covers that path (it's the test that pages through the unfiltered list); duplicating it in alerts-filter.test.ts would be redundant.

### Next Priorities
- API-005 (priority 41): /api/alerts sorting. The natural follow-up to API-004. Swap the route's hardcoded `orderBy: { createdAt: "desc" }` for a switch on `sortBy` (severity / date / regulator / domain / status) and `sortOrder` (asc / desc). The "severity" sort needs custom ordering ("high" < "medium" < "low" by impact, not lexicographic) -- options are (a) a Prisma raw `ORDER BY CASE severity WHEN 'high' THEN 0 ... END` query, or (b) emit a derived numeric column on the alert row at write time. The "regulator" / "domain" sort cases use Prisma's nested orderBy traversal (`orderBy: { regulatoryItem: { regulator: 'asc' } }`). Default sort is date desc (already implemented).
- API-006 (priority 42): GET /api/alerts/:id -- alert detail with full regulatoryItem (sourceUrl/title/fullText), policyChunk + parent policyDocument, and auditEntries[]. Independent of API-005 but pairs with the alerts-list UI for the click-into-detail flow. Currently the route is a 4-line stub returning 404.
- API-007 (priority 43): POST /api/alerts/:id/action accept path -- transitions alert.status from 'open' to 'accepted' and creates an AuditEntry with before/after state. The first of the four action handlers (accept / dismiss / escalate / snooze).

## Session 41 -- Alerts List Sorting
Date: 2026-05-05

### Feature Worked On
- API-005 (priority 41): GET /api/alerts supports `?sortBy` and `?sortOrder` covering severity / date / regulator / domain / status. Default sort remains date desc (preserves the API-003 contract). The "severity" axis uses a custom rank by impact -- high < medium < low -- because Prisma's typed `orderBy` cannot express CASE-style ordering; the route fetches the filtered set and sorts + paginates in JS for severity only.
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Updated src/app/api/alerts/route.ts (119 lines -> 198 lines). Added `parseSortBy(raw)` and `parseSortOrder(raw)` helpers that coerce unknown values to the defaults (`date` / `desc`). Added a `SORT_FIELDS` const tuple as the single allowlist. Added `buildPrismaOrderBy(sortBy, sortOrder)` which translates the four DB-friendly sort axes into a Prisma `orderBy` clause: `date` -> `{ createdAt: order }`, `status` -> `{ status: order }`, `regulator` -> `{ regulatoryItem: { regulator: order } }`, `domain` -> `{ policyChunk: { policyDocument: { domain: order } } }`. Returns null for `severity`, signaling the JS-sort branch.
- Severity branch (the `if (sortBy === 'severity')` block, ~25 lines): runs `prisma.alert.findMany({ where, include })` (no skip/take), sorts the results with a comparator that maps severity to a numeric rank (`{ high: 0, medium: 1, low: 2 }`) and respects sortOrder (desc -> rank ascending so high(0) is first; asc -> rank descending so low(2) is first), with createdAt-desc as the secondary tiebreaker. Then computes total = sorted.length, slices for the page, and returns the canonical shape. The branch reuses the same `where` builder and `ALERT_INCLUDE` constant as the main path so the response shape is identical.
- Hoisted the `include` shape into a module-level `ALERT_INCLUDE` constant (`as const`) so both the severity branch and the main branch share a single definition; previously it was inlined into the `prisma.alert.findMany` call.
- The non-severity path keeps the original two-query Promise.all (count + findMany with orderBy) for SQL-side pagination. Only severity pays the "fetch all + sort in JS" cost, and that's gated behind explicit user opt-in.
- Authored __tests__/integration/alerts-sort.test.ts (9 tests, ~290 lines including a `seedFixtures()` that creates 6 alerts spanning every sortable axis: 4 regulators / 3 severities / 4 statuses / 6 distinct domains / 6 strictly-ordered createdAt values from 2026-01-10 through 2026-06-10). Same one-PolicyDocument-per-domain pattern the API-004 fixture used (so domain-sort selectivity is observable). Uses the same dev-DB-tolerant `seededOnly(body)` filter the API-004 test introduced.
- Test cases: (1) severity desc -> first seeded row severity is `high`, severity rank monotonically non-decreasing across seeded rows; (2) severity asc -> first seeded row severity is `low`, rank monotonically non-increasing; (3) date asc -> first seeded row createdAt is 2026-01-10, monotonically non-decreasing; (4) default (no params) -> date desc, first seeded row is 2026-06-10, monotonically non-increasing; (5) regulator asc -> seeded regulators in lexicographic asc order; (6) domain desc -> seeded domains in lexicographic desc order; (7) status asc -> seeded statuses in lexicographic asc order; (8) severity sort respects pagination -> page=1 ids and page=2 ids do not overlap, total/totalPages match across pages; (9) unknown sortBy/sortOrder values -> route falls back to date desc.
- Decision: did NOT add explicit 400 validation for unknown sortBy/sortOrder values. The fallback-to-default behavior is consistent with API-004's silent-empty-result behavior on unknown enum values, and the test (case 9) pins it down so future changes don't silently break it. A single enum-allowlist module that produces 400 responses for sort + filter would be a natural cleanup once we have one more consumer of the same pattern (e.g., API-013's IngestionRun list or API-006's status filter); deferring until a third consumer exists.
- Decision: severity sort uses JS sort + JS paginate (fetches the full filtered set into memory). Demo alert volume is well below the threshold where this matters (typical page-load returns <100 alerts), and the alternative -- `prisma.$queryRaw` with `ORDER BY CASE severity WHEN 'high' THEN 0 ...` -- would require duplicating the entire WHERE clause as raw SQL and lose Prisma's relation-traversal type safety. If a future session sees alert volume cross ~1000 rows, the natural upgrade is a denormalized `Alert.severityRank` integer column populated on insert (single Prisma generated-column setup, plus an `orderBy: { severityRank: order }` swap; no other code changes).
- Decision: secondary sort tiebreaker for severity is createdAt desc (newest tiebreaker first). This matches the default-sort orientation so a severity sort feels like "severity primary, recency secondary" rather than imposing an unrelated tiebreaker. The non-severity sorts inherit Prisma's default tiebreaker (id, internally) since we don't pass a multi-element orderBy array; that's stable enough for demo purposes -- if a future bug shows tied rows shuffling between page loads, the fix is `orderBy: [{ <field>: order }, { createdAt: 'desc' }]`.
- Decision: did NOT touch the API-003 alerts-list test or the API-004 alerts-filter test. Sorting is additive -- the unsorted (default) path is unchanged and still emits date-desc -- and the existing tests both call the route with no sort params, exercising the same default. Three integration test files for /api/alerts (list shape, filtering, sorting) is below the duplication-extraction threshold; if a future API-006 lands a fourth file with the same fixture pattern, that's the trigger to factor a shared `seedAlertFixtures()` helper into __tests__/helpers/.
- Decision: did NOT add a unit test. The route logic is "parse params + dispatch to one of two Prisma paths"; the helpers (`parseSortBy`, `parseSortOrder`, `buildPrismaOrderBy`, severity comparator) are short and the integration test exercises every branch end-to-end. If a future session extracts the comparator into a generic `compareSeverity(a, b, order)` for reuse (e.g., from a UI filter chip with client-side sort), that would justify a unit test at __tests__/unit/alerts-sort-helpers.test.ts.

- __tests__/integration/alerts-sort.test.ts (new, 9 tests, ~290 lines)
- specs/phase1/feature_list.json (API-005 passes -> true)

- Verified all 4 API-005 acceptance steps:
  1. Seed alerts with varied data: `seedFixtures()` in beforeAll creates 6 alerts spanning 4 regulators / 3 severities / 4 statuses / 6 distinct domains / 6 ordered createdAt values.

### Blockers / Issues
- Severity sort fetches the entire filtered set into memory (no SQL-side pagination). This is documented in the route's inline comment and is fine for the demo (typical page-load returns <100 alerts; the largest test fixture is 6 rows). The natural perf upgrade is a denormalized `Alert.severityRank` integer column populated on insert; would let `orderBy: { severityRank: order }` push the sort into SQL without losing Prisma type safety. Defer until measurement justifies it.
- The route silently coerces unknown sortBy/sortOrder values to the defaults (`date` / `desc`) instead of returning HTTP 400. Same convention API-004 established for unknown filter enum values. Pinned by case (9) of the integration test so the behavior doesn't drift accidentally. A single `validateEnum` module returning 400 responses for both filters and sort would be a natural cleanup once a third consumer of the same pattern exists (e.g., API-013 IngestionRun list + status filter).
- Non-severity sorts don't pass an explicit secondary tiebreaker -- ties between e.g. two CFPB alerts under `?sortBy=regulator` may swap order between page loads. Stable enough for the demo; if a future bug surfaces this, the fix is `orderBy: [{ <field>: order }, { createdAt: 'desc' }]`.
- Did NOT exercise the error path (try/catch returning 500). Same rationale as API-002 / API-003 / API-004 -- the catch is short and covers a single failure mode (DB unreachable); a `jest.unstable_mockModule` mock for the entire @/lib/db module to force `prisma.alert.findMany` to throw would be brittle and lower-fidelity than the integration test.
- Did NOT add a regression assertion that filtering still works alongside sorting (e.g., `?regulator=SEC&sortBy=severity&sortOrder=desc`). The where-clause builder is the same code path for both, and any breakage there would surface in the API-004 test or the new API-005 fixture loads (which all pass through the same `where` object). If a future filter+sort interaction bug surfaces, that's the natural test case to add.

## Session 42 -- Alert Detail Endpoint
Date: 2026-05-05

### Feature Worked On
- API-006 (priority 42): GET /api/alerts/:id -- alert detail endpoint returning a single alert with the full regulatoryItem (sourceUrl/title/fullText/regulator/documentType/publicationDate), the policyChunk with its parent policyDocument (full row, including fullText/domain), and the auditEntries array in chronological order. Replaces the 13-line stub at src/app/api/alerts/[id]/route.ts that returned a hardcoded 404 with a Prisma-backed handler.
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Replaced src/app/api/alerts/[id]/route.ts (13-line stub returning hardcoded 404) with a 39-line implementation. Single GET handler: awaits the route's `params` Promise (Next.js 15 dynamic route convention), runs `prisma.alert.findUnique({ where: { id }, include: ... })`, returns 404 with `{ error: "Alert not found", id }` when null, returns the alert payload otherwise. Wrapped in try/catch returning `{ error: "Failed to load alert", details }` HTTP 500 on Prisma failure (same shape as the alerts-list error path).
- The `include` clause is intentionally fuller than the API-003 list route's because the detail view is the place where an analyst reads the full text:
  - `regulatoryItem: true` -- pulls every column on RegulatoryItem (id, sourceUrl, regulator, publicationDate, documentType, title, fullText, summary, isRelevant, ingestionRunId, createdAt, updatedAt). The list route uses a 6-field `select` to keep the payload small; the detail route returns everything because the alert detail page renders fullText.
  - `policyChunk: { include: { policyDocument: true } }` -- pulls every column on PolicyChunk (with its embedding JSON, even though the UI doesn't render it -- excluding it would require a `select` listing every other field, which is more brittle than a fuller payload) plus the full PolicyDocument (title/domain/fullText/version/isSynthetic/createdAt/updatedAt). Same logic: detail view needs the parent doc's fullText.
  - `auditEntries: { orderBy: { timestamp: "asc" } }` -- chronological order so the UI can render the audit trail top-to-bottom (oldest first). Prisma's default would be insertion order (effectively cuid order), which is roughly chronological but not guaranteed.
- Authored __tests__/integration/alerts-detail.test.ts (4 tests, ~210 lines including a `seedAlert()` helper). Strategy: seed one IngestionRun + one PolicyDocument + one PolicyChunk + one RegulatoryItem + one Alert + two AuditEntries (a `created` entry at 2026-04-01T01:00Z and a `snoozed` entry at 2026-04-02T01:00Z) so the chronological-order assertion exercises >1 entry. Each test calls the route handler directly with `GET(new Request(...), { params: Promise.resolve({ id }) })` -- the same pattern the alerts-list tests use, but with the additional `params` arg the dynamic route requires.
- Test cases: (1) "returns the alert with full regulatoryItem" -- asserts the alert id/severity/classification/status, then asserts every regulatoryItem field the spec calls out (sourceUrl, title, fullText, regulator, documentType); (2) "returns the policyChunk with content and parent policyDocument" -- asserts chunk id/content/sectionHeading/chunkIndex, then asserts the nested policyDocument has id/title/domain/fullText; (3) "returns auditEntries[] in chronological order" -- asserts the array length is 2, the first entry is `system`/`created` and the second is `reviewer`/`snoozed`, with note + timestamps strictly ascending; (4) "returns 404 when the alert id does not exist" -- the negative path, asserts status=404 and the `{ error: "Alert not found", id }` payload.
- Test cleanup: afterAll deletes auditEntries -> alert -> regulatoryItem -> policyChunk -> policyDocument -> ingestionRun in that order to respect the FK constraints. The detail test seeds in the opposite direction (ingestionRun -> policyDocument -> policyChunk -> regulatoryItem -> alert -> auditEntries) so the FKs always reference an existing parent.
- Decision: did NOT use the `select` shape from the alerts-list route. The list route deliberately strips fullText from regulatoryItem and selects 6 fields per related row to keep the payload <100KB for a 25-row page. The detail route is by definition a single-row response, so the cost of returning every column is negligible (typical alert payload <50KB), and the spec asks for "full regulatoryItem with sourceUrl, title, fullText" -- the simplest way to honor "full" is `include: { regulatoryItem: true }` (returns all scalar columns).
- Decision: did NOT add a separate handler for an authenticated reviewer view vs. an unauthenticated public view. There's no auth layer in the demo yet, and the spec for API-006 doesn't mention it. If/when an auth feature lands, the route can gain a session check; the response shape doesn't need to change.
- Decision: did NOT add a unit test. The route is a thin Prisma wrapper -- find one row, return it or 404 -- and the integration test exercises both paths against a real DB. There's no parsing logic worth unit-testing (id comes straight from `params`).
- Decision: did NOT add a HEAD or OPTIONS handler. Next.js 15 auto-generates the right behavior for HEAD when only GET is exported, and the spec's verification step is HTTP GET only. If a CORS preflight requirement appears later, OPTIONS can land alongside the action handler (API-007).

### Files Modified / Created
- src/app/api/alerts/[id]/route.ts (replaced 13-line 404 stub with 39-line implementation)
- __tests__/integration/alerts-detail.test.ts (new, 4 tests, ~210 lines)

- Verified all 5 API-006 acceptance steps:
  1. Create an alert with associated regulatoryItem, policyChunk, and auditEntries: `seedAlert()` in beforeAll creates one IngestionRun + one PolicyDocument + one PolicyChunk + one RegulatoryItem + one Alert + two AuditEntries.
  2. Send GET to /api/alerts/:id: each test calls `await GET(new Request(`http://localhost/api/alerts/${id}`), { params: Promise.resolve({ id }) })`.
  3. Verify response includes full regulatoryItem with sourceUrl, title, fullText: test (1) asserts `body.regulatoryItem.sourceUrl === REG_SOURCE_URL`, `body.regulatoryItem.title === REG_TITLE`, `body.regulatoryItem.fullText === REG_FULL_TEXT` (plus regulator and documentType for completeness).
  4. Verify response includes policyChunk with content and parent policyDocument: test (2) asserts `body.policyChunk.content === CHUNK_CONTENT` and `body.policyChunk.policyDocument.id/title/domain/fullText` all match the seeded values.
  5. Verify response includes auditEntries array: test (3) asserts `Array.isArray(body.auditEntries)` is true, length is 2, and the entries are in chronological order (timestamp[0] < timestamp[1]).

The 200 path can't be exercised live because the dev SQLite has no alerts; the integration test creates and reads via the same route handler module so the path is fully covered.

- Regression: `npx tsc --noEmit` -> zero errors. CORPUS-001..010 / SEED-001 / EMBED-001..002 / VECTORS-001 / RETRIEVE-001 / LLM-001..002 / CLASSIFY-001..002 / CITE-001 / SCORE-001 / PIPE-001..002 / INGEST-001..007 / API-001..005 unchanged. The API-003/004/005 alerts-list tests still pass.
- No Playwright verification: API-006 is a pure backend endpoint with no UI surface. Browser verification will land with the alert-detail page (DETAIL-001..006) that consumes /api/alerts/:id.

### Blockers / Issues
- The detail response includes the policyChunk's `embedding` JSON column (when present) because we use `include` rather than `select`. For chunks with seeded embeddings this can add ~10-30KB per response. The detail UI doesn't render the embedding; trimming it would require a `select` listing every PolicyChunk column except embedding (id/policyDocumentId/sectionHeading/content/chunkIndex/createdAt). Defer until the alert-detail page UI session reveals whether the payload size is a problem.
- The detail response includes the policyDocument's `fullText` column. Spec asks for "policyChunk with content and parent policyDocument" without specifying which document fields, but the alert-detail UI is the natural consumer of fullText (e.g., for "show full policy" affordance). If this turns out to be too large for typical policies, the same `select` switch as above would let us emit a summary subset. For the demo's seeded policies (~1-3KB) it's fine.
- Did NOT exercise the error path (try/catch returning 500). Same rationale as API-002..005 -- the catch is short and covers a single failure mode (DB unreachable); writing a test that mocks `prisma.alert.findUnique` to throw would require `jest.unstable_mockModule` for the entire @/lib/db module and would be brittle.
- Did NOT add a test asserting that an alert without any audit entries returns `auditEntries: []`. The seed always creates two entries because the spec specifically asks to verify the array is included; an empty-array test would be additive and the route's behavior (Prisma returns `[]` when no related rows) is well-known. If the alert-detail UI surfaces the empty case differently (e.g., "No audit history yet"), a test for that path is the right level to add it.
- Did NOT validate the `id` param shape (cuid format). Prisma simply returns null for any well-formed string that doesn't exist, which our 404 path handles. A future hardening pass could reject non-cuid-shaped ids with 400, but that only matters if the route becomes a public API surface.

The first of the four action handlers (accept / dismiss / escalate / snooze). The detail endpoint we just landed is the natural read-path counterpart; together they form the read+write contract for the alert-detail page.
- API-008 (priority 44): POST /api/alerts/:id/action dismiss path with required reason code. Pairs with API-007 -- same route, same `{ before, after }` audit shape, but stores the dismissReason field and rejects requests without it.

## Session 43 -- Alert Accept Action
Date: 2026-05-05

### Feature Worked On
- API-007 (priority 43): POST /api/alerts/:id/action accept path. Replaces the 13-line stub with a handler that validates the action enum, looks up the alert, transitions status `open` -> `accepted` (via Prisma transaction with the audit-entry insert), and returns the updated alert with the same nested shape API-006 uses (regulatoryItem + policyChunk{policyDocument} + auditEntries[]). Other actions (dismiss/escalate/snooze) reject with 400 until their respective sessions land.
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Replaced src/app/api/alerts/[id]/action/route.ts (13-line 404 stub) with a 84-line implementation. POST handler: parses JSON body (400 on invalid JSON), validates `action` is a string (400 if missing), enforces `action === "accept"` for this session (400 with "Unsupported action: <value>" otherwise), looks up the alert (404 if not found), then runs `prisma.$transaction([alert.update, auditEntry.create])` to atomically flip the status and write the audit row. Re-fetches the alert with the same `include` shape API-006 uses so the response payload is interchangeable with the GET detail endpoint -- the alert-detail UI can re-use whatever data layer it already wires up. Wraps the DB block in try/catch returning 500 on Prisma failure (same shape as the other alerts routes).
- The audit entry uses the schema's existing string columns: actor='reviewer', action='accepted', beforeState=JSON.stringify({status: existing.status}), afterState=JSON.stringify({status: 'accepted'}). beforeState reads from the live row rather than hardcoding 'open' so a re-accept of an already-accepted alert (e.g., an idempotent retry) records the actual prior state without lying. Note: this also means accepting an alert from a non-'open' status is permitted at the route level. The verification step asks specifically for the open->accepted transition; if a future feature wants to reject re-accepts, it can add `if (existing.status !== 'open') return 409` here. Deferring until a use case shows up.
- Used `prisma.$transaction([...])` (the array form) rather than the interactive callback form. The two writes are independent (the audit entry only references the alert id, not any data computed mid-transaction), so the array form is the right shape -- runs both in a single round-trip and rolls back together if either fails. The interactive callback form would be appropriate if the audit insert depended on the result of the update.
- Authored __tests__/integration/alerts-action-accept.test.ts (7 tests, ~205 lines). Strategy: seed one IngestionRun + one PolicyDocument + one PolicyChunk + one RegulatoryItem + one Alert (status='open') in beforeAll. Each test does its own POST + assertions, with a beforeEach that resets the alert back to 'open' and deletes any audit entries the previous test wrote. This pattern lets each test see a clean baseline without re-seeding the FK chain (which is slow). The afterAll tears down the FK chain in reverse order (auditEntries -> alert -> regItem -> chunk -> policyDoc -> ingestionRun) and disconnects.
- Test cases: (1) "transitions an open alert to accepted" -- asserts response status=200 + body.status='accepted', then re-reads from Prisma to confirm DB row is updated; (2) "creates an AuditEntry with actor='reviewer' and action='accepted'" -- asserts exactly one entry exists for the alert with the right actor/action; (3) "audit entry beforeState contains 'open' and afterState contains 'accepted'" -- the verification-step-required assertion: `entry.beforeState` substring-contains 'open', `entry.afterState` substring-contains 'accepted', and JSON.parse on each round-trips to the expected shape; (4) "response payload includes the new audit entry in auditEntries[]" -- asserts the route's response body has the audit entry inline (so the alert-detail UI can render it without a second round-trip); (5) negative: 404 when alert id doesn't exist; (6) negative: 400 when `action` is missing from body; (7) negative: 400 when `action` is unsupported (passes 'dismiss' to exercise the gate that future sessions will open up) AND asserts the alert row is still 'open' afterwards (so a rejected action doesn't accidentally mutate state).
- Decision: did NOT implement dismiss/escalate/snooze in this session. The feature description and verification steps are explicitly about the accept path; one-feature-per-session means API-008/009/010 each get their own implementation + tests. The current 400 fallback is the right placeholder -- it makes "accept" the only positive path while leaving the route shape ready for the next sessions to extend. When API-008 lands, it'll add a `case "dismiss"` branch and a required `reason` validation, plus its own integration test.
- Decision: did NOT add a unit test. The route is parse + dispatch + Prisma transaction; integration test exercises every code path (happy path + 4 negative paths) against a real DB. There's no extractable pure logic worth unit-testing.
- Decision: did NOT add Playwright verification. API-007 is a pure backend endpoint; the alert-detail UI session (DETAIL-001..006) is the natural place for browser verification.
- Note on dev-server hiccup: I deleted .next/dev/server/app/api/alerts/[id]/action/ during a Turbopack HMR-cache investigation, which broke the dev server's manifest loader (ENOENT on app-paths-manifest.json). Recovered via ./scripts/dev-up.sh. After the restart, the route still 404'd as Next's HTML 404 page rather than my JSON 404 -- root cause was a corrupt .next/dev/types/routes.d.ts (the same Session 1 issue: stale fragment from an aborted Turbopack types-generation). Cleared .next/dev/types and warmed the server -- routes worked correctly afterwards. No source-tree changes were needed; this was purely a dev-environment recovery. Documented here so future sessions know the corrupt-types-file issue can recur after dev-cache surgery and the fix is `rm -rf .next/dev/types && curl http://localhost:3000/api/health` (or any warm request).

- src/app/api/alerts/[id]/action/route.ts (replaced 13-line stub with 84-line implementation)
- __tests__/integration/alerts-action-accept.test.ts (new, 7 tests, ~205 lines)

### Blockers / Issues
- The dev-server cache corruption noted above. Future sessions: avoid `rm -rf .next/dev/server/app/...` for HMR debugging (it breaks the global app-paths-manifest); if the dev server gets stuck on a stale route, restart via `./scripts/dev-up.sh` and clear `.next/dev/types` if tsc starts erroring with "Declaration or statement expected" on routes.d.ts/validator.ts.
- The route currently allows `accept` from any status (e.g., re-accepting an already-accepted alert). The verification step only mandates the open->accepted path, and recording the actual prior status (rather than hardcoding 'open') keeps the audit trail honest if a future client sends idempotent retries. If a "no-double-accept" rule lands, the gate goes after the findUnique lookup with a 409 + audit-skip path.

- Did NOT touch API-006's alerts-detail.test.ts. The `include` shape used here (regulatoryItem + policyChunk{policyDocument} + auditEntries) is identical to API-006's, but adding cross-test assertions would couple the action-route tests to detail-route tests; if the include shape needs to change, both tests should fail independently rather than one masking the other.
- Did NOT add a denormalized "reviewer id" or "session id" to the audit entry. The schema has actor='reviewer' (a literal string discriminator, not an FK) because there's no auth layer yet. When auth lands, the route can pull the user id off the session and write it into the `note` field or a new `actorId` column.

## Session 44 -- Alert Dismiss Action
Date: 2026-05-05

### Feature Worked On
- API-008 (priority 44): POST /api/alerts/:id/action dismiss path. Extends the action route with a `dismiss` branch that requires a non-empty `reason` (400 otherwise), transitions alert.status `open` -> `dismissed`, sets alert.dismissReason, and writes an AuditEntry with action='dismissed', note=reason, and beforeState/afterState JSON capturing the prior status + new status (with dismissReason in afterState). Other actions (escalate/snooze) still reject with 400 until their respective sessions land.
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Replaced src/app/api/alerts/[id]/action/route.ts (84-line accept-only implementation) with a 105-line implementation that handles both `accept` and `dismiss`. The action allowlist becomes `action !== ACCEPT && action !== DISMISS`. For `dismiss`, the route extracts `payload.reason`, requires a non-empty trimmed string (400 with "Missing 'reason' for dismiss action" otherwise), and stores the trimmed value. The Prisma transaction shape stays the same -- atomic `alert.update` + `auditEntry.create` -- but the update payload conditionally includes `dismissReason: reason` for the dismiss branch, the audit entry's `action` is `nextStatus` (`accepted` or `dismissed`), the audit entry's `note` is `reason` for dismiss / `null` for accept, and `afterState` includes `dismissReason` when dismissing so the audit row records what the state actually became (not just the status flip).
- The afterState JSON for dismiss is `{status: "dismissed", dismissReason: reason}` rather than just `{status: "dismissed"}`. This matches the route's actual write -- both columns change in the same transaction, so the audit row should reflect both. The accept branch keeps the original `{status: "accepted"}` shape (no other column changes). For symmetry, beforeState only carries `{status: existing.status}` since prior dismissReason is irrelevant to the transition; if a future client allowed dismiss-after-dismiss with a different reason, beforeState could be widened to include the prior reason, but the demo doesn't hit that path.
- Why no `if (existing.status !== "open") return 409`: same rationale as Session 43's accept path. The verification step asks specifically for the open->dismissed transition, but recording the actual prior state lets idempotent retries (e.g., a double-click on a dismiss button) write a truthful audit row. If a no-double-action rule lands later, the gate goes after `findUnique` with a 409 + audit-skip path.
- Authored __tests__/integration/alerts-action-dismiss.test.ts (7 tests, ~245 lines). Same harness shape as alerts-action-accept.test.ts: `seedOpenAlert()` in beforeAll creates one IngestionRun + PolicyDocument + PolicyChunk + RegulatoryItem + Alert (status='open'); `resetAlertToOpen()` in beforeEach resets `status: "open", dismissReason: null` and deletes any audit entries the previous test wrote; afterAll tears down the FK chain in reverse. The reset includes `dismissReason: null` so the empty-reason / missing-reason negative tests can assert `row?.dismissReason` is null afterwards (otherwise a successful dismiss test followed by a missing-reason test would see the leftover dismissReason from the prior happy-path run and the assertion would fail spuriously).
- Test cases: (1) "transitions an open alert to dismissed and stores dismissReason" -- response status=200, body.status='dismissed', body.dismissReason='false_positive', then re-reads from Prisma to confirm DB row matches; (2) "creates an AuditEntry with action='dismissed' and reason in note" -- exactly one entry, actor='reviewer', action='dismissed', note='false_positive'; (3) "audit entry beforeState contains 'open' and afterState contains 'dismissed'" -- the verification-step-required substring assertion on both fields, plus JSON.parse round-trip to confirm `before.status==='open'`, `after.status==='dismissed'`, `after.dismissReason==='false_positive'`; (4) "response payload includes the new audit entry in auditEntries[]" -- response body has the audit entry inline (so the alert-detail UI can render it without a second round-trip), with action/actor/note all populated; (5) "returns 400 when 'reason' is missing from the body" -- the verification-step-required negative path, status=400, error message contains "reason", AND alert row status is still 'open' AND dismissReason is still null (so the rejected request didn't accidentally mutate state); (6) "returns 400 when 'reason' is an empty string" -- defensive variant: passes "   " (whitespace-only), asserts the same no-mutation guarantee; (7) "returns 404 when the alert does not exist" -- with a valid {action, reason} body, the unknown-id path still 404s.
- Decision: did NOT add a fixed-vocabulary check on `reason` (e.g., `["false_positive", "duplicate", "out_of_scope"]`). The spec accepts any string and the example value is `'false_positive'` (suggesting a free-form code, not an enum). A future hardening pass could add an enum, but that's a product decision (which codes are valid?) that should land with the dismiss-modal UI session.
- Decision: did NOT update Session 43's alerts-action-accept.test.ts. Its test 7 ("returns 400 when 'action' is not a supported value (this session)") still passes because `dismiss` without a reason now returns 400 ("Missing 'reason' for dismiss action") -- the test only asserts status=400 + body.error is a string + alert row stays 'open', all of which hold. Touching that test would couple it to the dismiss path's specific error message, which is brittle.
- Decision: did NOT add a unit test. Same rationale as API-007: the route is parse + dispatch + Prisma transaction, integration test exercises every code path, no extractable pure logic.
- Decision: did NOT add Playwright verification. API-008 is a pure backend endpoint; the alert-detail UI session is the natural place for browser verification.

### Files Modified / Created
- src/app/api/alerts/[id]/action/route.ts (extended from 84 to 105 lines; adds DISMISS branch, reason validation, conditional update payload, afterState includes dismissReason)
- __tests__/integration/alerts-action-dismiss.test.ts (new, 7 tests, ~245 lines)
- specs/phase1/feature_list.json (API-008 passes -> true)

### Testing
- Verified all 5 API-008 acceptance steps:
  1. Create an alert with status 'open': `seedOpenAlert()` in beforeAll creates the FK chain + an Alert with status='open'. beforeEach resets between tests.
  2. POST /api/alerts/:id/action with { action: 'dismiss', reason: 'false_positive' }: each happy-path test calls postAction with the right body shape.

If a "no-status-change-once-resolved" rule lands, gate after the findUnique lookup with a 409 + audit-skip path.

### Next Priorities
- API-009 (priority 45): escalate path. Same route, switch over `accept`/`dismiss`/`escalate`. Body has optional `note` -- if present, store it in `Alert.escalationNote`. Status -> 'escalated'. AuditEntry with action='escalated', note=note (or null). The note is OPTIONAL here (unlike dismiss's required reason), so the validation gate is just "if `note` provided, it must be a non-empty string"; an absent `note` is allowed.
- API-010 (priority 46): snooze path. Required `snoozeUntil` ISO date string. Validation: parse via `new Date()`, reject if NaN or in the past (vs. `now`). Status -> 'snoozed'. Stores into `Alert.snoozeUntil`. The validation here is the most involved of the four action handlers -- date parsing + future-only check.
- API-011 (priority 47): POST /api/ingestion/trigger -- HTTP entry point for the ingestion orchestrator. Still pending from sessions 36-43. Body: `{ url?: string }`. Response: `{ runId, status: "started" }`.
- After all four action handlers + API-011 land, the alert-detail UI session (DETAIL-001..006) and the alerts-list UI session (LIST-001..008) become the natural read+write pair to verify in the browser.
