## Session 45 -- Alert Escalate Action
Date: 2026-05-05

### Feature Worked On
- API-009 (priority 45): POST /api/alerts/:id/action escalate path. Extends the action route with an `escalate` branch that accepts an OPTIONAL `note` (rejects empty/whitespace-only when provided), transitions alert.status `open` -> `escalated`, sets alert.escalationNote (or leaves it null when no note was sent), and writes an AuditEntry with action='escalated', note=note (or null) and beforeState/afterState JSON capturing the prior status + new status (with escalationNote in afterState). Snooze still rejects with 400 until API-010 lands.
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Replaced src/app/api/alerts/[id]/action/route.ts (105-line accept+dismiss implementation) with a 130-line implementation that handles `accept`, `dismiss`, AND `escalate`. The action allowlist becomes `action !== ACCEPT && action !== DISMISS && action !== ESCALATE`. For `escalate`, the route extracts `payload.note`; if undefined/null it leaves escalationNote=null (and the audit row's note field is null), and if defined it must be a non-empty trimmed string (400 with "'note' must be a non-empty string when provided" otherwise). The Prisma transaction shape stays the same -- atomic `alert.update` + `auditEntry.create` -- but the update payload conditionally includes `escalationNote: escalationNote` for the escalate branch, the audit entry's `action` is `nextStatus` ('accepted' | 'dismissed' | 'escalated'), and `auditNote` is the value to write into AuditEntry.note (=reason for dismiss, =escalationNote for escalate, =null for accept).
- The afterState JSON for escalate is `{status: "escalated", escalationNote: escalationNote}` rather than just `{status: "escalated"}`. This matches the route's actual write -- both columns change in the same transaction, so the audit row should reflect both. Same pattern as Session 44's dismiss branch (where afterState carries `dismissReason`).
- Why optional `note` is rejected when whitespace-only: an absent `note` field (undefined) is the "no note provided" signal; a present-but-empty `note` is a client bug (the form sent the field but with no content). Treating "" the same as undefined would silently swallow the bug. Spec says note is optional, not that empty strings are equivalent to absent.
- Why the gate uses `payload.note !== undefined && payload.note !== null`: TS strict null/undefined check. JSON `null` would be a deliberate "explicitly no note" signal (vs `undefined` from a missing field), so we treat both as "no note". The trim+length-zero check then rejects only the case where the client SENT a string but with no actual content.
- Authored __tests__/integration/alerts-action-escalate.test.ts (7 tests, ~250 lines). Same harness shape as alerts-action-dismiss.test.ts: `seedOpenAlert()` in beforeAll creates the FK chain + an Alert (status='open'); `resetAlertToOpen()` in beforeEach resets `status: "open", escalationNote: null` and deletes any audit entries the previous test wrote; afterAll tears down the FK chain in reverse. The reset includes `escalationNote: null` so the no-note happy path can assert null afterwards even after a prior test set the column.
- Test cases: (1) "transitions an open alert to escalated and stores escalationNote" -- response status=200, body.status='escalated', body.escalationNote='Needs legal review', re-reads from Prisma to confirm; (2) "creates an AuditEntry with action='escalated' and the note" -- exactly one entry, actor='reviewer', action='escalated', note='Needs legal review'; (3) "audit entry beforeState contains 'open' and afterState contains 'escalated'" -- substring assertions + JSON.parse round-trip confirming `before.status==='open'`, `after.status==='escalated'`, `after.escalationNote==='Needs legal review'`; (4) "response payload includes the new audit entry in auditEntries[]" -- response body has the audit entry inline with action/actor/note populated; (5) "escalates without a note -- escalationNote stays null and audit note is null" -- the optional-note happy path: POST without `note`, asserts body.escalationNote is null AND DB row's escalationNote is null AND the audit entry was still written with action='escalated' but note=null; (6) "returns 400 when 'note' is provided but empty/whitespace" -- defensive variant: passes "   ", asserts 400 + alert row stays 'open' AND escalationNote stays null (no-mutation guarantee on rejected requests); (7) "returns 404 when the alert does not exist" -- with a valid {action, note} body, unknown id still 404s.
- Decision: did NOT add a max-length cap on `escalationNote`. Same rationale as the dismissReason column -- demo-scale data, no normalization beyond trim.
- Decision: did NOT update Sessions 43/44's tests. Their negative-path tests that POST `{action: "escalate"}` (Session 43's "unsupported action" test 7) and Session 44's no-reason behavior are unaffected: Session 43's test 7 actually posts `{action: "dismiss"}` with no reason and asserts 400, which still holds; nothing in either suite posts `{action: "escalate"}`. All 14 prior tests still pass.
- Decision: did NOT add a unit test. Same rationale as API-007/008: route is parse + dispatch + Prisma transaction, integration test exercises every code path, no extractable pure logic.
- Decision: did NOT add Playwright verification. API-009 is a pure backend endpoint; the alert-detail UI session is the natural place for browser verification.

## Session 46 -- Alert Snooze Action
Date: 2026-05-05

### Feature Worked On
- API-010 (priority 46): POST /api/alerts/:id/action snooze path. Extends the action route with a `snooze` branch that requires `snoozeUntil` (a parseable ISO date string AND in the future), transitions alert.status `open` -> `snoozed`, sets alert.snoozeUntil to the parsed Date, and writes an AuditEntry with action='snoozed', note=null, and beforeState/afterState JSON capturing the prior status + new status (with snoozeUntil ISO string in afterState). Completes the four action handlers (accept/dismiss/escalate/snooze) for the alerts/[id]/action route.
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Replaced src/app/api/alerts/[id]/action/route.ts (130-line accept+dismiss+escalate implementation) with a 162-line implementation that handles `accept`, `dismiss`, `escalate`, AND `snooze`. Added SNOOZE constant; extended action allowlist; for `snooze`, the route extracts `payload.snoozeUntil`, requires a non-empty trimmed string (400 with "Missing 'snoozeUntil' for snooze action" otherwise), parses via `new Date(rawSnoozeUntil)`, rejects with 400 + "...must be a valid ISO date string" if `Number.isNaN(parsed.getTime())`, and rejects with 400 + "...must be in the future" if `parsed.getTime() <= Date.now()`. The Prisma transaction shape stays the same -- atomic `alert.update` + `auditEntry.create` -- but the update payload conditionally includes `snoozeUntil: <Date>` for the snooze branch, the audit entry's `action` is `nextStatus` ('accepted' | 'dismissed' | 'escalated' | 'snoozed'), and `auditNote` stays null for snooze (no per-action note field; the snoozeUntil is the only payload).
- The afterState JSON for snooze is `{status: "snoozed", snoozeUntil: <ISO>}` -- snoozeUntil is serialized via `parsed.toISOString()` (Prisma stores it as DateTime, but the audit row is JSON, so we want the ISO string for consistency with how dismiss/escalate carry their per-action column). Same pattern as Sessions 44/45 (afterState carries the column that changed alongside `status`).
- Why both NaN and "<= Date.now()" gates exist as separate 400s with different error messages: NaN means the client sent a non-date string ("not-a-date", "abc", etc.) -- a parse failure. Past-date means the client sent a parseable date but in the past -- a semantic failure. Splitting them makes the error message specific to the actual failure mode (the UI can then surface "please pick a future date" vs "please pick a valid date"). The `<=` (rather than `<`) covers the edge case where a request with snoozeUntil=now would otherwise create an instantly-expired snooze.
- Why the spec's example date `'2026-06-01'` works: at session time today is 2026-05-05, so 2026-06-01 is ~27 days in the future. The test uses a 24-hour-from-now ISO instead so it doesn't depend on the wall clock matching the demo timeline -- if this codebase outlives the spec's demo dates, the verification step's literal value would start failing the future-only gate, but the test always passes. (The spec's example is illustrative, not a fixed contract.)
- Why the date is rounded to seconds in the test: SQLite via Prisma's libsql adapter stores DateTime values with millisecond precision in some configurations and second precision in others. To make the round-trip assertion (`row.snoozeUntil.toISOString() === FUTURE_ISO`) robust against either, the test rounds the future timestamp to the nearest second before stringifying, so both client and DB representations agree exactly.
- Authored __tests__/integration/alerts-action-snooze.test.ts (8 tests, ~270 lines). Same harness shape as alerts-action-escalate.test.ts: `seedOpenAlert()` in beforeAll creates the FK chain + an Alert (status='open'); `resetAlertToOpen()` in beforeEach resets `status: "open", snoozeUntil: null` and deletes any audit entries the previous test wrote; afterAll tears down the FK chain in reverse.
- Test cases: (1) "transitions an open alert to snoozed and stores snoozeUntil" -- response status=200, body.status='snoozed', body.snoozeUntil parses back to FUTURE_ISO, re-reads from Prisma to confirm `row.status === 'snoozed'` AND `row.snoozeUntil.toISOString() === FUTURE_ISO`; (2) "creates an AuditEntry with action='snoozed'" -- exactly one entry, actor='reviewer', action='snoozed'; (3) "audit entry beforeState contains 'open' and afterState contains 'snoozed'" -- the verification-step-required substring assertion + JSON.parse round-trip confirming `before.status==='open'`, `after.status==='snoozed'`, `after.snoozeUntil===FUTURE_ISO`; (4) "response payload includes the new audit entry in auditEntries[]" -- inline audit entry with action='snoozed' / actor='reviewer'; (5) "returns 400 when 'snoozeUntil' is missing from the body" -- the verification-step-required negative path: status=400, error message contains "snoozeuntil", alert row stays 'open' AND snoozeUntil stays null; (6) "returns 400 when 'snoozeUntil' is not a valid ISO date string" -- "not-a-date" produces 400 + same no-mutation guarantee; (7) "returns 400 when 'snoozeUntil' is in the past" -- 24h-ago ISO produces 400, error message contains "future", same no-mutation guarantee; (8) "returns 404 when the alert does not exist" -- with a valid {action, snoozeUntil} body, unknown id still 404s.
- Decision: did NOT add a max-snooze-window cap (e.g., reject snoozeUntil more than 90 days out). The spec only requires "in the future"; an admin-imposed maximum is a product decision and would land with the snooze-modal UI session.
- Decision: did NOT update Sessions 43/44/45's tests. Their negative-path tests posting `{action: "snooze"}` (Session 43's "unsupported action" test 7 actually posts `{action: "dismiss"}` with no reason and asserts 400, which still holds; nothing in those suites posts `{action: "snooze"}`). All 21 prior alerts-action tests still pass.
- Decision: did NOT add a unit test. Same rationale as API-007/008/009: route is parse + dispatch + Prisma transaction, integration test exercises every code path, no extractable pure logic.
- Decision: did NOT add Playwright verification. API-010 is a pure backend endpoint; the alert-detail UI session is the natural place for browser verification.
- Decision: did NOT consolidate the per-action conditionals (updateData / afterState / auditNote) into a single dispatch table. The branches are short and the readability cost of an extra abstraction (a Map<action, builder> or a switch over five returns) outweighs the small DRY win at four cases. If a fifth or sixth action lands, that's the time to refactor.

### Files Modified / Created
- src/app/api/alerts/[id]/action/route.ts (extended from 130 to 162 lines; adds SNOOZE branch, snoozeUntil validation -- required + ISO-parseable + future-only -- conditional update payload, afterState includes snoozeUntil ISO)
- __tests__/integration/alerts-action-snooze.test.ts (new, 8 tests, ~270 lines)

### Testing
- Verified all 5 API-010 acceptance steps:

API-001..009, INFRA-001..004, LAYOUT-001..002, CORPUS-001..010, SEED-001, EMBED-001..002, VECTORS-001, RETRIEVE-001, LLM-001..002, CLASSIFY-001..002, CITE-001, SCORE-001, PIPE-001..002, INGEST-001..007 all unchanged.

### Blockers / Issues
- Dev-server cache staleness as noted in Sessions 44/45. Not blocking implementation; route handler is fully tested via Jest.
- The 500 error path (try/catch on Prisma failure) remains untested. Same rationale as API-002..009.
- The route currently allows `snooze` from any status (e.g., re-snoozing an already-snoozed alert with a different date). The verification step only mandates the open->snoozed transition; recording the actual prior status keeps the audit trail honest if a future client sends idempotent retries. Same audit-honest rationale Sessions 43/44/45 documented for accept/dismiss/escalate.
- snoozeUntil is parsed via `new Date(string)`, which is permissive: it accepts non-strict ISO formats (`"2026-06-01"`, `"2026/06/01"`, `"June 1 2026"`). The spec's example uses the ISO date form, but a stricter regex (e.g., a full ISO-8601 datetime check) would be a hardening pass. For the demo, the future-only gate provides a usable signal.
- The audit row's afterState carries snoozeUntil as an ISO string, but the alert.snoozeUntil column is a DateTime. If the audit row is ever joined with the alert row for a "what changed" view, the consumer will need to round-trip the ISO through `new Date(...)` to match. The pattern matches Sessions 44 (dismissReason as string) and 45 (escalationNote as string) -- the only complication is that snoozeUntil's source is a Date.

## Session 47 -- Ingestion Trigger Endpoint
Date: 2026-05-05

### Feature Worked On
- API-011 (priority 47): POST /api/ingestion/trigger. Synchronous response with `{runId, status: "started"}` plus a fire-and-forget call to runIngestion(). The route creates the IngestionRun row up-front (so the runId is queryable before the response returns) and the orchestrator drives that pre-created row through completion/failure rather than creating its own.
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Replaced the 8-line stub at src/app/api/ingestion/trigger/route.ts with a 45-line implementation. The handler reads the body via `request.text()` (any body-read failure -> 400), parses any non-empty body as JSON (parse failure -> 400 + "Invalid JSON body"), creates `IngestionRun{ trigger: "manual", status: "running" }`, fires `runIngestion({ trigger: "manual", runId: run.id })` without awaiting, and returns `{ runId: run.id, status: "started" }`. The fire-and-forget catch logs to console.error -- a runIngestion top-level throw is non-fatal to the HTTP response (which has already been sent) but should still surface in logs.
- Why the route creates the IngestionRun row instead of letting runIngestion() create it: the spec verification step 3 ("an IngestionRun record was created with trigger='manual' and status='running'") plus step 2 ("response contains { runId: <string>, status: 'started' }") means the runId returned in the response MUST refer to the row that exists in the DB at response-time. If runIngestion creates the row, the route can only get the id back by awaiting the orchestrator, defeating the async contract. Pre-creating the row in the route gives us both: synchronous runId AND a fire-and-forget orchestrator.
- Added `runId?: string` to RunIngestionOptions in src/lib/ingestion/pipeline.ts. When provided, runIngestion calls `findUniqueOrThrow` to load the existing row instead of `prisma.ingestionRun.create`. The rest of the orchestrator (parser fan-out, dedupe, persist, drift detection, terminal-state update) is unchanged -- it operates on the loaded `run` variable just as it did the created one. The findUniqueOrThrow shape mirrors the create path's "this row must exist" assumption: if the caller passed a non-existent id, we want to throw rather than silently create a duplicate row.
- Why findUniqueOrThrow vs findUnique + null check: a missing row is a programmer error (caller passed a bad id), not a recoverable runtime state. Throwing surfaces the bug; the route's `.catch()` logs it. Keeps the happy path linear.
- Why use `void runIngestion(...).catch(...)`: the `void` operator silences the no-floating-promise lint without await; the chained `.catch()` ensures any orchestrator throw is captured and logged. Without the catch, Node would emit an unhandledRejection warning. Without the void, TS would still type-check but the implicit promise-discard reads as a bug to a reader.
- Authored __tests__/integration/ingestion-trigger.test.ts (6 tests, ~270 lines). Uses `jest.unstable_mockModule("@/lib/ingestion/pipeline", ...)` to mock runIngestion -- the route is exercised in isolation while the real orchestrator stays covered by pipeline.test.ts and pipeline-isolation.test.ts.
- Test cases: (1) "returns runId + status='started' and creates an IngestionRun with trigger='manual', status='running'" -- the verification-step-required happy path, asserts response shape (200 / runId is non-empty string / status='started'), asserts DB row exists with trigger='manual' AND status='running' AND completedAt=null *while the mock is gated mid-run* (proving the response returns synchronously, not after the orchestrator finishes), asserts mockRunIngestion was called with the runId from the response and trigger='manual', then releases the gate and polls until terminal status; (2) "kicks off ingestion that eventually reaches a terminal 'completed' state (not stuck)" -- the verification-step-4 contract: fast-completing mock, poll until status='completed', assert the row is final; (3) "transitions to 'failed' when the orchestrator throws" -- the route's fire-and-forget catch must swallow rejections so the HTTP response stays 200 / 'started'; the test asserts that AND that the row reaches 'failed' (the mock writes the failed state before throwing); (4) "accepts an empty body (no JSON) and treats it as the no-URL case" -- POST with no body, route's `raw.length > 0` gate skips the JSON.parse; (5) "accepts a JSON body without a url field" -- POST `{}`, also fine; (6) "returns 400 on invalid JSON body and does not create an IngestionRun" -- defensive variant: malformed JSON -> 400 + body.error contains 'json' AND IngestionRun count unchanged AND mockRunIngestion never called.
- Why the gated-promise pattern in test (1): the spec verification asserts the row is in 'running' state. If the mock immediately updates the row to 'completed', the row would already be terminal by the time the test queries it. The gate (a Promise that the test resolves explicitly) lets the test read the row mid-run.
- Why test (3) uses a mock that writes 'failed' BEFORE throwing: the real runIngestion catches its own errors and updates the row to 'failed' inside its top-level try/catch. The mock simulates that contract. If we just threw without writing, the route's catch would log the rejection but the row would stay 'running' forever -- which is not the contract we want to test.
- Decision: did NOT validate or propagate `body.url`. Spec for API-011 only requires the no-URL happy path. URL handling is API-012's territory and lands with that feature.
- Decision: did NOT add a unit test. The route is parse + DB row create + fire-and-forget; integration test exercises every code path; no extractable pure logic.
- Decision: did NOT add Playwright verification. API-011 is a pure backend endpoint; the dashboard's "Trigger Ingestion" button (UI session yet to land) is the natural place for browser verification.
- Decision: did NOT add a "request already in flight" gate (e.g., 409 if a `running` IngestionRun already exists). The spec doesn't require single-flight semantics, and the demo's serial trigger button + scheduler stub means concurrent calls are unusual. If a future revision wants idempotency, a `findFirst({where:{status:'running'}})` check before the create would do it.
- Decision: when `runId` is passed to runIngestion, we use findUniqueOrThrow rather than just trusting the caller; the cost is one extra round trip vs. catching the FK/constraint violation later if the row was deleted between create and fetch (unlikely in normal flow but defensive).

### Files Modified / Created
- src/app/api/ingestion/trigger/route.ts (rewritten from 8-line stub to 45-line handler)
- src/lib/ingestion/pipeline.ts (added optional `runId` to RunIngestionOptions; the create branch becomes a `?:` between findUniqueOrThrow and create -- 5 lines changed)
- __tests__/integration/ingestion-trigger.test.ts (new, 6 tests, ~270 lines)
- specs/phase1/feature_list.json (API-011 passes -> true)

### Testing
- Verified all 4 API-011 acceptance steps:
  1. POST to /api/ingestion/trigger: postTrigger() helper covers JSON-body, empty-body, and malformed-body shapes.
  2. Response contains { runId: <string>, status: 'started' }: every happy-path test asserts `body.runId` is a non-empty string AND `body.status === "started"` AND HTTP 200.
  3. IngestionRun record was created with trigger='manual' and status='running': test (1) gates the orchestrator mock so the row is observable mid-run, then asserts trigger='manual' AND status='running' AND completedAt=null AND that mockRunIngestion received the runId from the response.
  4. Run eventually completes or fails (not stuck): tests (2) and (3) poll waitForTerminalStatus(runId) -- (2) asserts 'completed', (3) asserts 'failed'. Polling deadline is 2s (the in-process tests resolve in <100ms typically).
- Test suite results: `npm test` -> 39 suites / 290 tests passing (was 38 / 284; +1 suite / +6 tests for API-011). Stable at ~42s.
- Regression: `npx tsc --noEmit` -> zero errors. Pre-flight regression on `--testPathPatterns='ingestion|alerts-action'` ran cleanly before any new code -- 4 suites / 29 tests passing. Post-implementation: 5 suites / 35 tests passing (this session adds the new ingestion-trigger suite alongside the existing pipeline / pipeline-isolation / alerts-action-* suites). API-001..010, INFRA-001..004, LAYOUT-001..002, CORPUS-001..010, SEED-001, EMBED-001..002, VECTORS-001, RETRIEVE-001, LLM-001..002, CLASSIFY-001..002, CITE-001, SCORE-001, PIPE-001..002, INGEST-001..007 all unchanged.

Confirmed end-to-end that the new handler is what Next.js serves and the response shape matches the contract.
- No Playwright verification: API-011 is a pure backend endpoint with no UI surface. Browser verification will land with the dashboard's "Trigger Ingestion" button (UI session).

### Blockers / Issues
- Live curl initially returned the old stub `{"runId":"","status":"not_implemented"}` -- the dev server's Turbopack route cache from sessions 44-46 was stale and did not pick up the new route handler via HMR even after `rm -rf .next/dev/types`. Resolved by `./scripts/dev-up.sh` which kills the old PID and restarts. Future sessions touching API routes that the dev server has previously served as a stub: the Turbopack stub-cache survives HMR; restart the dev server explicitly. The integration tests are unaffected by the dev cache (they import the POST handler module directly).
- The fire-and-forget pattern means that on a server crash mid-run, the IngestionRun row will be permanently stuck at status='running' (no resume / no cleanup). Acceptable for the demo (the run row is informational); a production version would need a "stuck-run reaper" (e.g., `WHERE status='running' AND startedAt < now() - interval '10 minutes' -> mark as failed`). Not required by the spec.
- The 500 error path (try/catch on the route's prisma.ingestionRun.create) is untested. If the DB is unreachable when the route is hit, the create throws and the route returns the default Next.js 500. Same rationale as API-002..010 -- mocking @/lib/db is brittle and the create is a single Prisma call.
- The `runId` injection makes runIngestion's `trigger` parameter unused when runId is provided (the trigger column is already set on the existing row). Currently silent; a future refactor could split runIngestion into createIngestionRun() + executeIngestionRun(runId) for clearer ownership, but that's a larger change than API-011 warrants.
- The route accepts `body.url` in the JSON payload but currently ignores it (no validation, no propagation). API-012 (priority 48) is the dedicated single-URL ingestion path. Until that lands, a client passing url will not see the URL respected.

Implementation: validate url is a string + a valid URL via `new URL()`, plumb it through to a single-URL parser path (probably a new `parsers` shape that bypasses regulator-wide fetch and processes one URL), persist as a RegulatoryItem with sourceUrl=that URL. The runId / fire-and-forget contract is reused from API-011.
- API-013 (priority 49): GET /api/ingestion/log -- paginated list of IngestionRun rows with metrics. Read-only; sort by startedAt desc; query params `page` + `pageSize` (default 1 / 20). Response shape: `{ runs, total, page, totalPages }`.

## Session 48 -- Single-URL Ingestion
Date: 2026-05-06

### Feature Worked On
- API-012 (priority 48): POST /api/ingestion/trigger with `{ url: <URL> }` ingests only that URL. The route validates the url (string + parseable via `new URL()`) and plumbs it to runIngestion via a new `url?: string` option. The orchestrator's existing parser fan-out is replaced by a single fetch on the single-URL path; the dedupe + persist + drift-detection downstream stages are reused unchanged. The runId / fire-and-forget contract from API-011 is preserved.
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Added src/lib/ingestion/single-url.ts (~95 lines): exports `fetchSingleRegulatoryItem(url)` which calls fetcher.fetchUrl, parses the HTML for `<title>` (falling back to `<h1>`) and a stripped-tag fullText body, derives the regulator from the URL hostname (sec.gov->SEC, finra.org->FINRA, consumerfinance.gov->CFPB, occ.(gov|treas.gov)->OCC, unknown->SEC + warning), and returns a `RawRegulatoryItem` with documentType="publication" and publicationDate=now. Returns null on fetch failure (matching the parser fan-out's graceful-failure contract).
- Why detectRegulator defaults to SEC for unknown hostnames: the spec verification only mentions SEC URLs as the test target, and the regulator field is required on RegulatoryItem -- a permissive default is more useful than a 400 when an unfamiliar host is provided. The warning logs the unknown hostname so a future hardening pass can decide whether to tighten this.
- Why the HTML extraction is regex-based: same approach as the SEC RSS parser (sec.ts) -- the project has no jsdom/cheerio dep and the parsers are tag-extractors, not full DOM walkers. Drops `<script>`/`<style>`/`<noscript>` blocks first so their bodies don't pollute the extracted fullText. Decodes the common HTML entities (&amp;/&lt;/&gt;/&quot;/&#39;/&apos;/&nbsp;).
- Extended src/lib/ingestion/pipeline.ts: added `url?: string` and `singleUrlFetcher?: (url) => Promise<RawRegulatoryItem | null>` to RunIngestionOptions. The latter mirrors the existing `parsers` test seam so integration tests can inject a mock fetcher without touching the network. When `options.url` is set, the orchestrator skips the parser fan-out (and the parserFetchFailures gate is no-op'd: `allParsersFailed = !options.url && parserFetchFailures === parsers.length`); a fetcher returning null OR throwing finalizes the run as 'failed' (single-URL has only one source, so failing it produces an empty run).
- Why the parser-fan-out branch and the single-url branch share the rest of the pipeline (dedupe + persist + drift detection): the spec contract for a single-URL run is identical to the contract for a regular run -- "produce RegulatoryItem rows with sourceUrl set, run drift detection, finalize the IngestionRun." The only difference is the *source* of the RawRegulatoryItem(s). Sharing the downstream code keeps duplicate-detection consistent (same URL ingested via fan-out OR single-url path is detected as a duplicate in either direction) and means drift detection / itemsFlagged / itemsSuppressed all work the same way.
- Updated src/app/api/ingestion/trigger/route.ts: when JSON body contains `url`, validate it's a non-empty string (400 with "'url' must be a string" otherwise), validate it parses via `new URL()` (400 with "'url' must be a valid URL" otherwise), and forward to runIngestion. Empty-string url is treated as "no url" so a request body of `{"url": ""}` keeps the full-crawl behavior. The route still creates the IngestionRun row up-front (per API-011's design) and fires runIngestion as a fire-and-forget.
- Why the route propagates `url` as a separate option rather than encoding it on the IngestionRun row itself: the IngestionRun schema doesn't carry per-run filter state, and adding it would couple IngestionRun to the trigger's body shape. Passing through RunIngestionOptions keeps the schema unchanged.
- Authored __tests__/integration/ingestion-trigger-url.test.ts (4 tests): mocks runIngestion (same pattern as ingestion-trigger.test.ts), verifies (1) a valid URL is forwarded with runId+trigger+url, (2) non-string url returns 400 + no row created + orchestrator not called, (3) non-URL string returns 400 + no row + no orchestrator, (4) empty-string url is treated as the no-URL path (call?.url is undefined, runIngestion still invoked).
- Authored __tests__/integration/pipeline-single-url.test.ts (3 tests): mocks runDriftDetection (same pattern as pipeline.test.ts), exercises the real runIngestion against the real DB. Tests (1) happy path -- exactly one RegulatoryItem persisted with sourceUrl=URL, fetcher called once with that URL, drift detector called once with the persisted item id, status='completed', itemsProcessed=1; (2) fetcher returns null -> status='failed', no item, no drift detection; (3) duplicate URL (pre-seeded as a prior-run RegulatoryItem) -> the dedupe gate skips persistence, status='completed', duplicatesSkipped=1, itemsProcessed=0, no drift detection. Splitting these from ingestion-trigger-url.test.ts (which mocks pipeline) avoids the cross-mock interaction footgun where the same module is both mocked-by-alias AND imported for real.
- Authored __tests__/unit/single-url.test.ts (12 tests): pure-logic coverage for detectRegulator (SEC/FINRA/CFPB/OCC hostname mapping including the occ.treas.gov variant, SEC-default for unknown hostnames, SEC-default for unparseable URLs) and extractTitleAndText (`<title>` extraction, `<h1>` fallback, `<script>`/`<style>` stripping, HTML entity decoding).
- Decision: did NOT add a regulator-restricted whitelist for the route's URL validation. The verification step only mandates "a real SEC publication URL" -- restricting to a hardcoded list of allowed hosts would block legitimate use cases (sec.gov vs. www.sec.gov vs. www.sec.gov:443) and force the route into a hostname-parsing role that detectRegulator already owns. The fallback-to-SEC behavior is enough for the demo.
- Decision: did NOT extract publicationDate from the fetched HTML. SEC press-release pages have a date in `<meta>` or near `<h1>`, but each regulator's page has a different shape. For the demo, publicationDate=now is an acceptable approximation -- the regulatory item is being ingested NOW, and the field's primary use is sort order on the alerts list. A future enhancement could parse a `<meta property="article:published_time">` or similar.
- Decision: did NOT classify documentType from the URL or page content. publicationDate=now + documentType="publication" is a deliberately neutral default; the existing `normalizeDocumentType` in pipeline.ts will then run keyword-matching over title+fullText to assign the canonical DocumentType ("final_rule" / "enforcement" / etc.). So a URL whose body says "SEC Charges Adviser" still ends up classified as "enforcement" by the normalizer.
- Decision: did NOT add a Playwright test. API-012 is a pure backend endpoint; the dashboard's URL-input form (yet to land) is the natural place for browser verification.

### Files Modified / Created
- src/lib/ingestion/single-url.ts (new, ~95 lines)
- src/lib/ingestion/pipeline.ts (added url + singleUrlFetcher options; new conditional branch around the parser fan-out; updated allParsersFailed gate to also account for singleUrlFetchFailed; ~30 lines changed)
- src/app/api/ingestion/trigger/route.ts (added URL validation + propagation; +27 lines)
- __tests__/integration/ingestion-trigger-url.test.ts (new, 4 tests, ~150 lines)

- __tests__/unit/single-url.test.ts (new, 12 tests, ~95 lines)

  - `curl -d '{"url":"not a url"}' /api/ingestion/trigger` -> 400 + `{"error":"'url' must be a valid URL"}`
  - `curl -d '{"url":123}' /api/ingestion/trigger` -> 400 + `{"error":"'url' must be a string"}`
  - `curl -d '{"url":"https://www.sec.gov/news/press-release/2025-9999-test"}' /api/ingestion/trigger` -> 200 + runId; dev log: fetcher 404 + null + run finalized as 'failed' (the spec's "real SEC publication URL" -- a fabricated path correctly gets handled by the failure path).
  - `curl -d '{"url":"https://www.sec.gov/newsroom/press-releases"}' /api/ingestion/trigger` -> 200 + runId; dev log: RegulatoryItem persisted, drift detection ran (LLM call failed at the auth layer because ANTHROPIC_API_KEY isn't set in this environment, but that's the standard non-fatal drift-detection failure path -- not a regression).

### Blockers / Issues
- Dev-server cache staleness as noted in Sessions 44-47: Turbopack does not pick up route-handler changes via HMR cleanly. `./scripts/dev-up.sh` resolved it (same workaround Session 47 documented).
- LLM call from drift-detection on a real SEC URL fails with 401 because no ANTHROPIC_API_KEY is configured in this environment. This is *not* a regression -- the existing drift-detection failure path catches and logs without aborting the run, so the IngestionRun still finalizes correctly. The single-URL ingestion contract (RegulatoryItem persisted with correct sourceUrl) is fully verified upstream of drift detection.
- The 500 error path (try/catch on the route's prisma.ingestionRun.create) remains untested. Same rationale as API-002..011.
- detectRegulator's fallback-to-SEC for unknown hostnames is permissive by design but could mis-classify a URL hosted on, e.g., a regulator's CDN domain (the patterns match `*.sec.gov` etc., but Cloudflare-fronted feeds may serve from a different host). For the demo this is fine; a hardening pass would either tighten the patterns or surface the fallback as a 400.
- The URL fetched by fetchSingleRegulatoryItem may be a list/index page (e.g., the SEC newsroom press-releases index), not a single article. The current implementation will happily ingest the index page as one RegulatoryItem with the index page's title and the index page's stripped text -- which is not what a downstream classifier wants. The spec doesn't require URL shape validation; if a follow-up wants to reject index pages, an opt-in heuristic (e.g., require `<article>` or `og:type=article`) would be the place to add it.
- publicationDate is set to "now" rather than parsed from the page. For correctly-displayed sort order on the alerts list, a follow-up should parse `<meta property="article:published_time">` or a similar signal. The spec's verification only requires the sourceUrl round-trip, so this is a known forward-compatibility gap, not a regression.

## Session 49 -- Ingestion Log Endpoint
Date: 2026-05-06

### Feature Worked On
- API-013 (priority 49): GET /api/ingestion/log -- paginated list of IngestionRun rows with metrics. Read-only endpoint; sorts startedAt desc; supports `page` (default 1) and `pageSize` (default 20, capped at 100). Response shape: `{ runs, total, page, pageSize, totalPages }`. Each row exposes id, trigger, status, startedAt, completedAt, itemsProcessed, itemsFlagged, itemsSuppressed (and errors -- the JSON column carrying parserErrors/driftErrors, included so the UI can surface failure details without a second round trip).
- Status: PASSED

### What Was Done
- Replaced the 10-line stub at src/app/api/ingestion/log/route.ts with a 64-line implementation. Reuses the same `parsePositiveInt` helper shape from src/app/api/alerts/route.ts (parses ?page= and ?pageSize=, falls back to defaults on invalid input, caps pageSize at MAX_PAGE_SIZE=100). Runs `count()` and `findMany({ skip, take, orderBy: { startedAt: "desc" }, select: <metric fields> })` in a Promise.all so total + page rows are issued concurrently. totalPages computed as `total === 0 ? 0 : Math.ceil(total / pageSize)`.
- Why include `errors` in the select list: the spec verification step lists id/trigger/status/startedAt/completedAt/itemsProcessed/itemsFlagged/itemsSuppressed as required; `errors` is on the IngestionRun model and contains the parser+drift error JSON the ingestion-log UI page will want to render. Including it in the response avoids a second round trip from the UI for failed runs. The select list is explicit (not `select: undefined`) because the IngestionRun model has a `regulatoryItems` relation that we explicitly do NOT want serialized into the response.
- Why `select` instead of leaving the model relation defaults: a default `findMany` returns scalar columns only (no relations), so omitting `select` would also work. Switching to an explicit allowlist makes the response shape contract visible at the route handler and prevents accidental data leakage if a future migration adds a sensitive column to IngestionRun.
- Why `orderBy: { startedAt: "desc" }` (not createdAt): IngestionRun has no `createdAt` (the schema uses `startedAt @default(now())` as the row-creation timestamp -- they're equivalent for new rows but `startedAt` is the canonical field the spec verification mentions). The pipeline orchestrator also writes `completedAt` separately, so sorting by startedAt is the user-facing "when was this run kicked off" order.
- Default pageSize is 20 (matching app_spec.txt § 4 "page?: number (default: 1) / pageSize?: number (default: 20)"), distinct from the alerts list endpoint's 25 default. The MAX_PAGE_SIZE=100 cap matches the alerts route's pattern -- prevents a single request from grabbing the entire IngestionRun table.
- Authored __tests__/integration/ingestion-log.test.ts (6 tests, ~230 lines). beforeAll seeds 5 IngestionRun rows (`STATUS_A` through `STATUS_E`) with strictly-increasing startedAt timestamps and sentinel statuses ("ing-log-test-a-completed" etc.) so assertions can filter the response down to just this suite's seeds without touching pre-existing rows from API-011/012's live curl runs. afterAll deletes the seeded ids.
- Test cases: (1) "default response shape" -- GET / no query params, asserts 200 + array `runs` + numeric total/page/pageSize/totalPages, asserts every returned row has the spec-required fields with correct types, asserts totalPages = ceil(total/pageSize); (2) "ordered by startedAt desc" -- pulls pageSize=100, filters to seeded rows, asserts order is E->D->C->B->A (newest first), AND asserts the full unfiltered response is monotonically descending; (3) "metrics surface correctly" -- spot-checks itemsProcessed/itemsFlagged/itemsSuppressed/trigger/completedAt for three of the seeded rows, including the running-row case (completedAt: null) which round-trips as null on the response; (4) "pagination" -- pageSize=2 across two pages, asserts page1.runs.length === page2.runs.length === 2, totals equal, totalPages = ceil(total/2), no overlap between pages, descending order across both pages combined; (5) "invalid pagination falls back" -- ?page=abc&pageSize=-5 returns page=1 + pageSize=20; (6) "page beyond totalPages" -- empty `runs` but stable total + echoed page number.
- Decision: did NOT add filtering by trigger/status to the route. The spec only mandates pagination + ordering. The ingestion-log UI page (yet to land) may want filter chips, but they belong to that UI session.
- Decision: did NOT add a unit test. Route is parse + count + findMany; integration test exercises every code path; no extractable pure logic beyond `parsePositiveInt` (already covered transitively by the alerts list/sort/filter test suites).
- Decision: did NOT add Playwright verification. API-013 is a pure backend endpoint; the ingestion-log page (yet to land) is the natural place for browser verification.
- Decision: included `pageSize` in the response shape (the spec snippet only lists runs/total/page/totalPages) for parity with the alerts list endpoint and so paginating UI can echo back its current page-size selection without round-tripping the query string.

### Files Modified / Created
- src/app/api/ingestion/log/route.ts (rewritten from 10-line stub to 64-line handler with pagination + descending sort + explicit select)
- __tests__/integration/ingestion-log.test.ts (new, 6 tests, ~230 lines)
- specs/phase1/feature_list.json (API-013 passes -> true)

### Testing
- Verified all 5 API-013 acceptance steps:
  1. Create several ingestion runs with varied statuses and metrics: beforeAll creates 5 IngestionRun rows with three statuses and varied trigger/itemsProcessed/itemsFlagged/itemsSuppressed combinations; live DB also has 8 real runs from Sessions 47/48 + the dev environment.

  4. Pagination works: test (4) covers page=1/2 with pageSize=2; live curl `curl /api/ingestion/log?page=2&pageSize=2` -> page=2, pageSize=2, total=8, totalPages=4, len(runs)=2. Tests (5) and (6) cover the invalid-input and beyond-last-page edge cases.
  5. Runs ordered by startedAt descending: test (2) asserts both the seeded subset (E->D->C->B->A) AND the full unfiltered response (every adjacent pair is monotonically desc).
- Test suite results: `npm test` -> 43 suites / 315 tests passing (was 42 / 309; +1 suite / +6 tests for API-013). Stable at ~45s.
- Regression: `npx tsc --noEmit` -> zero errors. Pre-flight curl regression: /api/health -> 200, /api/alerts?pageSize=1 -> 200, /api/dashboard/stats -> 200, /api/ingestion/log -> 200 (stub-shape) -- all four still respond after restart. API-001..012, INFRA-001..004, LAYOUT-001..002, CORPUS-001..010, SEED-001, EMBED-001..002, VECTORS-001, RETRIEVE-001, LLM-001..002, CLASSIFY-001..002, CITE-001, SCORE-001, PIPE-001..002, INGEST-001..007 all unchanged.
- Live curl verification: `./scripts/dev-up.sh` to restart the dev server (the prior Turbopack route cache from Sessions 47/48 still served the old 10-line stub even after the file was rewritten on disk -- same workaround), then:
  - `curl /api/ingestion/log?pageSize=3` -> 200 + 3 real rows, each with id/trigger/status/startedAt/completedAt/itemsProcessed/itemsFlagged/itemsSuppressed/errors. Newest row first (the API-012 SEC press-releases run from Session 48), followed by the failed 2025-9999-test run, then the Session 46 sample run.
  - `curl /api/ingestion/log?page=2&pageSize=2` -> page=2, pageSize=2, total=8, totalPages=4, runs.length=2. Pagination math holds.
- No Playwright verification: API-013 is a pure backend endpoint with no UI surface. Browser verification will land with the ingestion-log page UI session (yet to be specified beyond the existing /ingestion route stub).

### Blockers / Issues
- Dev-server cache staleness as noted in Sessions 44-48: Turbopack does not pick up route-handler changes via HMR cleanly. `./scripts/dev-up.sh` resolved it.
- The 500 error path (try/catch on prisma.ingestionRun.count / .findMany failure) is untested. Same rationale as API-002..012: mocking @/lib/db is brittle and the count+findMany are single Prisma calls.
- The route's pageSize cap (MAX_PAGE_SIZE=100) is opinionated; the spec doesn't specify a max. If a future client wants the full IngestionRun history in one call (e.g., for an "export to CSV" feature), they'd need either a higher cap, an "all=true" flag, or a streaming endpoint. For the demo, 100 is plenty.
- The `errors` column is included in the response as a raw JSON string (the column type), not pre-parsed. Clients that want the parserErrors/driftErrors structure will need to JSON.parse it. Pre-parsing at the route would either always succeed (the orchestrator always writes valid JSON) or fail loud if future code wrote a non-JSON string. Leaving it as-is is the lower-risk choice for the demo.
- The descending-by-startedAt sort uses millisecond precision. If two runs happen within the same ms (extremely unlikely in single-process dev, but possible under future parallel triggers), order is undefined relative to each other. A stable secondary sort on `id` (cuid is roughly time-ordered) would be the natural hardening pass.
